BNSS SECTION 1 - SHORT TITLE, EXTENT AND COMMENCEMENT
Core Content:
This Act is called the Bharatiya Nagarik Suraksha Sanhita, 2023. It extends to the whole of India except Nagaland and tribal areas (unless the State Government applies it). It shall come into force on a date to be notified by the Central Government.

Procedure: Application

Provisions of Chapters IX, XI and XII (relating to maintenance of public order, nuisance, disputes over immovable property) do NOT apply to Nagaland and tribal areas

State Government may, by notification, apply these provisions to Nagaland or tribal areas with modifications

Central Government shall notify the date of commencement in the Official Gazette

"Tribal areas" means territories included in tribal areas of Assam under paragraph 20 of Sixth Schedule to the Constitution (excluding Shillong municipality)

Illustration:
The Central Government issues a notification on June 1, 2024 stating that BNSS shall come into force from July 1, 2024. From that date, all criminal proceedings in India (except Nagaland and tribal areas) shall be governed by BNSS. The Nagaland government may later issue a notification adopting certain provisions.

BNSS SECTION 2 - DEFINITIONS
Core Content:
This section defines key terms used throughout the Sanhita including "audio-video electronic", "bail", "bailable offence", "cognizable offence", "complaint", "investigation", "victim", and "warrant-case".

Procedure: Understanding Key Definitions

"audio-video electronic" - includes video conferencing, recording of identification/search/seizure/evidence, electronic communication

"bail" - release of accused from custody on conditions imposed by officer or Court, on execution of bond or bail bond

"bailable offence" - shown as bailable in First Schedule or made bailable by any other law

"non-bailable offence" - any other offence

"cognizable offence" - police officer may arrest without warrant (as per First Schedule or any other law)

"complaint" - allegation made orally or in writing to a Magistrate for taking action (does NOT include police report)

Explanation: Police report disclosing non-cognizable offence after investigation shall be deemed a complaint

"investigation" - all proceedings for collection of evidence by police officer or person authorised by Magistrate

"victim" - person who suffered loss or injury due to act/omission of accused, includes guardian or legal heir

"warrant-case" - case relating to offence punishable with death, imprisonment for life, or imprisonment exceeding two years

"summons-case" - case relating to an offence not being a warrant-case

Illustration:
X commits theft of a mobile phone worth ₹10,000. The First Schedule shows theft as punishable with imprisonment up to 5 years. Since punishment exceeds 2 years, this is a warrant-case. If Y commits simple hurt punishable with 1 year imprisonment, it is a summons-case. The victim Z (whose phone was stolen) can participate in proceedings.

BNSS SECTION 3 - CONSTRUCTION OF REFERENCES
Core Content:
Any reference in any law to a Magistrate without qualification means a Judicial Magistrate of the first class or second class. Functions involving appreciation of evidence or decisions affecting liberty shall be exercised by Judicial Magistrates. Administrative functions shall be exercised by Executive Magistrates.

Procedure: Determining Magistrate Type

If a law refers to "Magistrate" without qualification, construe as:

Judicial Magistrate of the first class, OR

Judicial Magistrate of the second class (as applicable in that area)

Functions involving appreciation of evidence, shifting of evidence, formulation of decisions exposing person to punishment or detention, or sending for trial → Judicial Magistrate

Functions administrative or executive in nature (granting licences, cancelling licences, sanctioning prosecution, withdrawing from prosecution) → Executive Magistrate

Illustration:
The Prevention of Cruelty to Animals Act requires a complaint to be filed before a "Magistrate". In an area where a Judicial Magistrate of first class exercises jurisdiction, that Magistrate shall hear the complaint. If the law requires a Magistrate to grant a licence for a meat shop, an Executive Magistrate shall handle that application.

BNSS SECTION 4 - TRIAL OF OFFENCES UNDER BHARATIYA NYAYA SANHITA, 2023 AND OTHER LAWS
Core Content:
All offences under the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita (BNS), 2023 shall be investigated, inquired into, tried, and dealt with according to the provisions of BNSS. Offences under any other law shall be dealt with according to BNSS, subject to any specific enactment regulating the manner or place of such proceedings.

Procedure: Applicability

BNS offences → follow BNSS procedure for investigation, inquiry, trial

Other law offences → follow BNSS procedure, BUT subject to any special enactment that regulates the manner or place of investigation/inquiry/trial

If the special enactment has conflicting provisions, the special law prevails (as per Explanation to section 2(l))

Illustration:
A person commits murder (BNS section 103). The investigation and trial shall follow BNSS procedure. Another person commits an offence under the Narcotic Drugs and Psychotropic Substances (NDPS) Act. The trial shall follow BNSS, but the NDPS Act's special provisions regarding bail or trial court will prevail in case of conflict.

BNSS SECTION 5 - SAVING
Core Content:
Nothing in BNSS shall affect any special or local law for the time being in force, or any special jurisdiction or power conferred, or any special form of procedure prescribed, by any other law, unless BNSS has a specific provision to the contrary.

Procedure: Interpretation

If a special law exists, it continues to operate

BNSS does not override special/local laws unless BNSS explicitly says so

Special jurisdiction or power conferred by any other law remains unaffected

Special procedure prescribed by any other law continues to apply

Illustration:
The Protection of Children from Sexual Offences (POCSO) Act, 2012 has special procedures for recording child testimony. BNSS does not contain a specific provision to the contrary. Therefore, the POCSO procedures continue to apply alongside BNSS.

BNSS SECTION 6 - CLASSES OF CRIMINAL COURTS
Core Content:
Besides High Courts, there shall be in every State the following classes of Criminal Courts: (i) Courts of Session, (ii) Judicial Magistrates of the first class, (iii) Judicial Magistrates of the second class, and (iv) Executive Magistrates.

Procedure: Court Hierarchy

High Court - highest criminal court in the State

Court of Session - established for every sessions division

Judicial Magistrates (First Class) - handle serious cases, can sentence up to 3 years imprisonment and fine up to ₹50,000

Judicial Magistrates (Second Class) - handle less serious cases, can sentence up to 1 year imprisonment and fine up to ₹10,000

Executive Magistrates - handle administrative functions (peace, security, nuisance)

Illustration:
A murder case shall be tried by the Court of Session. A theft case with punishment up to 3 years shall be tried by a Judicial Magistrate of first class. A public nuisance case shall be handled by an Executive Magistrate who may issue orders for removal of nuisance.

BNSS SECTION 8 - COURT OF SESSION
Core Content:
The State Government shall establish a Court of Session for every sessions division. Each Court of Session shall be presided over by a Judge appointed by the High Court. The High Court may also appoint Additional Sessions Judges.

Procedure: Establishment and Sitting

State Government establishes Court of Session for every sessions division

High Court appoints Sessions Judge and may appoint Additional Sessions Judges

Court of Session shall ordinarily hold its sitting at places specified by High Court notification

Court may, with consent of prosecution and accused, sit at any other place in the sessions division for disposal of case or examination of witnesses if it tends to general convenience

Sessions Judge may distribute business among Additional Sessions Judges

In absence of Sessions Judge, urgent applications may be disposed by Additional Sessions Judge, or if none, by Chief Judicial Magistrate

Illustration:
The State Government establishes a Court of Session for Pune sessions division. The High Court appoints Judge A as Sessions Judge and Judge B as Additional Sessions Judge. For a case where witnesses are from a remote village, the Court may, with consent of both parties, hold a sitting in that village for recording their evidence.

BNSS SECTION 14 - EXECUTIVE MAGISTRATES
Core Content:
In every district, the State Government may appoint Executive Magistrates and shall appoint one of them as the District Magistrate. The State Government may appoint an Additional District Magistrate. A Sub-divisional Magistrate may be placed in charge of a sub-division.

Procedure: Appointment and Powers

State Government appoints Executive Magistrates in every district

State Government appoints one Executive Magistrate as District Magistrate

State Government may appoint any Executive Magistrate as Additional District Magistrate with such powers as directed

When District Magistrate office becomes vacant, the officer temporarily succeeding to executive administration shall exercise all powers of District Magistrate pending State Government orders

State Government may place an Executive Magistrate in charge of a sub-division (called Sub-divisional Magistrate)

State Government may delegate this power to District Magistrate

State Government may confer on Commissioner of Police all or any powers of an Executive Magistrate

Illustration:
In District X, the State Government appoints five Executive Magistrates. One is appointed as District Magistrate, one as Additional District Magistrate, and one as Sub-divisional Magistrate for Sub-division Y. The Commissioner of Police in a metropolitan city is also given Executive Magistrate powers.

BNSS SECTION 18 - PUBLIC PROSECUTORS
Core Content:
For every High Court, the Central Government or State Government shall appoint a Public Prosecutor after consultation with the High Court. For every district, the State Government shall appoint a Public Prosecutor. A person must have practiced as an advocate for at least 7 years to be eligible.

Procedure: Appointment of Public Prosecutor

For High Court: Central/State Government appoints Public Prosecutor and Additional Public Prosecutors after consultation with High Court

For National Capital Territory of Delhi: Central Government appoints after consultation with Delhi High Court

For every district: State Government appoints Public Prosecutor and may appoint Additional Public Prosecutors

District Magistrate, in consultation with Sessions Judge, prepares a panel of fit persons

State Government shall appoint only from this panel

If regular cadre of Prosecuting Officers exists, appointment shall be from that cadre

Minimum qualification: 7 years practice as advocate

For Special Public Prosecutor (any case or class of cases): 10 years practice as advocate

Victim may engage an advocate of his choice to assist prosecution

Illustration:
The State Government needs to appoint a Public Prosecutor for District A. The District Magistrate consults the Sessions Judge and prepares a panel of 5 advocates. From this panel, the State Government appoints X, who has 10 years of practice as an advocate, as the Public Prosecutor. For a high-profile murder case, the State Government appoints Y (15 years practice) as Special Public Prosecutor.

BNSS SECTION 23 - SENTENCES WHICH MAGISTRATES MAY PASS
Core Content:
Chief Judicial Magistrate can sentence up to 7 years imprisonment (except death or life imprisonment). Magistrate of first class can sentence up to 3 years imprisonment or fine up to ₹50,000 or both or community service. Magistrate of second class can sentence up to 1 year imprisonment or fine up to ₹10,000 or both or community service.

Procedure: Sentencing Limits

Chief Judicial Magistrate: any sentence except death, imprisonment for life, or imprisonment exceeding 7 years

Magistrate of First Class: imprisonment not exceeding 3 years OR fine not exceeding ₹50,000 OR both OR community service

Magistrate of Second Class: imprisonment not exceeding 1 year OR fine not exceeding ₹10,000 OR both OR community service

"Community service" means work ordered by Court as punishment that benefits the community, without any remuneration

Illustration:
A case of theft (punishable up to 5 years) is tried by a Magistrate of first class. The Magistrate cannot sentence more than 3 years. If the accused is a first-time offender who stole a bicycle worth ₹3,000, the Magistrate may sentence him to community service (e.g., cleaning a public park for 2 months) instead of imprisonment.

BNSS SECTION 30 - POWERS OF SUPERIOR OFFICERS OF POLICE
Core Content:
Police officers superior in rank to an officer in charge of a police station may exercise the same powers throughout the local area to which they are appointed, as may be exercised by such officer within the limits of his station.

Procedure: Exercise of Superior Powers

A police officer superior to the Station House Officer (SHO) can exercise all powers of the SHO

This power extends throughout the local area of their appointment, not just one police station

This includes powers to investigate, arrest, and all other powers under BNSS

Illustration:
A Deputy Superintendent of Police (DSP) is superior to the SHO of City Police Station. The DSP can exercise all SHO powers anywhere in the district where he is appointed, not just within City Police Station limits. If a crime occurs in Rural Police Station area, the DSP can still investigate and exercise SHO powers there.

BNSS SECTION 31 - PUBLIC WHEN TO ASSIST MAGISTRATES AND POLICE
Core Content:
Every person is bound to assist a Magistrate or police officer reasonably demanding his aid in taking or preventing escape of a person authorised to be arrested, in prevention or suppression of breach of peace, or in prevention of injury to public property.

Procedure: Duty to Assist

Every person must assist when a Magistrate or police officer reasonably demands aid for:

(a) Taking or preventing escape of any person whom the Magistrate/police officer is authorised to arrest

(b) Prevention or suppression of a breach of the peace

(c) Prevention of any injury attempted to be committed to any public property

Failure to assist may attract legal consequences

Illustration:
A police officer is chasing a thief and shouts, "Stop that man!" A bystander, X, is legally bound to assist by blocking the thief's path. Another officer calls for help to disperse a rioting crowd. Citizens present are bound to assist the officer.

BNSS SECTION 33 - PUBLIC TO GIVE INFORMATION OF CERTAIN OFFENCES
Core Content:
Every person aware of the commission of, or intention to commit, specified serious offences under BNS (including murder, robbery, kidnapping, rape, etc.) shall forthwith give information to the nearest Magistrate or police officer.

Procedure: Mandatory Reporting

The following categories of offences must be reported:

(i) Sections 103-105 (murder and culpable homicide)

(ii) Sections 111-113 (organised crime, terrorist act)

(iii) Sections 140-144 (kidnapping, abduction, trafficking)

(iv) Sections 147-154, 158 (waging war, sedition)

(v) Sections 178-182 (counterfeiting)

(vi) Sections 189, 191 (unlawful assembly, rioting)

(vii) Sections 274-280 (adulteration of food/drugs)

(viii) Section 307 (theft with preparation for causing death)

(ix) Sections 309-312 (robbery, dacoity)

(x) Sub-section (5) of section 316 (criminal breach of trust)

(xi) Sections 326-328 (mischief by fire/explosives)

(xii) Sections 331-332 (house-trespass, house-breaking)

"Offence" includes any act outside India that would constitute an offence if committed in India

Illustration:
X sees Y murder Z. X is legally bound to immediately inform the nearest police officer or Magistrate. If X fails to do so, he may face legal consequences. Similarly, if X sees someone preparing to commit a robbery, X must report it immediately.

BNSS SECTION 34 - DUTY OF OFFICERS EMPLOYED IN CONNECTION WITH AFFAIRS OF A VILLAGE TO MAKE CERTAIN REPORT
Core Content:
Every village officer and every person residing in a village shall forthwith communicate to the nearest Magistrate or police station information about residence of notorious receivers of stolen property, suspicious persons, commission of non-bailable offences, unnatural deaths, missing persons, and matters affecting maintenance of order.

Procedure: Village Reporting Obligations

Village officers and residents must report:

(a) Permanent/temporary residence of notorious receiver or vendor of stolen property

(b) Resort or passage of suspected robber, escaped convict, or proclaimed offender

(c) Commission or intention to commit non-bailable offence or offences under BNS sections 189, 191

(d) Sudden/unnatural death, suspicious death, discovery of corpse, disappearance of person raising suspicion of non-bailable offence

(e) Acts outside India near the village that would be offences under specified BNS sections (103, 105, 111, 112, 113, 178-181, 305, 307, 309-312, 326, 331, 332)

(f) Any matter likely to affect maintenance of order, prevention of crime, or safety directed by District Magistrate

"Village" includes village lands

"Proclaimed offender" includes persons proclaimed in any territory in India for offences punishable with 10+ years, life, or death

Illustration:
The village headman (a village officer) notices that a known criminal has started living in an abandoned house in the village. The headman must immediately report this to the nearest police station. Similarly, if a village resident finds a dead body in suspicious circumstances, he must report it.

BNSS SECTION 35 - WHEN POLICE MAY ARREST WITHOUT WARRANT
Core Content:
A police officer may arrest without warrant any person who commits a cognizable offence in their presence, or against whom a reasonable complaint exists of having committed a cognizable offence. For offences punishable with less than 7 years, arrest requires recorded reasons and necessity criteria. For offences punishable with less than 3 years where the person is infirm or above 60 years, prior permission from Deputy Superintendent of Police is required.

Procedure: Arrest with Notice

For offences punishable with death, or more than 7 years: police officer may arrest without warrant

For offences punishable with less than 7 years: police officer shall record reasons in writing why arrest is necessary (prevent further offence, proper investigation, prevent evidence tampering, prevent inducement to witnesses, ensure court presence)

If arrest is not required, police officer shall issue a notice directing the person to appear before him at a specified place

The person shall comply with the notice and continue to comply

If the person complies, he shall not be arrested unless reasons are recorded that arrest is necessary

If the person fails to comply or refuses to identify himself, police officer may arrest him

For offences punishable with less than 3 years where the person is infirm or above 60 years, arrest requires prior permission from Deputy Superintendent of Police or above

Illustration:
A is accused of theft punishable with 4 years imprisonment. The police officer believes arrest is not necessary to ensure A's presence. The officer issues a notice to A to appear at the police station. A appears as directed and continues to cooperate. The officer shall not arrest A. However, if later A fails to appear, the officer may arrest him.

BNSS SECTION 36 - PROCEDURE OF ARREST AND DUTIES OF OFFICER MAKING ARREST
Core Content:
Every police officer making an arrest must bear accurate, visible, and clear identification of his name. A memorandum of arrest shall be prepared, attested by a family member or respectable local person, and countersigned by the arrested person.

Procedure: Arrest Memorandum

Police officer shall bear an identification badge with his name clearly visible

Prepare a memorandum of arrest containing:

(i) Attested by at least one witness who is a family member of the arrested person OR a respectable member of the locality

(ii) Countersigned by the arrested person

If the memorandum is not attested by a family member, inform the arrested person that he has the right to have a relative or friend informed of his arrest

State Government shall establish police control rooms at district and State level

Designate a police officer (not below Assistant Sub-Inspector) in every district and police station to maintain information about arrested persons (names, addresses, nature of offence), prominently displayed in digital mode

Illustration:
Police officer arrests X for robbery. The officer has a visible name badge. He calls Y, a neighbour, to witness the arrest. He prepares a memorandum, Y attests it, and X countersigns it. No family member is present, so the officer informs X that he has the right to have his brother informed about the arrest.

BNSS SECTION 37 - DESIGNATED POLICE OFFICER
Core Content:
The State Government shall establish a police control room in every district and at State level. It shall designate a police officer in every district and police station (not below the rank of Assistant Sub-Inspector) responsible for maintaining information about arrested persons, which shall be prominently displayed including in digital mode.

Procedure: Designated Officer Duties

Establish police control room at district level and State level

Designate a police officer (not below Assistant Sub-Inspector) in every district

Designate a police officer (not below Assistant Sub-Inspector) in every police station

Such officer shall maintain information about:

(i) Names of persons arrested

(ii) Addresses of persons arrested

(iii) Nature of offence with which charged

This information shall be prominently displayed in every police station and at district headquarters (including in digital mode)

Illustration:
The State Government designates Officer X as the designated police officer for District A. Officer X maintains a digital database showing all persons arrested in the district, their addresses, and the charges against them. This database is displayed on a screen at the district headquarters and at each police station for public access.

BNSS SECTION 38 - RIGHT OF ARRESTED PERSON TO MEET AN ADVOCATE OF HIS CHOICE DURING INTERROGATION
Core Content:
When any person is arrested and interrogated by the police, he shall be entitled to meet an advocate of his choice during interrogation, though not throughout interrogation.

Procedure: Access to Advocate

Upon arrest, the person may request to meet an advocate of his choice

The police shall allow the arrested person to meet his advocate during interrogation

The advocate may NOT be present throughout the entire interrogation

The meeting is permitted for consultation purposes

Illustration:
X is arrested and taken to the police station for interrogation. X says, "I want to meet my lawyer, Mr. Y." The police allow Mr. Y to meet X during the interrogation process. Mr. Y advises X for 15 minutes, then leaves. The interrogation continues without Mr. Y present.

BNSS SECTION 39 - ARREST ON REFUSAL TO GIVE NAME AND RESIDENCE
Core Content:
When any person who has committed or has been accused of committing a non-cognizable offence refuses to give his name and residence or gives a false name/residence, he may be arrested. Once the true name and residence are ascertained, he shall be released on bond or bail bond.

Procedure: Arrest for Non-Disclosure

A person commits or is accused of a non-cognizable offence in the presence of a police officer

The officer demands his name and residence

The person refuses to give name/residence OR gives name/residence that the officer believes is false

The officer may arrest the person to ascertain his name and residence

Once true name and residence are ascertained, he shall be released on bond or bail bond to appear before a Magistrate if required

If the person is not resident in India, the bail bond shall be secured by a surety or sureties resident in India

If true name and residence are not ascertained within 24 hours from arrest, OR he fails to execute bond/bail bond, he shall be forwarded to the nearest Magistrate having jurisdiction

Illustration:
X is caught shoplifting (non-cognizable offence). The police officer asks X for his name and address. X refuses to tell him. The officer may arrest X. Later, X's true identity is found. The officer releases X on bond. If X's identity is not found within 24 hours, X is produced before a Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 40 - ARREST BY PRIVATE PERSON AND PROCEDURE ON SUCH ARREST
Core Content:
Any private person may arrest any person who in his presence commits a non-bailable and cognizable offence, or any proclaimed offender. Within six hours from such arrest, he shall make over the arrested person to a police officer.

Procedure: Private Person Arrest

A private person may arrest or cause to be arrested any person who:

(a) Commits a non-bailable and cognizable offence in his presence

(b) Is a proclaimed offender

Within six hours from such arrest, he shall make over or cause to be made over the arrested person to a police officer

In absence of a police officer, take such person in custody to the nearest police station

If there is reason to believe the person committed an offence under section 35(1), a police officer shall take him in custody

If he committed a non-cognizable offence and refuses to give name/residence or gives false name/residence, he shall be dealt with under section 39

If there is no sufficient reason to believe he committed any offence, he shall be at once released

Illustration:
X sees Y committing a robbery (non-bailable and cognizable offence) in front of him. X catches Y and holds him. Within 4 hours, X takes Y to the nearest police station and hands him over to the police officer. The police officer takes Y into custody. If Y had committed only a minor non-cognizable offence, he would be released.

BNSS SECTION 41 - ARREST BY MAGISTRATE
Core Content:
When any offence is committed in the presence of a Magistrate (Executive or Judicial) within his local jurisdiction, he may himself arrest or order any person to arrest the offender. Any Magistrate may at any time arrest or direct the arrest, in his presence, within his local jurisdiction, of any person for whose arrest he is competent to issue a warrant.

Procedure: Magistrate Arrest

Offence committed in the presence of a Magistrate within his local jurisdiction

Magistrate may himself arrest the offender OR order any person to arrest the offender

Thereafter, subject to bail provisions, commit the offender to custody

Any Magistrate (Executive or Judicial) may at any time arrest or direct arrest, in his presence, within his local jurisdiction, of any person for whose arrest he could issue a warrant

Illustration:
A Judicial Magistrate is walking in the market when he sees X assaulting Y. The Magistrate may immediately arrest X himself or order a nearby person to arrest X. The Magistrate then sends X to custody or grants bail as per law.

BNSS SECTION 42 - PROTECTION OF MEMBERS OF ARMED FORCES FROM ARREST
Core Content:
No member of the Armed Forces of the Union shall be arrested for anything done or purported to be done by him in the discharge of his official duties except after obtaining the consent of the Central Government. The State Government may extend this protection to forces charged with maintenance of public order.

Procedure: Armed Forces Protection

For Armed Forces of the Union: arrest requires Central Government consent

For any act done or purported to be done in discharge of official duties

State Government may, by notification, direct that this provision applies to members of forces charged with maintenance of public order

Upon such notification, the expression "Central Government" shall be substituted with "State Government"

Illustration:
An Army soldier fires at a suspected terrorist during a military operation. The suspected terrorist's family wants the soldier arrested. The police cannot arrest the soldier without first obtaining consent from the Central Government. The State Government may issue a notification giving similar protection to State police forces.

BNSS SECTION 43 - ARREST HOW MADE
Core Content:
In making an arrest, the police officer shall actually touch or confine the body of the person to be arrested unless there is submission by word or action. For women, submission on oral intimation is presumed. Force may be used if the person resists. Handcuffs may be used for habitual or repeat offenders or for specified serious offences.

Procedure: Physical Arrest and Handcuffs

Police officer shall actually touch or confine the body of the person to be arrested

If the person submits by word or action, actual touching is not required

For a woman: submission on oral intimation of arrest shall be presumed; police officer shall not touch her body unless the officer is female

If the person forcibly resists or attempts to evade arrest, the police officer may use all means necessary to effect the arrest

Handcuffs may be used while arresting or producing before court a person who is:

(a) Habitual or repeat offender

(b) Escaped from custody

(c) Committed organised crime, terrorist act, drug related crime, illegal possession of arms and ammunition

(d) Committed murder, rape, acid attack, counterfeiting coins/currency notes, human trafficking, sexual offence against children, offence against the State

Nothing gives the right to cause death of a person not accused of death penalty or life imprisonment

No woman shall be arrested after sunset and before sunrise except in exceptional circumstances, with prior written permission of a Magistrate of the first class

Illustration:
A is a habitual offender accused of murder. Police officer arrests A. Since A has a history of escape attempts, the officer may use handcuffs while arresting A and while producing him before court. If A is a woman, the officer must arrest her before sunset unless exceptional circumstances exist and a first class Magistrate has given written permission.

BNSS SECTION 44 - SEARCH OF PLACE ENTERED BY PERSON SOUGHT TO BE ARRESTED
Core Content:
If a person acting under a warrant of arrest or a police officer has reason to believe that the person to be arrested has entered any place, the person in charge of such place shall allow free ingress and afford reasonable facilities for search. If ingress cannot be obtained, the officer may break open doors/windows.

Procedure: Search of Premises

Person with warrant or police officer believes arrested person has entered a place

Person residing in or in charge of such place shall allow free ingress and afford reasonable facilities for search

If ingress cannot be obtained, it is lawful for the officer to enter and search

To effect entrance, break open any outer or inner door or window of any house or place after:

(a) Notifying his authority and purpose

(b) Demanding admittance duly made

(c) Cannot otherwise obtain admittance

If the place is an apartment occupied by a female (not the person to be arrested) who does not appear in public, the officer shall:

(a) Give notice that she is at liberty to withdraw

(b) Afford her every reasonable facility for withdrawing

(c) Then break open the apartment and enter

Any police officer may break open any door/window to liberate himself or any person lawfully detained

Illustration:
Police officer X has a warrant to arrest Y. X believes Y has entered Z's house. X demands entry. Z refuses. X can break open the door after notifying his authority and demanding entry. If the house has a woman who does not appear in public, X must first give her notice to withdraw before entering.

BNSS SECTION 45 - PURSUIT OF OFFENDERS INTO OTHER JURISDICTIONS
Core Content:
A police officer may, for the purpose of arresting without warrant any person whom he is authorised to arrest, pursue such person into any place in India.

Procedure: Fresh Pursuit

Police officer is authorised to arrest a person without warrant

That person runs away or goes to any other place in India

The police officer may pursue that person into that place

This applies to any place in India

Illustration:
Police officer X is chasing Y who just committed a robbery. Y runs from Delhi into Haryana. X can continue the pursuit into Haryana without needing any fresh warrant or permission from Haryana police.

BNSS SECTION 46 - NO UNNECESSARY RESTRAINT
Core Content:
The person arrested shall not be subjected to more restraint than is necessary to prevent his escape.

Procedure: Use of Restraint

Any restraint used on the arrested person must be:

(i) Only to prevent escape

(ii) No more than necessary for that purpose

Excessive or unnecessary restraint is prohibited

Illustration:
X is arrested for a minor theft. He is cooperative and shows no intention to escape. The police officer cannot tie X's hands and feet with multiple ropes. Using handcuffs may be unnecessary if X is not a flight risk. However, if X has a history of escaping custody, reasonable restraint is permitted.

BNSS SECTION 47 - PERSON ARRESTED TO BE INFORMED OF GROUNDS OF ARREST AND OF RIGHT TO BAIL
Core Content:
Every police officer or other person arresting any person without warrant shall forthwith communicate to him full particulars of the offence for which he is arrested or other grounds for such arrest.

Procedure: Information of Arrest Grounds and Bail Right

Police officer shall forthwith communicate to the arrested person:

(i) Full particulars of the offence for which he is arrested

(ii) Other grounds for such arrest

If the person is arrested without warrant for an offence other than a non-bailable offence, the police officer shall inform him that:

(i) He is entitled to be released on bail

(ii) He may arrange for sureties on his behalf

Illustration:
Police officer arrests X without warrant for theft, which is a bailable offence. The officer immediately tells X: "You are being arrested for theft of a mobile phone from a shop. This is a bailable offence. You can arrange for sureties and get bail."

BNSS SECTION 48 - OBLIGATION OF PERSON MAKING ARREST TO INFORM ABOUT ARREST TO RELATIVE OR FRIEND
Core Content:
Every police officer or other person making any arrest shall forthwith give information regarding such arrest and the place where the arrested person is being held to any relative, friend, or other person nominated by the arrested person, and also to the designated police officer in the district.

Procedure: Notification of Arrest

Police officer shall forthwith inform the following about the arrest and place of custody:

(i) Any relative of the arrested person

(ii) Any friend of the arrested person

(iii) Any other person disclosed or nominated by the arrested person

(iv) The designated police officer in the district

Police officer shall inform the arrested person of these rights as soon as he is brought to the police station

An entry of who has been informed shall be made in a book kept at the police station in the form prescribed by State Government rules

The Magistrate before whom the arrested person is produced shall satisfy himself that the above requirements have been complied with

Illustration:
Police officer arrests X. X says, "Please inform my brother Y at phone number 1234567890." The officer immediately calls Y and informs him that X has been arrested and is being held at the city police station. The officer also records this in the police station register. When X is produced before the Magistrate, the Magistrate checks that Y was properly informed.

BNSS SECTION 49 - SEARCH OF ARRESTED PERSON
Core Content:
When a person is arrested under a warrant not providing for bail, or under a warrant providing for bail but cannot furnish bail, or arrested without warrant and cannot be admitted to bail or cannot furnish bail, the officer making the arrest may search such person and place all articles (other than necessary wearing apparel) in safe custody. A receipt for seized articles shall be given.

Procedure: Search of Person

Arrest occurs under following circumstances:

(i) Warrant without bail provision

(ii) Warrant with bail but person cannot furnish bail

(iii) Arrest without warrant and cannot be admitted to bail or cannot furnish bail

(iv) Arrest by private person under warrant - police officer to whom person is handed over may search

The officer may search such person

All articles found upon him (other than necessary wearing apparel) shall be placed in safe custody

A receipt showing the articles taken in possession shall be given to the arrested person

When a female is to be searched, the search shall be made by another female with strict regard to decency

Illustration:
X is arrested without warrant for a non-bailable offence. The police officer searches X and finds a wallet, a knife, and ₹10,000 cash. The officer takes the knife and cash into custody, gives X a receipt listing these items, but allows X to keep his shirt and pants (necessary wearing apparel). If X were female, a female officer would conduct the search.

BNSS SECTION 50 - POWER TO SEIZE OFFENSIVE WEAPONS
Core Content:
The police officer or other person making any arrest may, immediately after the arrest, take from the person arrested any offensive weapons which he has about his person, and shall deliver all weapons so taken to the Court or officer before which or whom the arrested person is required to be produced.

Procedure: Seizure of Weapons

Immediately after arrest, the police officer may take any offensive weapons found on the arrested person's person

The officer shall deliver all such weapons to:

(i) The Court before which the arrested person is to be produced, OR

(ii) The officer before whom the arrested person is to be produced

Illustration:
Police officer arrests X. Upon searching X, the officer finds a knife and a pistol on X. The officer seizes both weapons. When X is produced before the Magistrate, the officer hands over the knife and pistol to the Magistrate as part of the case property.

BNSS SECTION 51 - EXAMINATION OF ACCUSED BY MEDICAL PRACTITIONER AT REQUEST OF POLICE OFFICER
Core Content:
When a person is arrested for an offence and there are reasonable grounds to believe that examination of his person will afford evidence, a registered medical practitioner may make such examination at the request of a police officer. For a female, examination shall be made only by or under supervision of a female registered medical practitioner.

Procedure: Medical Examination of Accused

Person arrested for an offence of such nature that examination of his person may afford evidence

Police officer requests a registered medical practitioner to conduct examination

Registered medical practitioner may make such examination as is reasonably necessary to ascertain facts

Force may be used as is reasonably necessary for that purpose

For a female: examination shall be made only by or under supervision of a female registered medical practitioner

The registered medical practitioner shall, without any delay, forward the examination report to the investigating officer

"Examination" includes blood tests, blood stains, semen, swabs (for sexual offences), sputum, sweat, hair samples, finger nail clippings, DNA profiling, and other tests

"Registered medical practitioner" means medical practitioner with qualification under National Medical Commission Act, 2019

Illustration:
X is arrested for a hit-and-run accident. The police suspect X was driving under the influence of alcohol. The police request a registered medical practitioner to take X's blood sample. The practitioner draws blood for testing. For a female accused, a female doctor must conduct the examination.

BNSS SECTION 52 - EXAMINATION OF PERSON ACCUSED OF RAPE BY MEDICAL PRACTITIONER
Core Content:
When a person is arrested for rape or attempt to commit rape, a registered medical practitioner employed in a Government hospital (or within 16 km, any registered medical practitioner) may examine him at the request of a police officer. The report shall include name, age, marks of injury, material taken for DNA profiling, and other particulars.

Procedure: Medical Examination in Rape Cases

Person arrested for rape or attempt to commit rape

Registered medical practitioner employed in Government hospital or local authority hospital shall conduct examination

If no such practitioner within 16 km from place of offence, any other registered medical practitioner may conduct examination

Police officer makes request; person acting in good faith under his direction may assist

Reasonable force may be used for examination

The practitioner shall without delay examine and prepare report with:

(i) Name and address of accused and person who brought him

(ii) Age of accused

(iii) Marks of injury on accused, if any

(iv) Description of material taken from accused for DNA profiling

(v) Other material particulars

Report shall state reasons for each conclusion

Exact time of commencement and completion of examination shall be noted

Report shall be forwarded to investigating officer, who shall forward to Magistrate under section 193

Illustration:
X is arrested for rape of a woman. The police take X to the Government hospital. A registered medical practitioner examines X, notes any injuries on X's body, takes swabs and blood for DNA profiling, and prepares a detailed report. The report notes the exact time examination started (2:00 PM) and ended (2:45 PM). The report is sent to the investigating officer.

BNSS SECTION 53 - EXAMINATION OF ARRESTED PERSON BY MEDICAL OFFICER
Core Content:
When any person is arrested, he shall be examined by a medical officer in service of Central or State Government soon after arrest. If such medical officer is not available, by a registered medical practitioner. The record of examination mentioning any injuries or marks of violence shall be prepared. A copy of the report shall be furnished to the arrested person.

Procedure: Post-Arrest Medical Examination

Soon after arrest is made, the arrested person shall be examined by:

(i) Medical officer in service of Central Government or State Government

(ii) If such medical officer not available, by a registered medical practitioner

If the medical officer or practitioner believes one more examination is necessary, he may do so

For a female arrested person: examination shall be made only by or under supervision of a female medical officer; if not available, by a female registered medical practitioner

The medical officer or practitioner shall prepare a record of examination mentioning:

(i) Any injuries or marks of violence upon the person arrested

(ii) Approximate time when such injuries or marks may have been inflicted

A copy of the examination report shall be furnished to the arrested person or person nominated by him

Illustration:
X is arrested for assault. He claims the police beat him during arrest. X is taken to a government hospital where a medical officer examines him, notes bruises on his arms, and records that the bruises appear to have been inflicted within the last 2 hours. A copy of this report is given to X. If X is female, a female medical officer must conduct the examination.

BNSS SECTION 54 - IDENTIFICATION OF PERSON ARRESTED
Core Content:
Where a person is arrested and his identification by any other person is necessary for investigation, the Court having jurisdiction may, on request of the police station officer, direct the arrested person to subject himself to identification. If the identifying person is mentally or physically disabled, the process shall be under Magistrate supervision and recorded by audio-video electronic means.

Procedure: Identification Parade

Person arrested for an offence

His identification by any other person(s) is necessary for investigation

Officer in charge of police station makes request to Court having jurisdiction

Court may direct the arrested person to subject himself to identification by any person(s) in such manner as Court deems fit

If the identifying person is mentally or physically disabled:

(a) Process of identification shall take place under supervision of a Magistrate

(b) Magistrate shall take appropriate steps to ensure identification using methods the person is comfortable with

(c) Identification process shall be recorded by audio-video electronic means

Illustration:
X is arrested for robbery. The victim Y can identify X. The police request the Court to hold an identification parade. The Court directs X to participate in the parade. If Y is visually impaired, a Magistrate supervises the identification, using voice recognition or touch methods, and the entire process is video recorded.

BNSS SECTION 55 - PROCEDURE WHEN POLICE OFFICER DEPUTES SUBORDINATE TO ARREST WITHOUT WARRANT
Core Content:
When an officer in charge of a police station requires any subordinate officer to arrest a person without warrant, he shall deliver an order in writing specifying the person to be arrested and the offence. The subordinate officer shall notify the substance of the order to the person to be arrested and show him the order if required.

Procedure: Subordinate Arrest Order

Officer in charge of police station or investigating officer requires subordinate officer to arrest a person without warrant (not in his presence)

He shall deliver to the subordinate officer an order in writing specifying:

(i) The person to be arrested

(ii) The offence or other cause for which arrest is to be made

The subordinate officer shall, before making arrest, notify to the person to be arrested the substance of the order

If required by the person, the subordinate officer shall show him the order

Illustration:
The SHO of City Police Station wants Sub-Inspector X to arrest Y who is suspected of theft. The SHO gives X a written order: "Arrest Y for theft under BNS section 303." X goes to Y's house and says, "Y, I am arresting you for theft." Y asks to see the order. X shows him the written order from the SHO.

BNSS SECTION 56 - HEALTH AND SAFETY OF ARRESTED PERSON
Core Content:
It shall be the duty of the person having the custody of an accused to take reasonable care of the health and safety of the accused.

Procedure: Custody Obligations

Any person who has custody of an accused (police, jail authorities, etc.) is responsible

They must take reasonable care of:

(i) Health of the accused

(ii) Safety of the accused

This includes providing medical attention when needed and protecting from harm

Illustration:
X is in police custody. He complains of chest pain. The police officer must immediately take X to a doctor or hospital for medical attention. If X is attacked by other prisoners, the custodial authorities must protect him. Failure to do so is a breach of duty.

BNSS SECTION 57 - PERSON ARRESTED TO BE TAKEN BEFORE MAGISTRATE OR OFFICER IN CHARGE OF POLICE STATION
Core Content:
A police officer making an arrest without warrant shall, without unnecessary delay and subject to bail provisions, take or send the person arrested before a Magistrate having jurisdiction in the case, or before the officer in charge of a police station.

Procedure: Production After Arrest

Police officer makes arrest without warrant

He shall take or send the arrested person before:

(i) A Magistrate having jurisdiction in the case, OR

(ii) The officer in charge of a police station

This must be done without unnecessary delay

Subject to bail provisions (if person can be granted bail, he may be released instead)

Illustration:
Police officer X arrests Y for theft at 10:00 AM. The police station is 30 minutes away. X takes Y to the police station and then to the Magistrate. By 4:00 PM, Y is produced before the Magistrate. This is without unnecessary delay. If X kept Y in a lockup for 3 days without producing him, that would violate this section.

BNSS SECTION 58 - PERSON ARRESTED NOT TO BE DETAINED MORE THAN TWENTY-FOUR HOURS
Core Content:
Officers in charge of police stations shall report to the District Magistrate (or Sub-divisional Magistrate if directed) the cases of all persons arrested without warrant within their station limits, whether such persons have been admitted to bail or otherwise.

Procedure: 24-Hour Rule and Reporting

Person arrested without warrant cannot be detained beyond 24 hours without production before Magistrate (see section 187)

Officer in charge of police station shall report to the District Magistrate (or Sub-divisional Magistrate if directed) about:

(i) All persons arrested without warrant within their station limits

(ii) Whether such persons have been admitted to bail or not

Illustration:
The SHO of City Police Station makes a weekly report to the District Magistrate listing all persons arrested without warrant in the past week, showing their names, offences, and whether they got bail or were sent to jail.

BNSS SECTION 59 - POLICE TO REPORT APPREHENSIONS
Core Content:
Officers in charge of police stations shall report to the District Magistrate (or Sub-divisional Magistrate if directed) the cases of all persons arrested without warrant within the limits of their respective stations, whether such persons have been admitted to bail or otherwise.

Procedure: Reporting Apprehensions

Same as section 58 - reporting requirement

All arrests without warrant must be reported to District Magistrate or Sub-divisional Magistrate

Report must indicate whether the person was granted bail or not

Illustration:
The SHO sends a daily report to the District Magistrate listing: "Arrested: X for theft (bail granted), Y for assault (bail refused, sent to jail), Z for robbery (in custody)."

BNSS SECTION 60 - DISCHARGE OF PERSON APPREHENDED
Core Content:
No person who has been arrested by a police officer shall be discharged except on his bond, or bail bond, or under the special order of a Magistrate.

Procedure: Lawful Discharge

A person arrested by police cannot be simply let go

He can be discharged only in three ways:

(i) On his own bond

(ii) On bail bond (with sureties)

(iii) Under special order of a Magistrate

Police cannot release an arrested person without following these procedures

Illustration:
X is arrested for theft. The police later realise the complaint was false. They cannot simply tell X "go home." They must either take a bond from X (promising to appear if needed) or obtain a Magistrate's order discharging him. If X is granted bail, he gives a bail bond with sureties and is released.

BNSS SECTION 61 - POWER, ON ESCAPE, TO PURSUE AND RETAKE
Core Content:
If a person in lawful custody escapes or is rescued, the person from whose custody he escaped or was rescued may immediately pursue and arrest him in any place in India. The provisions of section 44 (search of place entered) shall apply to such arrests.

Procedure: Fresh Pursuit After Escape

A person in lawful custody escapes OR is rescued

The person from whose custody he escaped or was rescued may immediately pursue and arrest him

This can be done in any place in India (no territorial limitation)

Section 44 (breaking open doors/windows to search) applies to such arrests, even if the person making arrest is:

(a) Not acting under a warrant

(b) Not a police officer having authority to arrest

Illustration:
X is in police custody at the police station. He escapes and runs to another city 500 km away. The police officer from whose custody X escaped can immediately pursue X to that city and arrest him without needing a fresh warrant. If X hides in a house, the officer can break open the door after following section 44 procedure.

BNSS SECTION 62 - ARREST TO BE MADE STRICTLY ACCORDING TO SANHITA
Core Content:
No arrest shall be made except in accordance with the provisions of this Sanhita or any other law for the time being in force providing for arrest.

Procedure: Lawful Arrest Only

All arrests must comply with BNSS provisions

Or comply with any other law that provides for arrest (e.g., NDPS Act, Customs Act)

Any arrest made outside these legal provisions is illegal

This section reinforces the principle that no one can be arrested arbitrarily

Illustration:
A police officer arrests X simply because X looked suspicious and refused to answer questions. No offence has been committed, no warrant exists, and no provision of BNSS permits such arrest. This arrest is illegal under section 62. X can challenge the arrest in court and seek compensation.


BNSS SECTION 63 - FORM OF SUMMONS
Core Content:
Every summons issued by a Court shall be in writing, in duplicate, signed by the presiding officer or such other officer as the High Court may direct, and shall bear the seal of the Court. Summons may also be issued in encrypted or any other form of electronic communication bearing the image of the seal of the Court or digital signature.

Procedure: Issuing Summons

Summons shall be in writing, in duplicate

Signed by presiding officer of the Court OR other officer authorised by High Court rules

Shall bear the seal of the Court

Alternative method: encrypted or other form of electronic communication bearing:

(i) Image of the seal of the Court, OR

(ii) Digital signature

Illustration:
The Court issues a summons to X to appear as a witness. The presiding officer signs the written summons in duplicate and affixes the Court seal. Alternatively, the Court sends an encrypted email with the Court's digital signature to X's registered email address.

BNSS SECTION 64 - SUMMONS HOW SERVED
Core Content:
Every summons shall be served by a police officer, or by an officer of the Court issuing it or other public servant. The summons shall be served personally on the person summoned by delivering one duplicate. Summons bearing Court seal may also be served by electronic communication. The person served shall sign a receipt on the back of the other duplicate.

Procedure: Service of Summons

Summons shall be served by:

(i) A police officer, OR

(ii) Officer of the Court issuing it, OR

(iii) Other public servant (subject to State Government rules)

Police station or registrar in Court shall maintain a register with address, email, phone number, and other details as per State Government rules

If practicable, serve personally by delivering or tendering one duplicate of the summons

Summons bearing image of Court seal may also be served by electronic communication in form and manner prescribed by State Government rules

Person served personally shall, if required, sign a receipt on the back of the other duplicate

Illustration:
The Court issues a summons to X. A police officer goes to X's house, hands X one copy of the summons, and asks X to sign the second copy as proof of receipt. X signs. The officer returns the signed duplicate to the Court. Alternatively, the Court emails a digitally signed summons to X, and X confirms receipt electronically.

BNSS SECTION 65 - SERVICE OF SUMMONS ON CORPORATE BODIES, FIRMS, AND SOCIETIES
Core Content:
Service on a company or corporation may be effected by serving on the Director, Manager, Secretary, or other officer, or by registered post addressed to such officer. Service on a firm or association may be effected by serving on any partner or by registered post addressed to such partner.

Procedure: Service on Legal Entities

For a company or corporation (including society registered under Societies Registration Act, 1860):

(i) Serve on Director, Manager, Secretary, or other officer, OR

(ii) Send by registered post addressed to Director, Manager, Secretary, or other officer in India

Service deemed effected when letter would arrive in ordinary course of post

For a firm or other association of individuals:

(i) Serve on any partner of such firm or association, OR

(ii) Send by registered post addressed to such partner

Service deemed effected when letter would arrive in ordinary course of post

Illustration:
A summons is issued to XYZ Company. The serving officer delivers the summons to the Company Secretary at the registered office. Alternatively, the Court sends the summons by registered post to the Managing Director. Service is considered complete when the letter would normally have arrived. For a partnership firm, serving one partner is sufficient.

BNSS SECTION 66 - SERVICE WHEN PERSONS SUMMONED CANNOT BE FOUND
Core Content:
Where the person summoned cannot be found with due diligence, the summons may be served by leaving one duplicate with some adult member of his family residing with him. The person with whom the summons is left shall sign a receipt if required. A servant is not a member of the family.

Procedure: Substituted Service on Family Member

Person summoned cannot be found even after exercise of due diligence

Summons may be served by leaving one duplicate with some adult member of his family residing with him

The family member shall, if required, sign a receipt on the back of the other duplicate

A servant is NOT a member of the family for this purpose

Illustration:
X is summoned by the Court but the police officer cannot find X anywhere despite checking his workplace, frequented places, and calling his phone. X's adult son Y lives with X. The officer leaves the summons with Y. Y signs a receipt. Service is considered valid even though X did not personally receive it.

BNSS SECTION 67 - PROCEDURE WHEN SERVICE CANNOT BE EFFECTED AS BEFORE PROVIDED
Core Content:
If service cannot be effected by due diligence as provided in sections 64, 65, or 66, the serving officer shall affix one duplicate of the summons to a conspicuous part of the house where the person ordinarily resides. The Court may then either declare that the summons has been duly served or order fresh service.

Procedure: Affixation of Summons

Service cannot be effected by due diligence under sections 64, 65, or 66

Serving officer shall affix one duplicate of the summons to some conspicuous part of the house or homestead where the person ordinarily resides

The Court, after making such inquiries as it thinks fit, may either:

(i) Declare that the summons has been duly served, OR

(ii) Order fresh service in such manner as it considers proper

Illustration:
X cannot be found. No adult family member is available. The police officer affixes a copy of the summons to the front door of X's house. The Court reviews the officer's report, makes inquiries, and declares that the summons has been duly served by affixation. X is now deemed to have notice of the proceedings.

BNSS SECTION 68 - SERVICE ON GOVERNMENT SERVANT
Core Content:
Where the person summoned is in active service of the Government, the Court shall ordinarily send the summons in duplicate to the head of the office where such person is employed. The head shall cause the summons to be served and return it to the Court with his signature. Such signature shall be evidence of due service.

Procedure: Service on Government Employees

Person summoned is in active service of the Government

Court shall ordinarily send summons in duplicate to the head of the office where the person is employed

The head of office shall:

(i) Cause the summons to be served in the manner provided by section 64

(ii) Return the summons to the Court under his signature with the required endorsement

The signature of the head of office shall be evidence of due service

Illustration:
X is a government employee working in the Ministry of Finance. The Court sends a summons in duplicate to the Secretary of the Ministry. The Secretary arranges for X to receive the summons personally, signs the return, and sends it back to the Court. The Court accepts the Secretary's signature as proof that X was served.

BNSS SECTION 69 - SERVICE OF SUMMONS OUTSIDE LOCAL LIMITS
Core Content:
When a Court desires that a summons issued by it shall be served at any place outside its local jurisdiction, it shall ordinarily send such summons in duplicate to a Magistrate within whose local jurisdiction the person summoned resides or is present.

Procedure: Out-of-Jurisdiction Service

Court issues a summons to be served at a place outside its local jurisdiction

Court shall ordinarily send the summons in duplicate to a Magistrate within whose local jurisdiction the person summoned resides or is present

That Magistrate shall cause the summons to be served

Illustration:
A Court in Delhi issues a summons to X who lives in Mumbai. The Delhi Court sends the summons in duplicate to a Magistrate in Mumbai. The Mumbai Magistrate arranges for the summons to be served on X and returns the proof of service to the Delhi Court.

BNSS SECTION 70 - PROOF OF SERVICE IN SUCH CASES AND WHEN SERVING OFFICER NOT PRESENT
Core Content:
When a summons is served outside local jurisdiction, an affidavit before a Magistrate that the summons has been served, and a duplicate endorsed by the person served, shall be admissible in evidence. Statements made therein shall be deemed correct unless proven otherwise. All summons served through electronic communication shall be considered duly served.

Procedure: Proof of Service

When summons is served outside local jurisdiction of issuing Court

When serving officer is not present at hearing of the case

An affidavit (purporting to be made before a Magistrate) that summons has been served shall be admissible in evidence

A duplicate of summons endorsed (as per section 64 or 66) by the person to whom it was delivered/tendered/left shall be admissible in evidence

Statements made in such affidavit and duplicate shall be deemed correct unless contrary is proved

Affidavit may be attached to duplicate of summons and returned to the Court

All summons served through electronic communication (under sections 64 to 71) shall be considered duly served. A copy shall be attested and kept as proof of service.

Illustration:
A Delhi Court sends a summons to X in Mumbai. A Mumbai police officer serves X, who signs the duplicate. The officer cannot attend the Delhi Court hearing. The Court accepts an affidavit from the Mumbai officer (sworn before a Mumbai Magistrate) as proof of service, along with the signed duplicate. The statements in the affidavit are presumed correct.

BNSS SECTION 71 - SERVICE OF SUMMONS ON WITNESS
Core Content:
A Court issuing a summons to a witness may, in addition to and simultaneously with the issue of such summons, direct a copy to be served by electronic communication or by registered post at the witness's ordinary residence, business, or work place. When acknowledgement signed by the witness or postal endorsement of refusal is received, or proof of delivery by electronic communication is received, the Court may deem the summons duly served.

Procedure: Additional Service Methods for Witnesses

Court issues summons to a witness

Court may, in addition and simultaneously, direct a copy of the summons to be served by:

(i) Electronic communication, OR

(ii) Registered post addressed to the witness at his ordinary residence, business, or place of work

When any of the following is received, Court may deem summons duly served:

(i) Acknowledgement purporting to be signed by the witness

(ii) Endorsement by postal employee that the witness refused to take delivery

(iii) Proof of delivery of summons by electronic communication to the satisfaction of the Court

Illustration:
The Court issues a summons to witness X. Simultaneously, the Court sends a copy by registered post to X's home address and an email to X's registered email. The postal department returns a receipt signed by X. The Court deems the summons duly served even if the police officer could not personally serve X.

BNSS SECTION 72 - FORM OF WARRANT OF ARREST AND DURATION
Core Content:
Every warrant of arrest issued by a Court shall be in writing, signed by the presiding officer, and shall bear the seal of the Court. Every such warrant shall remain in force until it is cancelled by the Court which issued it, or until it is executed.

Procedure: Issuing Arrest Warrant

Warrant of arrest shall be in writing

Signed by presiding officer of the Court

Shall bear the seal of the Court

Warrant remains in force until:

(i) Cancelled by the Court which issued it, OR

(ii) Executed (person is arrested)

No expiry date - warrant continues indefinitely until cancelled or executed

Illustration:
A Court issues an arrest warrant for X who has absconded. The warrant is signed by the Magistrate and bears the Court's seal. Police officers try to find X but cannot. Five years later, X is found in another city. The same warrant can still be executed - it remains valid until cancelled or executed.

BNSS SECTION 73 - POWER TO DIRECT SECURITY TO BE TAKEN
Core Content:
Any Court issuing a warrant for arrest may direct by endorsement on the warrant that if the person executes a bail bond with sufficient sureties for his attendance, the officer to whom the warrant is directed shall take such security and release the person from custody.

Procedure: Bailable Warrant

Court issues warrant for arrest of any person

Court may, in its discretion, direct by endorsement on the warrant that:

If the person executes a bail bond with sufficient sureties for his attendance before Court at a specified time, the officer shall take such security and release the person from custody

The endorsement shall state:

(a) Number of sureties

(b) Amount in which they and the person are to be respectively bound

(c) Time at which he is to attend before the Court

When security is taken, the officer shall forward the bond to the Court

Illustration:
Court issues warrant for X's arrest but adds an endorsement: "If X gives bail bond of ₹10,000 with one surety of ₹10,000 to appear on March 1, release him." Police arrest X. X arranges a surety. Police take the bond and release X instead of taking him to jail. The bond is forwarded to the Court.

BNSS SECTION 74 - WARRANTS TO WHOM DIRECTED
Core Content:
A warrant of arrest shall ordinarily be directed to one or more police officers. If immediate execution is necessary and no police officer is available, the Court may direct it to any other person or persons. When a warrant is directed to more officers or persons than one, it may be executed by all or any one or more of them.

Procedure: Directing Warrants

Warrant of arrest ordinarily directed to one or more police officers

If immediate execution is necessary AND no police officer is immediately available:

Court may direct warrant to any other person or persons

Such person(s) shall execute the warrant

When warrant directed to more officers/persons than one:

May be executed by all of them

May be executed by any one or more of them

Illustration:
A Court issues an arrest warrant for X who is about to board a flight in 30 minutes. No police officer is at the airport. The Court directs the warrant to the airport security officer. The security officer arrests X. Alternatively, if the warrant is directed to five police officers, any one of them can execute it alone.

BNSS SECTION 75 - WARRANT MAY BE DIRECTED TO ANY PERSON
Core Content:
The Chief Judicial Magistrate or a Magistrate of the first class may direct a warrant to any person within his local jurisdiction for the arrest of any escaped convict, proclaimed offender, or any person accused of a non-bailable offence who is evading arrest.

Procedure: Warrant to Private Person for Specific Categories

Only Chief Judicial Magistrate or Magistrate of first class can do this

May direct warrant to any person within his local jurisdiction

Applicable only for arrest of:

(i) Any escaped convict

(ii) Proclaimed offender

(iii) Any person accused of a non-bailable offence who is evading arrest

Such person shall:

(i) Acknowledge in writing receipt of the warrant

(ii) Execute it if the person is in, or enters, any land or other property under his charge

When arrested, the person shall be made over with the warrant to the nearest police officer

Illustration:
A proclaimed offender X is believed to be hiding on a farm owned by Y. A first class Magistrate issues a warrant directed to Y, the landowner. Y acknowledges receipt in writing. If Y finds X on his farm, Y can arrest X and hand him over to the nearest police officer.

BNSS SECTION 76 - WARRANT DIRECTED TO POLICE OFFICER
Core Content:
A warrant directed to any police officer may also be executed by any other police officer whose name is endorsed upon the warrant by the officer to whom it is directed or endorsed.

Procedure: Endorsement of Warrant

Warrant is directed to a specific police officer (e.g., SHO of City Police Station)

That officer may endorse the warrant by writing another police officer's name on it

The other police officer whose name is endorsed may also execute the warrant

Illustration:
A warrant is directed to SHO A of City Police Station. SHO A is busy with another case. SHO A endorses the warrant: "Sub-Inspector B is authorised to execute this warrant." Sub-Inspector B can now arrest X using this warrant, even though B's name was not originally on it.

BNSS SECTION 77 - NOTIFICATION OF SUBSTANCE OF WARRANT
Core Content:
The police officer or other person executing a warrant of arrest shall notify the substance thereof to the person to be arrested, and, if so required, shall show him the warrant.

Procedure: Informing the Arrestee

When executing a warrant, the officer shall notify the substance of the warrant to the person to be arrested

This means telling the person why he is being arrested

If the person requires to see the warrant, the officer shall show him the warrant

Illustration:
Police officer X goes to arrest Y with a warrant. X says, "Y, I have a warrant for your arrest for the murder of Z." Y asks to see the warrant. X shows Y the warrant document. X then arrests Y.

BNSS SECTION 78 - PERSON ARRESTED TO BE BROUGHT BEFORE COURT WITHOUT DELAY
Core Content:
The police officer or other person executing a warrant of arrest shall, without unnecessary delay, bring the person arrested before the Court before which he is required by law to produce such person. Such delay shall not, in any case, exceed twenty-four hours exclusive of the time necessary for the journey from the place of arrest to the Magistrate's Court.

Procedure: Production After Warrant Arrest

Execute warrant of arrest

Subject to section 73 (bail on endorsement), bring the arrested person before the Court

Must be done without unnecessary delay

Maximum delay: 24 hours (excluding journey time from place of arrest to Magistrate's Court)

Illustration:
X is arrested at 10:00 AM in a village 6 hours away from the Magistrate's Court. Travel time is 6 hours. X must be produced before the Magistrate by 10:00 AM next day + 6 hours = 4:00 PM next day at the latest. If produced later, the police officer has violated this section.

BNSS SECTION 79 - WHERE WARRANT MAY BE EXECUTED
Core Content:
A warrant of arrest may be executed at any place in India.

Procedure: Territorial Scope of Warrant

Any warrant issued by any Court in India

Can be executed at any place in India

No territorial restriction

Illustration:
A Court in Tamil Nadu issues an arrest warrant for X. X is found in Punjab. Punjab police can execute the Tamil Nadu warrant. No need to get a fresh warrant from a Punjab Court.

BNSS SECTION 80 - WARRANT FORWARDED FOR EXECUTION OUTSIDE JURISDICTION
Core Content:
When a warrant is to be executed outside the local jurisdiction of the Court issuing it, the Court may forward it by post or otherwise to any Executive Magistrate or District Superintendent of Police or Commissioner of Police within whose jurisdiction it is to be executed. The Court shall also forward the substance of the information against the person and sufficient documents to enable the receiving Court to decide on bail.

Procedure: Sending Warrant to Another Jurisdiction

Warrant to be executed outside local jurisdiction of issuing Court

Issuing Court may forward warrant by post or otherwise to:

(i) Any Executive Magistrate, OR

(ii) District Superintendent of Police, OR

(iii) Commissioner of Police
within whose local jurisdiction it is to be executed

The receiving Magistrate/SP/Commissioner shall endorse his name and cause it to be executed

Issuing Court shall forward along with warrant:

(i) Substance of the information against the person to be arrested

(ii) Such documents as may be sufficient to enable the Court acting under section 83 to decide whether bail should or should not be granted

Illustration:
Delhi Court issues warrant for X who is in Mumbai. Delhi Court forwards the warrant to the Commissioner of Police, Mumbai. The forwarding includes a summary of the case against X and relevant documents. Mumbai Police execute the warrant and produce X before a Mumbai Magistrate who can decide on bail based on the documents sent.

BNSS SECTION 81 - WARRANT DIRECTED TO POLICE OFFICER FOR EXECUTION OUTSIDE JURISDICTION
Core Content:
When a warrant directed to a police officer is to be executed beyond the local jurisdiction, he shall ordinarily take it for endorsement to an Executive Magistrate or to a police officer not below the rank of officer in charge of a police station within whose jurisdiction it is to be executed. If delay would prevent execution, he may execute without such endorsement.

Procedure: Execution with or without Endorsement

Warrant directed to a police officer

To be executed beyond local jurisdiction of issuing Court

Ordinary procedure: Take warrant for endorsement to:

(i) An Executive Magistrate, OR

(ii) A police officer not below rank of officer in charge of a police station (SHO)
within whose jurisdiction warrant is to be executed

Such Magistrate or police officer shall endorse his name on the warrant

The endorsement is sufficient authority for the police officer to execute the warrant

Local police shall assist if required

Exception - no endorsement needed: If there is reason to believe that delay caused by obtaining endorsement will prevent execution, the police officer may execute without endorsement in any place beyond local jurisdiction

Illustration:
Delhi Police Officer A has a warrant for X who is in Jaipur. A takes the warrant to the SHO of Jaipur City Police Station, who endorses it. A can now execute the warrant in Jaipur with local police assistance. If X is about to leave India in 2 hours, A may skip the endorsement and execute immediately.

BNSS SECTION 82 - PROCEDURE ON ARREST OF PERSON AGAINST WHOM WARRANT ISSUED
Core Content:
When a warrant of arrest is executed outside the district in which it was issued, the person arrested shall, unless the issuing Court is within thirty kilometres or nearer than the Executive Magistrate/SP/Commissioner, or unless security is taken, be taken before such Magistrate/SP/Commissioner. The police officer shall forthwith give information of such arrest to the designated police officer in the district and to an officer in the district where the arrested person normally resides.

Procedure: Post-Arrest in Another District

Warrant executed outside the district where it was issued

The arrested person shall be taken before the Executive Magistrate, District Superintendent of Police, or Commissioner of Police within whose jurisdiction the arrest was made, UNLESS:

(i) The issuing Court is within 30 kilometres of the place of arrest, OR

(ii) The issuing Court is nearer than the Magistrate/SP/Commissioner, OR

(iii) Security is taken under section 73

The police officer shall forthwith give information of such arrest and place of holding to:

(i) The designated police officer in the district, AND

(ii) An officer of another district where the arrested person normally resides

Illustration:
Delhi Court issues warrant for X. X is arrested in Agra, 200 km away. The Delhi Court is not within 30 km. The arresting officer takes X before the Agra District Magistrate. The officer also informs the designated police officer in Delhi (where warrant was issued) and the officer in X's home district of Jaipur.

BNSS SECTION 83 - PROCEDURE BY MAGISTRATE BEFORE WHOM SUCH PERSON ARRESTED IS BROUGHT
Core Content:
The Executive Magistrate or SP/Commissioner before whom a person arrested outside the issuing district is brought shall direct his removal in custody to the issuing Court if he appears to be the person intended. For bailable offences or if bail is endorsed on the warrant, he may take bail bond and forward it. For non-bailable offences, the Chief Judicial Magistrate or Sessions Judge of the district may release him on bail.

Procedure: Handling by Receiving Magistrate/SP

Person arrested appears to be the person intended by the issuing Court

The Executive Magistrate/SP/Commissioner shall direct his removal in custody to the issuing Court, UNLESS:

If offence is bailable: and person is ready to give bail bond to satisfaction of Magistrate/SP/Commissioner → take bail bond and forward to issuing Court

If bail is endorsed on warrant under section 73: and person is ready to give required security → take security and forward bond to issuing Court

If offence is non-bailable: Chief Judicial Magistrate or Sessions Judge of the district where arrest is made may release person on bail after considering information and documents under section 80(2)

Illustration:
X is arrested in Agra on warrant from Delhi. The offence is bailable. X arranges surety. The Agra Magistrate takes bail bond from X and forwards it to Delhi Court, then sends X to Delhi. If the offence is non-bailable, X can apply to the Agra Chief Judicial Magistrate for bail.

BNSS SECTION 84 - PROCLAMATION FOR PERSON ABSCONDING
Core Content:
If any Court has reason to believe that any person against whom a warrant has been issued has absconded or is concealing himself, it may publish a written proclamation requiring him to appear at a specified place and time not less than thirty days from the date of publishing such proclamation. For offences punishable with 10+ years, life imprisonment, or death, if the person fails to appear, the Court may pronounce him a proclaimed offender.

Procedure: Proclamation and Proclaimed Offender

Court has reason to believe person against whom warrant issued has absconded or is concealing himself

Court may publish written proclamation requiring him to appear at specified place and time

Time specified shall be not less than 30 days from date of publishing proclamation

Proclamation shall be published as:

(i)(a) Publicly read in conspicuous place of town/village where he ordinarily resides

(i)(b) Affixed to conspicuous part of his house/homestead or conspicuous place of town/village

(i)(c) Copy affixed to conspicuous part of Court-house

(ii) Court may also direct copy to be published in a daily newspaper circulating in that place

A statement in writing by the Court that proclamation was duly published on a specified day shall be conclusive evidence of compliance

For offences punishable with 10+ years, life imprisonment, or death: if person fails to appear at specified time and place, Court may after inquiry pronounce him a proclaimed offender and make declaration to that effect

Illustration:
Warrant issued against X for murder (punishable with death). X cannot be found. Court issues a proclamation requiring X to appear within 30 days.
