Time limit for inquiry: Inquiry under this section shall be completed within a period of six months from date of its commencement

Automatic termination: If inquiry is not so completed, proceedings shall on expiry of said period stand terminated, unless for special reasons recorded in writing, Magistrate otherwise directs

Detention limit: Where any person has been kept in detention pending such inquiry, proceedings against that person shall stand terminated on expiry of a period of six months of such detention (unless terminated earlier)

Sessions Judge intervention: Where direction is made permitting continuance of proceedings, Sessions Judge may on application by aggrieved party vacate such direction if satisfied it was not based on any special reason or was perverse

Illustration:
Magistrate initiates inquiry against X for likely breach of peace. Inquiry must be completed within 6 months. If not completed, proceedings automatically terminate. X is in jail pending inquiry - after 6 months in detention, proceedings automatically terminate even if inquiry not complete, unless Magistrate records special reasons for extension.

BNSS SECTION 136 - ORDER TO GIVE SECURITY
Core Content:
If upon inquiry it is proved that it is necessary for keeping the peace or maintaining good behaviour that the person should execute a bond or bail bond, the Magistrate shall make an order accordingly. The security shall not be of a nature different from, or amount larger than, or period longer than that specified in the order under section 130.

Procedure: Final Security Order

Upon inquiry under section 135, it is proved that it is necessary for keeping the peace or maintaining good behaviour that the person should execute a bond or bail bond

Magistrate shall make an order accordingly

Limitations:

(a) No person shall be ordered to give security of a nature different from that specified in order under section 130

(b) No person shall be ordered to give security of an amount larger than that specified in order under section 130

(c) No person shall be ordered to give security for a period longer than that specified in order under section 130

Amount of every bond or bail bond shall be fixed with due regard to circumstances of case and shall not be excessive

When the person is a child, the bond shall be executed only by his sureties

Illustration:
After inquiry, Magistrate finds it necessary for X to give security for keeping peace. The original section 130 order specified bond of ₹10,000 with one surety for 6 months. Magistrate cannot order ₹20,000 or two sureties or 1 year - must stick to what was specified in the show cause order.

BNSS SECTION 137 - DISCHARGE OF PERSON INFORMED AGAINST
Core Content:
If on an inquiry under section 135 it is not proved that it is necessary for keeping the peace or maintaining good behaviour that the person should execute a bond, the Magistrate shall make an entry on the record to that effect, and if such person is in custody only for the purposes of the inquiry, shall release him, or if not in custody, shall discharge him.

Procedure: Discharge

Inquiry under section 135 completed

It is not proved that it is necessary for keeping the peace or maintaining good behaviour that the person should execute a bond

Magistrate shall make an entry on the record to that effect

If person is in custody only for purposes of the inquiry: Magistrate shall release him

If person is not in custody: Magistrate shall discharge him

Illustration:
Magistrate conducted inquiry against X for allegedly planning to cause breach of peace. The evidence showed X had no such intention. Magistrate records: "No sufficient grounds found." X was in jail pending inquiry. Magistrate orders X's immediate release.

BNSS SECTION 138 - COMMENCEMENT OF PERIOD FOR WHICH SECURITY IS REQUIRED
Core Content:
If the person ordered to give security is at the time of the order sentenced to or undergoing imprisonment, the period for which security is required shall commence on expiration of such sentence. In other cases, such period shall commence on the date of such order unless the Magistrate fixes a later date for sufficient reason.

Procedure: Commencement Date

Person ordered to give security under section 125 or 136

If undergoing imprisonment: Period for which security is required shall commence on the expiration of such sentence

In other cases: Period shall commence on the date of such order, unless Magistrate for sufficient reason fixes a later date

Illustration:
X is sentenced to 1 year imprisonment and also ordered to give security for 2 years under section 125. The 2-year security period starts after X completes the 1-year sentence. Y is not in jail; Magistrate orders security for 6 months starting from next month because Y is currently out of town.

BNSS SECTION 139 - CONTENTS OF BOND
Core Content:
The bond or bail bond to be executed by any such person shall bind him to keep the peace or to be of good behaviour, as the case may be. In the latter case, the commission or attempt to commit, or the abetment of, any offence punishable with imprisonment, wherever it may be committed, is a breach of the bond or bail bond.

Procedure: Bond Conditions

Bond or bail bond shall bind the person to:

(i) Keep the peace, OR

(ii) Be of good behaviour (as the case may be)

For good behaviour bond: commission or attempt to commit or abetment of any offence punishable with imprisonment, wherever it may be committed, shall be a breach of the bond

Illustration:
X executes a good behaviour bond. Even if X commits a minor imprisonable offence in another city or another country, that constitutes a breach of the bond. The bond is not limited to the local jurisdiction.

BNSS SECTION 140 - POWER TO REJECT SURETIES
Core Content:
A Magistrate may refuse to accept any surety offered, or may reject any surety previously accepted, on the ground that such surety is an unfit person. Before doing so, he shall hold an inquiry on oath into the fitness of the surety, give reasonable notice to the surety and the person who offered him, and record the substance of evidence.

Procedure: Rejecting Sureties

Magistrate may refuse to accept any surety offered, or reject any surety previously accepted

Ground: such surety is an unfit person for purposes of the bail bond

Mandatory preconditions before refusal/rejection:

(i) Magistrate shall either himself hold an inquiry on oath into the fitness of the surety, OR cause such inquiry to be held and report made by a subordinate Magistrate

(ii) Magistrate shall give reasonable notice to the surety and to the person by whom the surety was offered

(iii) Magistrate shall, in making the inquiry, record the substance of the evidence adduced before him

If Magistrate is satisfied that the surety is an unfit person, he shall make an order refusing to accept or rejecting the surety, recording his reasons

Before rejecting a surety previously accepted, Magistrate shall issue summons or warrant and cause the person for whom the surety is bound to appear or be brought before him

Illustration:
X offers Y as surety. Magistrate suspects Y is a known criminal with pending cases. Magistrate gives notice to Y and X, holds an inquiry, takes evidence, records that Y has three pending theft cases. Magistrate orders rejection of Y as surety, recording reasons, and summons X to appear to arrange another surety.

BNSS SECTION 141 - IMPRISONMENT IN DEFAULT OF SECURITY
Core Content:
If any person ordered to give security does not give such security on or before the date on which the period commences, he shall be committed to prison or detained until the period expires or until he gives security. Imprisonment for failure to give security for keeping peace shall be simple. For good behaviour, it may be rigorous or simple as the Court directs.

Procedure: Imprisonment for Default

Person ordered to give security under section 125 or 136 does not give such security on or before the date on which period commences

He shall be committed to prison (or if already in prison, detained) until:

(i) The period expires, OR

(ii) Within such period he gives the security to the Court or Magistrate who made the order

Breach of bond: If person after executing bond for keeping peace is proved to have committed breach, Magistrate or successor may order arrest and detention in prison until expiry of bond period (without prejudice to any other punishment or forfeiture)

For security period exceeding one year: If person does not give security, Magistrate shall issue warrant directing him to be detained pending orders of Sessions Judge, and proceedings shall be laid before such Court

Sessions Court after examining proceedings and giving reasonable opportunity of being heard may pass such order as it thinks fit

Maximum imprisonment for failure to give security shall not exceed three years

Imprisonment for failure to give security for keeping the peace shall be simple

Imprisonment for failure to give security for good behaviour shall be:

For proceedings under section 127 (disseminating matters): simple

For proceedings under section 128 (suspected persons) or section 129 (habitual offenders): rigorous or simple as Court directs

Illustration:
X is ordered to give security for keeping peace for 2 years but fails to provide bond. Magistrate sends X to prison for simple imprisonment until he provides security or 2 years pass. Y is a habitual offender under section 129 who fails to give good behaviour security. Court may sentence Y to rigorous imprisonment for default.

BNSS SECTION 142 - POWER TO RELEASE PERSONS IMPRISONED FOR FAILING TO GIVE SECURITY
Core Content:
The District Magistrate (for orders by Executive Magistrate under section 136) or Chief Judicial Magistrate (for other cases) may order discharge of any person imprisoned for failing to give security if of opinion that he may be released without hazard to the community. They may also reduce the amount of security, number of sureties, or time period. The High Court or Court of Session may cancel any bond for keeping peace or good behaviour.

Procedure: Release and Modification

Discharge power:

District Magistrate (for order passed by Executive Magistrate under section 136)

Chief Judicial Magistrate (for any other case)

May order any person imprisoned for failing to give security to be discharged if of opinion he may be released without hazard to community or to any other person

Reduction power:

High Court or Court of Session, OR

District Magistrate (for Executive Magistrate orders under section 136), OR

Chief Judicial Magistrate (for other cases)

May reduce the amount of security, number of sureties, or time for which security has been required

Conditional discharge: Order under sub-section (1) may direct discharge without conditions or upon any conditions which such person accepts. Conditions cease when period for which security was required has expired

Cancellation of bond: High Court or Court of Session may at any time for sufficient reasons recorded in writing cancel any bond for keeping peace or good behaviour. District Magistrate (for Executive Magistrate orders under section 136) or Chief Judicial Magistrate (for other cases) may make such cancellation where bond was executed under his order or under order of any other Court in his district

Surety application to cancel bond: Any surety may at any time apply to the Court making the order to cancel the bond. Court shall issue summons or warrant requiring the person for whom surety is bound to appear or be brought before it

Illustration:
X has been in prison for 4 months for failing to give security. District Magistrate reviews and finds X's health is failing and he poses no threat. DM orders X's conditional discharge on condition X reports to police weekly. Alternatively, the High Court may cancel X's bond entirely if new evidence shows X was innocent.

BNSS SECTION 143 - SECURITY FOR UNEXPIRED PERIOD OF BOND
Core Content:
When a person appears or is brought before the Magistrate or Court pursuant to summons/warrant issued under proviso to section 140(3) or section 142(10), the Magistrate or Court shall cancel the bond or bail bond executed by such person and shall order such person to give, for the unexpired portion of the term of such bond, fresh security of the same description as the original security.

Procedure: Fresh Security for Unexpired Period

Person appears or is brought before Magistrate or Court pursuant to:

Summons/warrant issued under proviso to section 140(3) (before rejecting previously accepted surety), OR

Summons/warrant issued under section 142(10) (surety applies to cancel bond)

Magistrate or Court shall:

(i) Cancel the bond or bail bond executed by such person

(ii) Order such person to give, for the unexpired portion of the term of such bond, fresh security of the same description as the original security

Every such order shall, for purposes of sections 139 to 142, be deemed to be an order made under section 125 or section 136, as the case may be

Illustration:
X executed a 2-year good behaviour bond. After 1 year, the surety applies to cancel the bond. Court summons X, cancels the original bond, and orders X to give fresh security for the remaining 1 year with a new surety. The same rules (imprisonment for default, etc.) apply to this fresh security order.

BNSS SECTION 144 - ORDER FOR MAINTENANCE OF WIVES, CHILDREN AND PARENTS
Core Content:
If any person having sufficient means neglects or refuses to maintain his wife unable to maintain herself, his legitimate or illegitimate child unable to maintain itself, his legitimate or illegitimate child (not being a married daughter) who has attained majority but is unable to maintain itself due to physical or mental abnormality or injury, or his father or mother unable to maintain himself/herself, a Magistrate of first class may order such person to make a monthly allowance for maintenance at such monthly rate as the Magistrate thinks fit.

Procedure: Maintenance Application

Jurisdiction: Magistrate of first class

Applicant must prove:

(i) The person has sufficient means

(ii) The person neglects or refuses to maintain

(iii) The claimant falls under one of four categories:

(a) Wife unable to maintain herself

(b) Legitimate or illegitimate child (whether married or not) unable to maintain itself

(c) Legitimate or illegitimate child (not being a married daughter) who has attained majority, but by reason of physical or mental abnormality or injury unable to maintain itself

(d) Father or mother unable to maintain himself/herself

Court may order monthly allowance at such monthly rate as Magistrate thinks fit

Payment to be made to such person as Magistrate may from time to time direct

Special provision for female child: Magistrate may order father of female child under clause (b) to make allowance until she attains majority, if Magistrate is satisfied that her husband (if married) is not possessed of sufficient means

Interim maintenance (Second Proviso): During pendency of proceeding, Magistrate may order:

(i) Monthly allowance for interim maintenance of wife, child, father, or mother

(ii) Expenses of such proceeding which Magistrate considers reasonable

Payment to be made to such person as Magistrate directs

Time limit for interim application (Third Proviso): Application for interim maintenance and expenses shall, as far as possible, be disposed of within sixty days from the date of service of notice of the application to such person

"Wife" includes a woman who has been divorced by, or has obtained a divorce from, her husband and has not remarried

Maintenance/interim maintenance payable from date of order, or if so ordered, from date of application

Enforcement: If person fails without sufficient cause to comply, Magistrate may:

Issue warrant for levying amount due as fines

Sentence such person, for whole or any part of each month's allowance remaining unpaid after execution of warrant, to imprisonment for term which may extend to one month or until payment if sooner made

Limitation for recovery application: No warrant shall be issued unless application made within one year from date on which amount became due

Wife's refusal to live with husband: If husband offers to maintain wife on condition of her living with him, and she refuses, Magistrate may consider any grounds of refusal stated by her, and may make order notwithstanding such offer if satisfied there is just ground for refusal

Just ground: If husband has contracted marriage with another woman or keeps a mistress, it shall be considered just ground for wife's refusal to live with him

Wife not entitled to maintenance if:

She is living in adultery, OR

Without sufficient reason she refuses to live with her husband, OR

They are living separately by mutual consent

Cancellation of order: On proof that wife in whose favour order was made is living in adultery, or without sufficient reason refuses to live with husband, or living separately by mutual consent, Magistrate shall cancel the order

Illustration:
X earns ₹50,000 per month but refuses to maintain his elderly mother who cannot work. Mother applies to Magistrate under section 144. Magistrate orders X to pay ₹10,000 per month as maintenance. During the proceeding, Magistrate also orders interim maintenance of ₹5,000 per month pending final order, to be disposed of within 60 days. X fails to pay - Magistrate issues warrant and sentences X to 15 days imprisonment for each month's default.

BNSS SECTION 145 - PROCEDURE
Core Content:
Proceedings under section 144 may be taken against any person in any district where he is, where he or his wife resides, where he last resided with his wife or with the mother of the illegitimate child, or where his father or mother resides. Evidence shall be taken in presence of the person against whom order is proposed, recorded in manner prescribed for summons-cases. If the person is wilfully avoiding service or neglecting to attend, Magistrate may proceed ex parte.

Procedure: Venue and Evidence

Proceedings may be taken against any person in any district:

(a) Where he is

(b) Where he or his wife resides

(c) Where he last resided with his wife, or as the case may be, with the mother of the illegitimate child

(d) Where his father or mother resides

All evidence shall be taken in the presence of the person against whom order for payment of maintenance is proposed to be made

If personal attendance is dispensed with, evidence shall be taken in presence of his advocate

Evidence shall be recorded in the manner prescribed for summons-cases

Ex parte proceeding: If Magistrate is satisfied that the person against whom order is proposed is:

(i) Wilfully avoiding service, OR

(ii) Wilfully neglecting to attend the Court
→ Magistrate may proceed to hear and determine the case ex parte

Setting aside ex parte order: Any ex parte order may be set aside for good cause shown on an application made within three months from date thereof, subject to such terms including terms as to payment of costs to the opposite party as Magistrate may think just and proper

Court may make such order as to costs as may be just

Illustration:
X's wife files maintenance application. X has moved to a different city. Wife can file in the district where X currently lives, or where she resides, or where they last lived together. X avoids accepting summons. Magistrate is satisfied of wilful avoidance, proceeds ex parte, and orders maintenance. X appears after 2 months showing he was hospitalized - Court sets aside ex parte order on payment of wife's costs.

BNSS SECTION 146 - ALTERATION IN ALLOWANCE
Core Content:
On proof of change in circumstances of any person receiving monthly allowance or ordered to pay monthly allowance, the Magistrate may make such alteration as he thinks fit in the allowance. If a competent Civil Court decision requires cancellation or variation of an order under section 144, the Magistrate shall cancel or vary accordingly. For divorced women, if she remarries, receives customary/ personal law sum on divorce, or voluntarily surrenders rights to maintenance, the Magistrate shall cancel the order.

Procedure: Modification of Maintenance Order

Change in circumstances: On proof of change in circumstances of any person:

(i) Receiving monthly allowance for maintenance or interim maintenance, OR

(ii) Ordered to pay monthly allowance for maintenance or interim maintenance to wife, child, father, or mother
→ Magistrate may make such alteration as he thinks fit in the allowance for maintenance or interim maintenance

Effect of Civil Court decision: Where it appears to Magistrate that in consequence of any decision of a competent Civil Court, any order made under section 144 should be cancelled or varied, he shall cancel or vary the same accordingly

Cancellation for divorced women: Where any order has been made under section 144 in favour of a woman who has been divorced by, or has obtained a divorce from, her husband, the Magistrate shall cancel such order if satisfied that:

(a) The woman has, after the date of such divorce, remarried → cancel from date of remarriage

(b) The woman has been divorced by her husband and has received (whether before or after the date of the order) the whole of the sum which under any customary or personal law was payable on such divorce → cancel:

(i) If sum paid before such order: from date on which order was made

(ii) In any other case: from date of expiry of period for which maintenance has been actually paid by husband to woman

(c) The woman has obtained a divorce from her husband and had voluntarily surrendered her rights to maintenance or interim maintenance after her divorce → cancel from date thereof

Civil Court credit for maintenance paid: At time of making any decree for recovery of maintenance or dowry by any person to whom monthly allowance for maintenance and interim maintenance has been ordered to be paid under section 144, the Civil Court shall take into account the sum which has been paid to, or recovered by, such person as monthly allowance for maintenance and interim maintenance in pursuance of the said order

Illustration:
X was ordered to pay ₹10,000/month maintenance to wife. X loses his job. Magistrate reduces maintenance to ₹3,000/month based on change in circumstances. Later, wife remarries. Magistrate cancels maintenance order from date of remarriage. Wife later files civil suit for recovery of more maintenance - Civil Court deducts amounts already paid under Magistrate's order.

BNSS SECTION 147 - ENFORCEMENT OF ORDER OF MAINTENANCE
Core Content:
A copy of the order of maintenance or interim maintenance and expenses of proceedings shall be given without payment to the person in whose favour it is made, or to his guardian, or to the person to whom the allowance is to be paid. Such order may be enforced by any Magistrate in any place where the person against whom it is made may be, on being satisfied as to identity of parties and non-payment.

Procedure: Cross-Jurisdictional Enforcement

Free copy of order: A copy of the order of maintenance or interim maintenance and expenses of proceedings shall be given without payment to:

(i) The person in whose favour it is made, OR

(ii) His guardian (if any), OR

(iii) The person to whom the allowance for maintenance or allowance for interim maintenance and expenses of proceeding is to be paid

Enforcement anywhere in India: Such order may be enforced by any Magistrate in any place where the person against whom it is made may be

Conditions for enforcement: The enforcing Magistrate must be satisfied as to:

(i) Identity of the parties

(ii) Non-payment of the allowance or expenses due

Illustration:
Delhi Court orders X to pay maintenance to his wife. X moves to Mumbai and stops paying. Wife takes the maintenance order copy to a Magistrate in Mumbai. The Mumbai Magistrate verifies wife's identity, X's identity, and that payment is due. The Mumbai Magistrate then enforces the order against X in Mumbai - no need to go back to Delhi Court.

BNSS SECTION 148 - DISPERSAL OF ASSEMBLY BY USE OF CIVIL FORCE
Core Content:
Any Executive Magistrate or officer in charge of a police station or any police officer not below the rank of sub-inspector may command any unlawful assembly or any assembly of five or more persons likely to cause disturbance of public peace to disperse. If the assembly does not disperse, the Magistrate or police officer may proceed to disperse such assembly by force and may require assistance of any person (not being armed forces member) for that purpose.

Procedure: Dispersal of Unlawful Assembly

Executive Magistrate OR officer in charge of police station OR any police officer not below rank of sub-inspector may command:

(i) Any unlawful assembly, OR

(ii) Any assembly of five or more persons likely to cause a disturbance of the public peace
→ to disperse

It shall be the duty of the members of such assembly to disperse accordingly

If upon being commanded, such assembly does not disperse, OR without being commanded it conducts itself in such manner as to show determination not to disperse:

The Executive Magistrate or police officer may proceed to disperse such assembly by force

May require the assistance of any person (not being an officer or member of armed forces acting as such) for the purpose of dispersing such assembly

If necessary, arrest and confine the persons who form part of it, in order to disperse such assembly or that they may be punished according to law

Illustration:
Five or more persons gather outside a government office, shouting slogans and blocking the entrance, likely to cause disturbance. The SHO commands them to disperse. They refuse. The SHO uses police force to disperse the crowd and arrests the leaders.

BNSS SECTION 149 - USE OF ARMED FORCES TO DISPERSE ASSEMBLY
Core Content:
If any assembly referred to in section 148(1) cannot otherwise be dispersed and it is necessary for public security that it should be dispersed, the District Magistrate or any other Executive Magistrate authorised by him who is present may cause it to be dispersed by the armed forces. The Magistrate may require any officer in command of armed forces to disperse the assembly and arrest and confine persons. The officer shall obey using as little force and doing as little injury as possible.

Procedure: Armed Forces Dispersal

Assembly under section 148(1) cannot otherwise be dispersed

It is necessary for public security that it should be dispersed

District Magistrate OR any other Executive Magistrate authorised by him who is present may cause it to be dispersed by the armed forces

Such Magistrate may require any officer in command of any group of persons belonging to the armed forces to:

(i) Disperse the assembly with the help of armed forces under his command

(ii) Arrest and confine such persons forming part of it as the Executive Magistrate may direct, or as it may be necessary to arrest and confine in order to disperse the assembly or to have them punished according to law

Every such officer of the armed forces shall obey such requisition in such manner as he thinks fit

While doing so, he shall use as little force, and do as little injury to person and property, as may be consistent with:

(i) Dispersing the assembly, and

(ii) Arresting and detaining such persons

Illustration:
A mob of 5000 people is rioting, police force is overwhelmed and cannot disperse them. The District Magistrate authorises the Army to intervene. The Army officer uses minimum necessary force to disperse the mob and arrest the instigators.

BNSS SECTION 150 - POWER OF CERTAIN ARMED FORCE OFFICERS TO DISPERSE ASSEMBLY
Core Content:
When public security is manifestly endangered by any such assembly and no Executive Magistrate can be communicated with, any commissioned or gazetted officer of the armed forces may disperse such assembly with the help of armed forces under his command, and may arrest and confine any persons forming part of it. If it becomes practicable to communicate with an Executive Magistrate, he shall do so and obey the Magistrate's instructions.

Procedure: Emergency Dispersal by Armed Forces

Public security is manifestly endangered by any such assembly

No Executive Magistrate can be communicated with

Any commissioned or gazetted officer of the armed forces may disperse such assembly with the help of armed forces under his command

He may arrest and confine any persons forming part of it, in order to:

(i) Disperse such assembly, OR

(ii) That they may be punished according to law

If while acting under this section, it becomes practicable for him to communicate with an Executive Magistrate, he shall do so

He shall thenceforward obey the instructions of the Magistrate as to whether he shall or shall not continue such action

Illustration:
A violent mob attacks an army convoy in a remote area. No Executive Magistrate can be reached by phone or radio. A commissioned Army officer orders his troops to disperse the mob using necessary force and arrests the attackers. Once contact with the District Magistrate is established, the officer follows the Magistrate's further instructions.

BNSS SECTION 151 - PROTECTION AGAINST PROSECUTION FOR ACTS DONE UNDER SECTIONS 148, 149 AND 150
Core Content:
No prosecution shall be instituted against any person for any act purporting to be done under sections 148, 149, or 150 except with sanction of Central Government (for armed forces members) or State Government (for other cases). Executive Magistrates, police officers, armed forces officers and members acting in good faith, and persons acting in compliance with requisition in good faith shall not be deemed to have committed an offence.

Procedure: Protection from Prosecution

Sanction requirement for prosecution: No prosecution against any person for any act purporting to be done under section 148, 149, or 150 shall be instituted in any Criminal Court except:

(a) With sanction of Central Government where such person is an officer or member of the armed forces

(b) With sanction of State Government in any other case

Good faith protection: The following shall not be deemed to have committed an offence:

(a) No Executive Magistrate or police officer acting under any of the said sections in good faith

(b) No person doing any act in good faith in compliance with a requisition under section 148 or 149

(c) No officer of the armed forces acting under section 150 in good faith

(d) No member of the armed forces doing any act in obedience to any order which he was bound to obey

Definitions for this Chapter:

(a) "armed forces" means army, naval and air forces operating as land forces, and includes any other armed forces of the Union so operating

(b) "officer" in relation to armed forces means a person commissioned, gazetted or in pay as an officer, and includes junior commissioned officer, warrant officer, petty officer, non-commissioned officer, and non-gazetted officer

(c) "member" in relation to armed forces means a person in the armed forces other than an officer

Illustration:
An Army officer acting in good faith under section 150 disperses a violent mob using force. A person injured in the dispersal wants to sue the officer. No court can take cognizance without Central Government sanction. If the officer acted in good faith, he is deemed not to have committed any offence.

BNSS SECTION 152 - CONDITIONAL ORDER FOR REMOVAL OF NUISANCE
Core Content:
Whenever a District Magistrate, Sub-divisional Magistrate, or any other Executive Magistrate specially empowered by State Government considers that any unlawful obstruction/nuisance should be removed from any public place/way/river/channel, or any trade/occupation is injurious to health/physical comfort of community, or any building/tent/structure/tree is in dangerous condition, or any tank/well/excavation needs fencing, or any dangerous animal should be destroyed/confined, the Magistrate may make a conditional order requiring the person concerned to remove the nuisance, desist from the trade, repair the building, fence the excavation, or destroy the animal, or to appear and show cause.

Procedure: Conditional Order for Nuisance Removal

Magistrate (District, Sub-divisional, or other Executive Magistrate specially empowered by State Government) on receiving police report or other information and taking such evidence as he thinks fit considers that:

(a) Any unlawful obstruction or nuisance should be removed from any public place or from any way, river or channel which is or may be lawfully used by the public, OR

(b) The conduct of any trade or occupation, or keeping of any goods/merchandise, is injurious to health or physical comfort of the community, and in consequence such trade/occupation should be prohibited or regulated or such goods removed or regulated, OR

(c) Construction of any building or disposal of any substance likely to occasion conflagration or explosion should be prevented or stopped, OR

(d) Any building, tent, structure, or tree is in such condition that it is likely to fall and cause injury to persons living/carrying on business in neighbourhood or passing by, and in consequence removal/repair/support is necessary, OR

(e) Any tank, well or excavation adjacent to any such way or public place should be fenced to prevent danger to public, OR

(f) Any dangerous animal should be destroyed, confined or otherwise disposed of

Magistrate may make a conditional order requiring the person causing such obstruction/nuisance, or carrying on such trade/occupation, or keeping such goods, or owning/possessing/controlling such building/tent/structure/substance/tank/well/excavation, or owning/possessing such animal/tree, within a time to be fixed in the order:

(i) To remove such obstruction or nuisance

(ii) To desist from carrying on, or to remove or regulate such trade/occupation, or to remove such goods or regulate keeping thereof

(iii) To prevent or stop construction of such building, or to alter disposal of such substance

(iv) To remove, repair or support such building, tent or structure, or to remove or support such trees

(v) To fence such tank, well or excavation

(vi) To destroy, confine or dispose of such dangerous animal as provided in the order

OR, if he objects so to do, to appear before himself or some other Executive Magistrate subordinate to him at a time and place fixed and show cause why order should not be made absolute

No order duly made by Magistrate under this section shall be called in question in any Civil Court

"Public place" includes property belonging to State, camping grounds, and grounds left unoccupied for sanitary or recreative purposes

Illustration:
A building is leaning dangerously and likely to fall on pedestrians. The District Magistrate issues a conditional order to the owner: "Repair or demolish this building within 15 days, or appear before me on date X to show cause why this order should not be made absolute." Owner can either comply or appear and argue.

BNSS SECTION 153 - SERVICE OR NOTIFICATION OF ORDER
Core Content:
The order shall, if practicable, be served on the person against whom it is made in the manner provided for service of summons. If such order cannot be so served, it shall be notified by proclamation published in such manner as State Government rules direct, and a copy shall be stuck up at such place or places as may be fittest for conveying the information to such person.

Procedure: Service of Nuisance Order

Order shall, if practicable, be served on the person against whom it is made in the manner provided for service of summons (as per Chapter VI)

If such order cannot be so served, it shall be notified by proclamation published in such manner as the State Government may, by rules, direct

A copy thereof shall be stuck up at such place or places as may be fittest for conveying the information to such person

Illustration:
The owner of the dangerous building cannot be found. The Magistrate orders a proclamation to be published in the local newspaper and a copy of the order to be affixed to the building itself. This is deemed sufficient notice to the owner.

BNSS SECTION 154 - PERSON TO WHOM ORDER IS ADDRESSED TO OBEY OR SHOW CAUSE
Core Content:
The person against whom such order is made shall perform, within the time and in the manner specified in the order, the act directed thereby, or appear and show cause against the order.

Procedure: Compliance or Show Cause

Person against whom order is made shall either:

(a) Perform, within the time and in the manner specified in the order, the act directed thereby, OR

(b) Appear and show cause against the order

Illustration:
Owner receives conditional order to repair dangerous building within 15 days. He can either hire a contractor and repair it within 15 days, OR appear in Court on the specified date to argue why the order should not be enforced.

BNSS SECTION 155 - PENALTY FOR FAILURE TO COMPLY WITH SECTION 154
Core Content:
If the person against whom an order is made under section 154 does not perform such act or appear and show cause, he shall be liable to the penalty specified in BNS section 223 (disobedience to order lawfully promulgated by public servant), and the order shall be made absolute.

Procedure: Default Consequences

Person against whom order is made under section 154:

(i) Does not perform the act directed, AND

(ii) Does not appear and show cause

He shall be liable to the penalty specified in BNS section 223 (disobedience to order lawfully promulgated by public servant)

The conditional order shall be made absolute

Illustration:
Owner ignores the conditional order. He neither repairs the building nor appears in Court. The Magistrate makes the conditional order absolute, meaning it becomes final and enforceable. The owner is also liable for punishment under BNS section 223.

BNSS SECTION 156 - PROCEDURE WHERE EXISTENCE OF PUBLIC RIGHT IS DENIED
Core Content:
Where an order is made under section 152 for preventing obstruction, nuisance or danger to the public in use of any way, river, channel or place, the Magistrate shall question the person who appears whether he denies existence of any public right in respect of such place. If he does, the Magistrate shall inquire into the matter. If reliable evidence supports denial, he shall stay proceedings until the matter is decided by a competent Court. If no such evidence, he shall proceed under section 157.

Procedure: Public Right Denial

Order made under section 152 for preventing obstruction, nuisance or danger to the public in use of any way, river, channel or place

Person against whom order was made appears before Magistrate

Magistrate shall question him as to whether he denies the existence of any public right in respect of the way, river, channel or place

If he does deny, Magistrate shall, before proceeding under section 157, inquire into the matter

If Magistrate finds reliable evidence in support of such denial: He shall stay the proceedings until the matter of existence of such right has been decided by a competent Court

If Magistrate finds no such evidence: He shall proceed as laid down in section 157

Estoppel: A person who has on being questioned failed to deny existence of public right, or who having made such denial has failed to adduce reliable evidence in support thereof, shall not in subsequent proceedings be permitted to make any such denial

Illustration:
Magistrate orders removal of obstruction from a road. Owner claims the road is private, not public. Magistrate inquires and finds registered documents showing it's a public road - no reliable evidence for denial. Magistrate proceeds under section 157. If owner had produced a court decree showing it's private, Magistrate would stay proceedings for civil court to decide.

BNSS SECTION 157 - PROCEDURE WHERE PERSON AGAINST WHOM ORDER IS MADE UNDER SECTION 152 APPEARS TO SHOW CAUSE
Core Content:
If the person appears and shows cause, the Magistrate shall take evidence as in a summons-case. If satisfied the order is reasonable and proper, it shall be made absolute (with or without modification). If not satisfied, no further proceedings shall be taken. Proceedings shall be completed as soon as possible within ninety days, extendable to one hundred and twenty days for reasons recorded in writing.

Procedure: Show Cause Hearing

Person against whom order under section 152 is made appears and shows cause against the order

Magistrate shall take evidence in the matter as in a summons-case

If Magistrate satisfied that the order (either as originally made or subject to such modification as he considers necessary) is reasonable and proper:

Order shall be made absolute without modification, OR as the case may be, with such modification

If Magistrate is not so satisfied: No further proceedings shall be taken in the case

Time limit: Proceedings under this section shall be completed, as soon as possible, within a period of ninety days, which may be extended for reasons to be recorded in writing, to one hundred and twenty days

Illustration:
Owner appears and shows cause that the building is not dangerous - he has an engineer's certificate. Magistrate takes evidence from both sides. After hearing, Magistrate is not satisfied the building is dangerous. Proceedings are dropped. If Magistrate is satisfied, he makes the order absolute, maybe giving extra time for repairs.

BNSS SECTION 158 - POWER OF MAGISTRATE TO DIRECT LOCAL INVESTIGATION AND EXAMINATION OF AN EXPERT
Core Content:
The Magistrate may, for the purposes of an inquiry under section 156 or section 157, direct a local investigation to be made by such person as he thinks fit, or summon and examine an expert.

Procedure: Local Investigation and Expert Evidence

Magistrate is conducting inquiry under section 156 (public right denial) or section 157 (show cause hearing)

Magistrate may:

(a) Direct a local investigation to be made by such person as he thinks fit, OR

(b) Summon and examine an expert

Illustration:
During inquiry into whether a building is dangerous, Magistrate orders a local investigation by a government engineer. The engineer inspects the building and submits a report. Magistrate also summons an independent structural expert to give opinion evidence.

BNSS SECTION 159 - POWER OF MAGISTRATE TO FURNISH WRITTEN INSTRUCTIONS, ETC.
Core Content:
Where the Magistrate directs a local investigation, he may furnish written instructions for guidance and declare by whom expenses shall be paid. The report of such person may be read as evidence. Where Magistrate summons and examines an expert, he may direct by whom costs shall be paid.

Procedure: Investigation Instructions and Costs

Magistrate directs local investigation by any person under section 158

Magistrate may:

(a) Furnish such person with such written instructions as may seem necessary for his guidance

(b) Declare by whom the whole or any part of the necessary expenses of the local investigation shall be paid

The report of such person may be read as evidence in the case

Where Magistrate summons and examines an expert under section 158, the Magistrate may direct by whom the costs of such summoning and examination shall be paid

Illustration:
Magistrate orders engineer to conduct local investigation, gives written instructions: "Check foundation cracks, measure tilt angle, photograph all damage." Magistrate declares that the owner shall pay the engineer's fees. The engineer's report is read as evidence. Expert witness costs are also directed to be paid by the owner.

BNSS SECTION 160 - PROCEDURE ON ORDER BEING MADE ABSOLUTE AND CONSEQUENCES OF DISOBEDIENCE
Core Content:
When an order has been made absolute, the Magistrate shall give notice to the person and require him to perform the act within the time fixed, informing him that disobedience will attract penalty under BNS section 223. If the act is not performed within the time fixed, the Magistrate may cause it to be performed and recover costs by sale of property of such person. No suit shall lie in respect of anything done in good faith under this section.

Procedure: Enforcement of Absolute Order

Order has been made absolute under section 155 or section 157

Magistrate shall give notice of the same to the person against whom the order was made

Magistrate shall further require him to perform the act directed by the order within the time to be fixed in the notice

Magistrate shall inform him that, in case of disobedience, he shall be liable to the penalty provided by BNS section 223

If such act is not performed within the time fixed, the Magistrate may cause it to be performed

Magistrate may recover the costs of performing it either by:

(i) Sale of any building, goods or other property removed by his order, OR

(ii) Distress and sale of any other movable property of such person within or without such Magistrate's local jurisdiction

If such other property is without such jurisdiction, the order shall authorise its attachment and sale when endorsed by the Magistrate within whose local jurisdiction the property to be attached is found

No suit shall lie in respect of anything done in good faith under this section

Illustration:
Order to demolish dangerous building is made absolute. Owner ignores it. Magistrate gets the building demolished by government contractors. The cost of demolition (₹2 lakh) is recovered by seizing and selling the owner's car parked nearby. Owner cannot sue the Magistrate for acting in good faith.

BNSS SECTION 161 - INJUNCTION PENDING INQUIRY
Core Content:
If a Magistrate making an order under section 152 considers that immediate measures should be taken to prevent imminent danger or injury of a serious kind to the public, he may issue an injunction to the person requiring him to take action to obviate or prevent such danger or injury pending determination of the matter. In default, the Magistrate may himself use such means as he thinks fit. No suit shall lie in respect of anything done in good faith under this section.

Procedure: Interim Injunction

Magistrate making order under section 152 considers that immediate measures should be taken to prevent imminent danger or injury of a serious kind to the public

Magistrate may issue such an injunction to the person against whom the order was made, as is required to obviate or prevent such danger or injury pending the determination of the matter

In default of such person forthwith obeying such injunction, the Magistrate may himself use, or cause to be used, such means as he thinks fit to obviate such danger or to prevent such injury

No suit shall lie in respect of anything done in good faith by a Magistrate under this section

Illustration:
Magistrate issues conditional order about a building that is about to collapse imminently. Pending the inquiry, Magistrate issues injunction: "Erect barricades around the building immediately to prevent pedestrians from being injured." Owner fails to comply. Magistrate sends police to erect barricades at owner's expense. No suit lies against Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 162 - MAGISTRATE MAY PROHIBIT REPETITION OR CONTINUANCE OF PUBLIC NUISANCE
Core Content:
A District Magistrate or Sub-divisional Magistrate, or any other Executive Magistrate or Deputy Commissioner of Police empowered by the State Government or the District Magistrate in this behalf, may order any person not to repeat or continue a public nuisance, as defined in the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023, or any special or local law.

Procedure: Prohibition Order

Magistrate (District Magistrate, Sub-divisional Magistrate, or any other Executive Magistrate or Deputy Commissioner of Police empowered by State Government or District Magistrate) has authority

May order any person not to repeat or continue a public nuisance

Public nuisance as defined in BNS, 2023 or any special or local law

Illustration:
A factory is emitting noxious fumes causing public nuisance. District Magistrate orders the factory owner: "You are prohibited from continuing this nuisance. Stop emissions immediately." If the owner continues, he violates this order.

BNSS SECTION 163 - POWER TO ISSUE ORDER IN URGENT CASES OF NUISANCE OR APPREHENDED DANGER
Core Content:
In cases where a District Magistrate, Sub-divisional Magistrate, or any other Executive Magistrate specially empowered by State Government has sufficient ground for proceeding under this section and immediate prevention or speedy remedy is desirable, such Magistrate may by written order direct any person to abstain from a certain act or to take certain order with respect to property, if such direction is likely to prevent obstruction, annoyance, injury, danger to human life/health/safety, disturbance of public tranquillity, riot, or affray.

Procedure: Urgent Order in Emergencies

Magistrate (District, Sub-divisional, or other Executive Magistrate specially empowered by State Government) has sufficient ground for proceeding under this section

Immediate prevention or speedy remedy is desirable

Magistrate may, by a written order stating the material facts of the case and served in the manner provided by section 153, direct any person to:

(i) Abstain from a certain act, OR

(ii) Take certain order with respect to certain property in his possession or under his management

Condition: such direction is likely to prevent, or tends to prevent, obstruction, annoyance or injury to any person lawfully employed, or danger to human life/health/safety, or disturbance of public tranquillity, or a riot, or an affray

Ex parte order: Order may, in cases of emergency or where circumstances do not admit of serving notice upon the person against whom order is directed, be passed ex parte

Order may be directed to a particular individual, or to persons residing in a particular place or area, or to the public generally when frequenting or visiting a particular place or area

Duration: No order under this section shall remain in force for more than two months from the making thereof

Extension by State Government: If State Government considers it necessary for preventing danger to human life/health/safety or for preventing a riot or affray, it may by notification direct that order shall remain in force for such further period not exceeding six months from date on which the order would have expired

Rescission/alteration: Any Magistrate (on own motion or application of aggrieved person) may rescind or alter any order made by himself or any Magistrate subordinate to him or his predecessor-in-office. State Government may rescind or alter any order made by it under the proviso

Hearing on application: On receiving application under sub-section (5) or (6), the Magistrate or State Government shall afford the applicant an early opportunity of appearing (in person or by advocate) and showing cause against the order. If application rejected wholly or in part, reasons shall be recorded in writing

Illustration:
Intelligence reports that a communal procession is planned for tomorrow which is likely to cause a riot. A Sub-divisional Magistrate passes an ex parte order prohibiting the procession. The order remains in force for 2 months. If still needed, State Government can extend up to 6 months. The organisers can apply to the Magistrate to rescind the order and will be given a hearing.

BNSS SECTION 164 - PROCEDURE WHERE DISPUTE CONCERNING LAND OR WATER IS LIKELY TO CAUSE BREACH OF PEACE
Core Content:
Whenever an Executive Magistrate is satisfied from police report or other information that a dispute likely to cause breach of peace exists concerning any land or water or boundaries thereof within his local jurisdiction, he shall make an order in writing stating grounds and requiring parties to attend and put in written statements of their respective claims as to fact of actual possession. The Magistrate shall decide which party was in possession at the date of the order, without reference to merits of legal right.

Procedure: Land/Water Dispute Resolution

Executive Magistrate is satisfied from police report or other information that a dispute likely to cause a breach of the peace exists concerning any land or water or boundaries thereof within his local jurisdiction

Magistrate shall make an order in writing, stating the grounds of his being so satisfied

Order shall require the parties concerned in such dispute to:

(i) Attend his Court in person or by an advocate on specified date and time

(ii) Put in written statements of their respective claims as respects the fact of actual possession of the subject of dispute

"Land or water" includes buildings, markets, fisheries, crops or other produce of land, and rents or profits of any such property

Copy of order shall be served as per summons procedure, and at least one copy shall be published by being affixed to some conspicuous place at or near the subject of dispute

Magistrate shall, without reference to the merits or the claims of any of the parties to a right to possess the subject of dispute:

(i) Peruse the statements put in

(ii) Hear the parties

(iii) Receive all such evidence as may be produced by them

(iv) Take such further evidence as he thinks necessary

(v) If possible, decide whether any and which of the parties was, at the date of the order under sub-section (1), in possession of the subject of dispute

Dispossession within 2 months: If it appears to Magistrate that any party has been forcibly and wrongfully dispossessed within two months next before the date on which police report or other information was received by the Magistrate, or after that date and before date of his order under sub-section (1), he may treat the party so dispossessed as if that party had been in possession on the date of his order

Any party or interested person may show that no such dispute exists or has existed - Magistrate shall cancel his order and stay all further proceedings. Subject to such cancellation, the Magistrate's order under sub-section (1) shall be final

If Magistrate decides one party was (or should be treated as being) in such possession, he shall:

(i) Issue an order declaring such party to be entitled to possession thereof until evicted in due course of law

(ii) Forbidding all disturbance of such possession until such eviction

(iii) When proceeding under proviso to sub-section (4), may restore to possession the party forcibly and wrongfully dispossessed

Order shall be served and published as per sub-section (3)

Death of party: Magistrate may cause legal representative of deceased party to be made a party and continue inquiry

Perishable property: If Magistrate is of opinion that any crop or other produce of property is subject to speedy and natural decay, he may order proper custody or sale

Magistrate may issue summons to any witness

Nothing in this section affects Magistrate's power to proceed under section 126

Illustration:
Two neighbours dispute ownership of a strip of land, leading to fights. Executive Magistrate issues order requiring both to state who was in actual possession on a certain date. Magistrate hears evidence, finds Party A was in possession on that date. Magistrate declares A entitled to retain possession until evicted by a civil court, and forbids B from disturbing A's possession. B must now go to civil court to establish legal ownership.

BNSS SECTION 165 - POWER TO ATTACH SUBJECT OF DISPUTE AND TO APPOINT RECEIVER
Core Content:
If the Magistrate at any time after making order under section 164(1) considers the case to be one of emergency, or if he decides that none of the parties was in such possession, or if he is unable to satisfy himself as to which party was in such possession, he may attach the subject of dispute until a competent Court determines the rights of the parties. He may appoint a receiver to look after the property.

Procedure: Attachment and Receiver

Any of the following circumstances exist:

(i) Magistrate considers the case to be one of emergency at any time after making order under section 164(1), OR

(ii) Magistrate decides that none of the parties was in such possession as referred to in section 164, OR

(iii) Magistrate is unable to satisfy himself as to which of them was in such possession of the subject of dispute

Magistrate may attach the subject of dispute until a competent Court has determined the rights of the parties with regard to the person entitled to possession thereof

Withdrawal of attachment: Such Magistrate may withdraw the attachment at any time if satisfied that there is no longer any likelihood of breach of the peace with regard to the subject of dispute

When Magistrate attaches the subject of dispute, he may (if no receiver appointed by any Civil Court):

(i) Make such arrangements as he considers proper for looking after the property, OR

(ii) Appoint a receiver thereof

Receiver shall have, subject to control of Magistrate, all the powers of a receiver appointed under Code of Civil Procedure, 1908

If Civil Court subsequently appoints receiver: Magistrate shall:

(i) Order receiver appointed by him to hand over possession of subject of dispute to receiver appointed by Civil Court, and thereafter discharge the receiver appointed by him

(ii) May make such other incidental or consequential orders as may be just

Illustration:
Magistrate cannot determine which party was in possession of disputed farmland. He attaches the land and appoints a receiver to manage it, collect crops, etc., until a civil court decides ownership. Later, Civil Court appoints its own receiver. Magistrate directs his receiver to hand over possession to the Civil Court receiver and discharges his receiver.

BNSS SECTION 166 - DISPUTE CONCERNING RIGHT OF USE OF LAND OR WATER
Core Content:
Whenever an Executive Magistrate is satisfied that a dispute likely to cause breach of peace exists regarding any alleged right of user of any land or water (whether claimed as easement or otherwise), he shall make an order requiring parties to attend and put in written statements. He shall peruse statements, hear parties, receive evidence, and if possible decide whether such right exists. If such rights exist, he may make an order prohibiting any interference with the exercise of such right, including removal of any obstruction.

Procedure: Right of Use Disputes

Executive Magistrate is satisfied from police report or other information that a dispute likely to cause a breach of the peace exists regarding any alleged right of user of any land or water within his local jurisdiction (whether such right be claimed as an easement or otherwise)

Magistrate shall make an order in writing, stating grounds, and requiring parties concerned to:

(i) Attend his Court in person or by an advocate on a specified date and time

(ii) Put in written statements of their respective claims

"Land or water" has same meaning as in section 164(2) (includes buildings, markets, fisheries, crops, rents, profits)

Magistrate shall:

(i) Peruse the statements put in

(ii) Hear the parties

(iii) Receive all such evidence as may be produced

(iv) Consider effect of such evidence

(v) Take such further evidence as he thinks necessary

(vi) If possible, decide whether such right exists

Provisions of section 164 shall, so far as may be, apply to such inquiry

If it appears to such Magistrate that such rights exist, he may make an order prohibiting any interference with the exercise of such right, including, in a proper case, an order for the removal of any obstruction in the exercise of any such right

Limitation on order: No such order shall be made where the right is exercisable at all times of the year, unless such right has been exercised within three months next before the receipt of police report or other information leading to institution of inquiry

If right is exercisable only at particular seasons or on particular occasions, unless the right has been exercised during the last of such seasons or on the last of such occasions before such receipt

Conversion between section 164 and 166: When in proceedings under section 164(1) Magistrate finds dispute is as regards alleged right of user of land or water, he may after recording reasons continue with proceedings as if commenced under this section. When in proceedings under this section Magistrate finds dispute should be dealt with under section 164, he may after recording reasons continue as if commenced under section 164(1)

Illustration:
Villagers claim a right of way through a private farm to reach a temple. The farmer obstructs the path, causing disputes. Executive Magistrate holds inquiry, finds the right of way has been exercised for generations. Magistrate orders farmer to remove the obstruction and prohibits any interference with villagers' right to use the path.

BNSS SECTION 167 - LOCAL INQUIRY
Core Content:
Whenever a local inquiry is necessary for the purposes of sections 164, 165, or 166, a District Magistrate or Sub-divisional Magistrate may depute any Magistrate subordinate to him to make the inquiry, furnish written instructions, and declare by whom expenses shall be paid. The report of the person so deputed may be read as evidence. The Magistrate passing a decision may direct by whom costs (including witness expenses and advocate's fees) shall be paid.

Procedure: Local Inquiry and Costs

A local inquiry is necessary for the purposes of section 164, 165, or 166

District Magistrate or Sub-divisional Magistrate may depute any Magistrate subordinate to him to make the inquiry

Such Magistrate may:

(i) Furnish him with such written instructions as may seem necessary for his guidance

(ii) Declare by whom the whole or any part of the necessary expenses of the inquiry shall be paid

The report of the person so deputed may be read as evidence in the case

When any costs have been incurred by any party to a proceeding under section 164, 165, or 166, the Magistrate passing a decision may direct by whom such costs shall be paid:

(i) Whether by such party or by any other party to the proceeding

(ii) Whether in whole or in part or proportion

Such costs may include:

(i) Any expenses incurred in respect of witnesses

(ii) Advocate's fees, which the Court may consider reasonable

Illustration:
For a land dispute under section 164, the District Magistrate deputes a subordinate Magistrate to conduct a local inquiry. The subordinate Magistrate visits the land, inspects boundaries, interviews neighbours, and submits a report with photographs. The report is read as evidence. The final decision orders the losing party to pay ₹20,000 as costs, including the other party's advocate fees and witness expenses.

BNSS SECTION 168 - POLICE TO PREVENT COGNIZABLE OFFENCES
Core Content:
Every police officer may interpose for the purpose of preventing, and shall, to the best of his ability, prevent, the commission of any cognizable offence.

Procedure: Duty to Prevent Cognizable Offences

Every police officer has the power to interpose (intervene) for the purpose of preventing the commission of any cognizable offence

Every police officer has the duty to prevent, to the best of his ability, the commission of any cognizable offence

This power and duty exists before the offence is actually committed

The police officer may take reasonable steps to prevent the offence

Illustration:
A police officer sees X pulling out a knife and approaching Y with intent to stab. The officer may (and must) immediately intervene, disarm X, and prevent the stabbing from occurring. The officer does not need to wait for the actual commission of the offence.

BNSS SECTION 169 - INFORMATION OF DESIGN TO COMMIT COGNIZABLE OFFENCES
Core Content:
Every police officer receiving information of a design to commit any cognizable offence shall communicate such information to the police officer to whom he is subordinate, and to any other officer whose duty it is to prevent or take cognizance of the commission of any such offence.

Procedure: Reporting Criminal Designs

Police officer receives information of a design (plan) to commit any cognizable offence

He shall communicate such information to:

(i) The police officer to whom he is subordinate (superior officer), AND

(ii) Any other officer whose duty it is to prevent or take cognizance of the commission of any such offence (e.g., SHO, investigating officer, Magistrate)

Illustration:
A constable learns from an informant that a group is planning to rob a bank tomorrow. The constable immediately reports this information to his SHO and also to the police control room. This allows preventive action to be taken.

BNSS SECTION 170 - ARREST TO PREVENT COMMISSION OF COGNIZABLE OFFENCES
Core Content:
A police officer knowing of a design to commit any cognizable offence may arrest, without orders from a Magistrate and without a warrant, the person so designing, if it appears to such officer that the commission of the offence cannot be otherwise prevented. No person arrested under this section shall be detained in custody for a period exceeding twenty-four hours from the time of his arrest unless his further detention is required or authorised under any other provision of BNSS or any other law.

Procedure: Preventive Arrest

Police officer knows of a design (plan) to commit any cognizable offence

It appears to such officer that the commission of the offence cannot be otherwise prevented (no other way to stop it)

Police officer may arrest, without orders from a Magistrate and without a warrant, the person so designing

Detention limit: No person arrested under this section shall be detained in custody for a period exceeding twenty-four hours from the time of his arrest unless:

(i) His further detention is required under any other provision of BNSS, OR

(ii) His further detention is authorised under any other law for the time being in force

Illustration:
Police receive credible information that X, a known terrorist, has planted a bomb set to explode in 6 hours. The police know X's location. They cannot prevent the explosion except by arresting X to stop him from triggering it. Police arrest X without warrant. They can hold X for up to 24 hours. After 24 hours, they must either charge him with an offence under other provisions (e.g., attempt to commit offence) or release him.

BNSS SECTION 171 - PREVENTION OF INJURY TO PUBLIC PROPERTY
Core Content:
A police officer may of his own authority interpose to prevent any injury attempted to be committed in his view to any public property, movable or immovable, or the removal or injury of any public landmark, buoy or other mark used for navigation.

Procedure: Protecting Public Property

A police officer sees (in his view) any injury attempted to be committed to:

(i) Any public property (movable or immovable), OR

(ii) Any public landmark, OR

(iii) Any buoy, OR

(iv) Any other mark used for navigation

Police officer may, of his own authority (without needing orders from anyone), interpose to prevent such injury

This includes preventing removal of such property or marks

Illustration:
A police officer on patrol sees a person trying to break a public statue (public property) with a hammer. The officer can immediately stop the person and prevent the damage. Similarly, if a police officer sees someone removing a navigation buoy from a river, the officer can intervene to prevent the removal.

BNSS SECTION 172 - PERSONS BOUND TO CONFORM TO LAWFUL DIRECTIONS OF POLICE
Core Content:
All persons shall be bound to conform to the lawful directions of a police officer given in fulfilment of any of his duty under this Chapter. A police officer may detain or remove any person resisting, refusing, ignoring or disregarding to conform to any direction given by him under sub-section (1), and may either take such person before a Magistrate or, in petty cases, release him as soon as possible within a period of twenty-four hours.

Procedure: Enforcement of Police Directions

All persons shall be bound to conform to the lawful directions of a police officer given in fulfilment of any of his duty under this Chapter (Chapter XII - Preventive Action)

Detention power: A police officer may detain or remove any person:

(i) Resisting such direction

(ii) Refusing to conform to such direction

(iii) Ignoring such direction

(iv) Disregarding such direction

After detention, police officer may either:

(i) Take such person before a Magistrate, OR

(ii) In petty cases, release him as soon as possible within a period of twenty-four hours

Illustration:
Police officer orders a crowd to disperse under section 148. X refuses to leave and continues shouting. The police officer detains X. Since this is a petty case (simple disobedience), the officer releases X after 2 hours instead of taking him to a Magistrate. If X had committed a more serious violation, the officer would take X before a Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 173 - INFORMATION IN COGNIZABLE CASES
Core Content:
Every information relating to the commission of a cognizable offence, irrespective of the area where the offence is committed, may be given orally or by electronic communication to an officer in charge of a police station. For sexual offences against a woman, the information shall be recorded by a woman police officer. For mentally or physically disabled victims, the statement shall be recorded at their residence or convenient place, with interpreter/special educator, and shall be videographed. A copy shall be given forthwith free of cost to the informant or victim.

Procedure: Recording FIR (Zero FIR)

Information may be given orally or by electronic communication to any police station (irrespective of jurisdiction - Zero FIR)

If given orally: shall be reduced to writing, read over to the informant, and signed by the informant

If given by electronic communication: shall be taken on record and signed within three days by the person giving it

Substance shall be entered in a book prescribed by State Government rules

Special protection for sexual offence victims: For offences under BNS sections 64-71, 74-79, or 124 (rape, sexual harassment, etc.) against a woman:

Information shall be recorded by a woman police officer or any woman officer

Special protection for disabled victims: If the victim is temporarily or permanently mentally or physically disabled:

Statement shall be recorded at the victim's residence or convenient place of choice

In presence of an interpreter or special educator

The recording shall be videographed

Police officer shall get statement recorded by a Magistrate under section 183(6)(a) as soon as possible

A copy of the information shall be given forthwith, free of cost, to the informant or victim

Preliminary enquiry for 3-7 year offences: For offences punishable with 3 to 7 years, officer in charge may with prior permission from Deputy Superintendent of Police:

(i) Proceed to conduct preliminary enquiry within 14 days to ascertain prima facie case, OR

(ii) Proceed with investigation when prima facie case exists

Remedy for refusal to register FIR: Any person aggrieved by refusal to record information may send it to Superintendent of Police who shall investigate or direct investigation. Failing which, aggrieved person may make application to Magistrate

Illustration:
A woman is raped in Mumbai. She goes to a police station in Delhi (different jurisdiction). The Delhi police cannot refuse - they register a Zero FIR. A woman police officer records her statement in writing, reads it to her, and takes her signature. A free copy is given immediately. Since she is the victim of a sexual offence, the entire process is videographed.

BNSS SECTION 174 - INFORMATION AS TO NON-COGNIZABLE CASES AND INVESTIGATION OF SUCH CASES
Core Content:
When information is given of a non-cognizable offence within police station limits, the officer shall enter the substance in a book, refer the informant to the Magistrate, and forward a daily diary report fortnightly to the Magistrate. No police officer shall investigate a non-cognizable case without a Magistrate's order. If a case relates to two or more offences of which at least one is cognizable, the case shall be deemed cognizable.

Procedure: Non-Cognizable Offence Handling

Information given to officer in charge of police station of commission of a non-cognizable offence within limits of such station

Officer shall enter or cause to be entered the substance of information in a book in form prescribed by State Government rules

Officer shall:

(i) Refer the informant to the Magistrate

(ii) Forward the daily diary report of all such cases fortnightly to the Magistrate

No police officer shall investigate a non-cognizable case without the order of a Magistrate having power to try such case or commit the case for trial

Any police officer receiving such Magistrate's order may exercise same powers in investigation (except power to arrest without warrant) as officer in charge of police station may exercise in a cognizable case

Mixed offences: Where a case relates to two or more offences of which at least one is cognizable, the case shall be deemed to be a cognizable case (notwithstanding that other offences are non-cognizable)

Illustration:
X files a complaint of simple hurt (non-cognizable) at police station. SHO records it, gives X a reference to go to Magistrate, and sends fortnightly report to Magistrate. X goes to Magistrate who orders police to investigate. Police then investigate but cannot arrest without warrant. If the same act also involves criminal intimidation (cognizable), the whole case is treated as cognizable.

BNSS SECTION 175 - POLICE OFFICER'S POWER TO INVESTIGATE COGNIZABLE CASE
Core Content:
Any officer in charge of a police station may, without order of a Magistrate, investigate any cognizable case which a Court having jurisdiction over the local area would have power to inquire into or try. The Superintendent of Police may require the Deputy Superintendent of Police to investigate considering the nature and gravity of the offence. No proceeding of a police officer in any such case shall be called in question on the ground that he was not empowered to investigate.

Procedure: Investigation of Cognizable Cases

Any officer in charge of a police station may, without order of a Magistrate, investigate any cognizable case which a Court having jurisdiction over the local area would have power to inquire into or try under Chapter XIV

Considering the nature and gravity of the offence, the Superintendent of Police may require the Deputy Superintendent of Police to investigate the case

No proceeding of a police officer in any such case shall at any stage be called in question on the ground that the case was one which such officer was not empowered under this section to investigate

Any Magistrate empowered under section 210 may, after considering application supported by affidavit under section 173(4) and after inquiry and submissions, order such investigation

Any Magistrate under section 210 may, upon receiving a complaint against a public servant arising in course of discharge of official duties, order investigation subject to:

(a) Receiving a report containing facts and circumstances from the officer superior to him

(b) After consideration of assertions made by the public servant as to the situation that led to the incident

Illustration:
The SHO of City Police Station receives information about a murder. He can immediately begin investigation without waiting for a Magistrate's order. If the case is very serious, the SP can direct the DSP to personally investigate. Even if someone later argues that the SHO was not supposed to investigate this type of case, the investigation cannot be challenged on that ground alone.

BNSS SECTION 176 - PROCEDURE FOR INVESTIGATION
Core Content:
On receiving information about a cognizable offence, the officer in charge shall forthwith send a report to the Magistrate and proceed to investigate. For rape offences, the victim's statement shall be recorded at her residence or place of choice, by a woman police officer if practicable, in presence of parents/guardian/relative/social worker, and may be recorded through audio-video electronic means. For offences punishable with 7 years or more, a forensic expert shall visit the crime scene to collect forensic evidence and the process shall be videographed.

Procedure: Commencing Investigation

Officer in charge of police station has reason to suspect commission of an offence which he is empowered under section 175 to investigate

He shall forthwith send a report of the same to a Magistrate empowered to take cognizance of such offence upon a police report

He shall proceed in person, or depute a subordinate officer (not below rank prescribed by State Government) to:

(i) Proceed to the spot

(ii) Investigate the facts and circumstances of the case

(iii) If necessary, take measures for discovery and arrest of the offender

Exceptions where full spot investigation not required:

(a) When information is given against any person by name and the case is not of a serious nature - officer need not proceed in person or depute subordinate to investigate on the spot

(b) If it appears to officer that there is no sufficient ground for investigation - he shall not investigate

In both cases, officer shall state reasons in his report and forward daily diary report fortnightly to Magistrate. In case (b), shall also forthwith notify informant

Rape victim statement (First Proviso to sub-section (1)):

Recording of statement of victim shall be conducted at residence of victim or place of her choice

As far as practicable by a woman police officer

In presence of her parents or guardian or near relatives or social worker of the locality

Such statement may also be recorded through any audio-video electronic means including mobile phone

Forensic investigation for serious offences (sub-section (3)):

On receipt of information relating to commission of an offence punishable for 7 years or more

From such date as may be notified within 5 years by State Government

Officer in charge shall cause the forensic expert to visit the crime scene to collect forensic evidence

Shall also cause videography of the process on mobile phone or any other electronic device

If forensic facility not available in the State, State Government shall notify utilisation of such facility of any other State

Illustration:
A rape is reported. A woman police officer goes to the victim's home (as she requested) and records her statement in presence of her mother, using a mobile phone video recording. The offence is punishable with more than 7 years. A forensic expert is called to the scene to collect DNA samples, fingerprints, and other evidence. The entire forensic collection process is videographed.

BNSS SECTION 177 - REPORT HOW SUBMITTED
Core Content:
Every report sent to a Magistrate under section 176 shall, if the State Government so directs, be submitted through such superior officer of police as the State Government appoints. Such superior officer may give instructions to the officer in charge and shall, after recording such instructions on the report, transmit the same without delay to the Magistrate.

Procedure: Report Submission Chain

Report sent to Magistrate under section 176

If State Government so directs, report shall be submitted through a superior officer of police appointed by the State Government

Such superior officer may give instructions to the officer in charge of the police station as he thinks fit

He shall, after recording such instructions on the report, transmit the same without delay to the Magistrate
