Illustration:
State Government directs that all investigation reports shall go through the Superintendent of Police. The SHO sends his report to the SP. The SP reviews it, adds instructions: "Further investigate witness X," records this on the report, and forwards it to the Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 178 - POWER TO HOLD INVESTIGATION OR PRELIMINARY INQUIRY
Core Content:
The Magistrate, on receiving a report under section 176, may direct an investigation, or if he thinks fit, at once proceed or depute any Magistrate subordinate to him to hold a preliminary inquiry or otherwise dispose of the case in the manner provided in BNSS.

Procedure: Magistrate's Options on Receipt of Report

Magistrate receives report under section 176

Magistrate may:

(i) Direct an investigation, OR

(ii) If he thinks fit, at once proceed to hold a preliminary inquiry himself, OR

(iii) Depute any Magistrate subordinate to him to hold a preliminary inquiry, OR

(iv) Otherwise dispose of the case in the manner provided in BNSS

Illustration:
Magistrate receives police report about a cognizable offence. Instead of sending it back for more investigation, the Magistrate decides to conduct a preliminary inquiry himself. He examines the complainant and witnesses present, records their statements, and then decides whether to issue process.

BNSS SECTION 179 - POLICE OFFICER'S POWER TO REQUIRE ATTENDANCE OF WITNESSES
Core Content:
Any police officer making an investigation may, by order in writing, require the attendance before himself of any person within the limits of his own or any adjoining station who appears acquainted with the facts. No male person under 15 years or above 60 years, woman, mentally/physically disabled person, or person with acute illness shall be required to attend at any place other than their residence. If such person is willing to attend at the police station, they may be permitted.

Procedure: Summoning Witnesses for Investigation

Police officer making investigation under Chapter XIII may, by order in writing, require attendance before himself of any person:

(i) Being within limits of his own police station, OR

(ii) Being within limits of any adjoining police station

(iii) Who, from information given or otherwise, appears to be acquainted with facts and circumstances of case

Such person shall attend as so required

Protected persons not required to attend away from residence:

(i) No male person under age of 15 years

(ii) No male person above age of 60 years

(iii) No woman

(iv) No mentally or physically disabled person

(v) No person with acute illness
→ shall be required to attend at any place other than the place in which such person resides

If such person is willing to attend at the police station, they may be permitted to do so

State Government may make rules providing for payment by police officer of reasonable expenses of every person attending under this section at any place other than their residence

Illustration:
Investigating officer wants to question X, a 70-year-old man who witnessed a crime. The officer cannot require X to come to the police station. The officer must go to X's residence to question him. If X is willing and able to come to the station, he may be permitted.

BNSS SECTION 180 - EXAMINATION OF WITNESSES BY POLICE
Core Content:
Any police officer making investigation may examine orally any person supposed to be acquainted with the facts. Such person shall be bound to answer truly all questions relating to the case, other than questions which would expose him to a criminal charge or penalty. The police officer may reduce the statement to writing and shall make a separate and true record of each person's statement. The statement may also be recorded by audio-video electronic means.

Procedure: Witness Examination

Any police officer making investigation, or any police officer not below such rank as State Government prescribes acting on requisition of such officer, may examine orally any person supposed to be acquainted with the facts and circumstances of the case

Such person shall be bound to answer truly all questions relating to such case put to him by such officer

Privilege against self-incrimination: The person need not answer questions the answers to which would have a tendency to expose him to a criminal charge or to a penalty or forfeiture

The police officer may reduce into writing any statement made to him

If he does so, he shall make a separate and true record of the statement of each such person whose statement he records

Statement may also be recorded by audio-video electronic means

For offences under BNS sections 64-71, 74-79, or 124 against a woman, the statement shall be recorded by a woman police officer or any woman officer

Illustration:
Investigating officer examines witness X. X tells the officer what he saw. The officer writes down X's statement as a separate record. X is asked "Did you also participate in the crime?" X can refuse to answer because it would incriminate him. The officer also records the statement on video as a backup.

BNSS SECTION 181 - STATEMENTS TO POLICE AND USE THEREOF
Core Content:
No statement made by any person to a police officer in the course of investigation, if reduced to writing, shall be signed by the person making it. Such statement shall not be used for any purpose save as hereinafter provided. When a prosecution witness is called, any part of his statement, if duly proved, may be used by the accused (and with Court permission, by the prosecution) to contradict the witness as per Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023 section 148.

Procedure: Use of Police Statements

No statement made by any person to a police officer in the course of investigation under this Chapter, if reduced to writing, shall be signed by the person making it

No such statement or any record thereof (whether in police diary or otherwise) or any part of such statement or record shall be used for any purpose, save as hereinafter provided, at any inquiry or trial in respect of any offence under investigation at the time when such statement was made

Exception - contradiction: When any witness is called for the prosecution in such inquiry or trial whose statement has been reduced into writing as aforesaid:

Any part of his statement, if duly proved, may be used by the accused

With permission of the Court, by the prosecution

To contradict such witness in the manner provided by section 148 of Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023

When any part of such statement is so used, any part thereof may also be used in re-examination of such witness, but for purpose only of explaining any matter referred to in his cross-examination

Nothing in this section applies to:

Any statement falling within clause (a) of section 26 of Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023 (statements causing discovery of facts)

Or affects the proviso to section 23(2) of that Adhiniyam

Omission as contradiction: An omission to state a fact or circumstance in the statement may amount to contradiction if the same appears to be significant and otherwise relevant having regard to the context. Whether any omission amounts to a contradiction in the particular context shall be a question of fact

Illustration:
X makes a statement to police during investigation that he saw Y at the crime scene. The statement is not signed by X. At trial, X as prosecution witness says he did not see Y. The defence lawyer can use X's previous police statement (duly proved) to contradict him. The significant omission of a fact from the police statement can also be treated as a contradiction.

BNSS SECTION 182 - NO INDUCEMENT TO BE OFFERED
Core Content:
No police officer or other person in authority shall offer or make any inducement, threat or promise as mentioned in section 22 of Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023 (which makes confessions caused by inducement, threat or promise irrelevant). But no police officer or other person shall prevent any person from making any statement he may be disposed to make of his own free will.

Procedure: Prohibition on Inducement

No police officer or other person in authority shall offer or make, or cause to be offered or made, any such inducement, threat or promise as is mentioned in section 22 of Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023

But no police officer or other person shall prevent, by any caution or otherwise, any person from making in the course of any investigation under this Chapter any statement which he may be disposed to make of his own free will

Nothing in this section affects the provisions of section 183(4) (Magistrate's explanation before recording confession)

Illustration:
Police officer tells suspect X: "If you confess, I'll let you go home." This is an inducement prohibited under this section. Any confession made as a result would be irrelevant under evidence law. However, if X wants to voluntarily make a statement, the police officer cannot stop him or caution him not to speak (except as required under section 183(4) before a Magistrate).

BNSS SECTION 183 - RECORDING OF CONFESSIONS AND STATEMENTS
Core Content:
Any Magistrate of the district where the offence information has been registered may record any confession or statement made to him in the course of investigation, whether or not he has jurisdiction. Confession may be recorded by audio-video electronic means in presence of accused's advocate. No confession shall be recorded by a police officer. The Magistrate shall explain that the person is not bound to confess and that it may be used against him, and shall only record if believed to be voluntary.

Procedure: Recording Confession before Magistrate

Any Magistrate of the District in which information about commission of any offence has been registered may, whether or not he has jurisdiction in the case, record any confession or statement made to him:

(i) In the course of investigation under this Chapter or under any other law, OR

(ii) At any time afterwards but before commencement of inquiry or trial

Confession may also be recorded by audio-video electronic means in the presence of the advocate of the person accused of an offence

No police confession: No confession shall be recorded by a police officer on whom any power of a Magistrate has been conferred under any law

Magistrate's duties before recording:

(i) Explain to the person making it that he is not bound to make a confession

(ii) Explain that if he does so, it may be used as evidence against him

(iii) Magistrate shall not record any such confession unless, upon questioning the person making it, he has reason to believe that it is being made voluntarily

If at any time before confession is recorded, the person states that he is not willing to make the confession, the Magistrate shall not authorise the detention of such person in police custody

Confession shall be recorded in the manner provided in section 316 for recording examination of accused, and shall be signed by the person making the confession

Magistrate shall make a memorandum at the foot of such record stating:

"I have explained to (name) that he is not bound to make a confession and that, if he does so, any confession he may make may be used as evidence against him and I believe that this confession was voluntarily made. It was taken in my presence and hearing, and was read over to the person making it and admitted by him to be correct, and it contains a full and true account of the statement made by him." (Signed) A.B. Magistrate

Any statement (other than a confession) shall be recorded in such manner as is best fitted to circumstances, and Magistrate may administer oath

Sexual offence victim statement (sub-section (6)):

For offences under BNS sections 64-71, 74-79, or 124, Magistrate shall record statement of victim as soon as commission of offence is brought to police notice

As far as practicable, record by a woman Magistrate; in her absence, by a male Magistrate in presence of a woman

For offences punishable with 10+ years/life/death, Magistrate shall record statement of witness brought before him by police officer

If victim is mentally or physically disabled, Magistrate shall take assistance of interpreter or special educator

Statement of mentally/physically disabled person recorded with assistance of interpreter/special educator shall be recorded through audio-video electronic means preferably by mobile phone

Such statement shall be considered a statement in lieu of examination-in-chief as per section 142 of Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, and the maker can be cross-examined on such statement without needing to record it again at trial

Illustration:
X is arrested for murder. He tells police he wants to confess. Police take him to a Magistrate. The Magistrate asks X: "Are you making this confession voluntarily?" X says yes. Magistrate explains: "You don't have to confess. If you do confess, it can be used as evidence against you." X still wants to confess. Magistrate records the confession on video with X's advocate present. Magistrate signs the memorandum. This confession can be used as evidence at trial.

BNSS SECTION 184 - MEDICAL EXAMINATION OF VICTIM OF RAPE
Core Content:
Where during investigation of rape or attempt to commit rape, it is proposed to examine the woman victim by a medical expert, such examination shall be conducted by a registered medical practitioner employed in a Government or local authority hospital (or any other registered medical practitioner if none available within 24 hours), with the consent of the woman or person competent to give consent on her behalf. The woman shall be sent to such practitioner within twenty-four hours from time of receiving information of the offence.

Procedure: Medical Examination of Rape Victim

During stage when offence of committing rape or attempt to commit rape is under investigation

It is proposed to get the person of the woman examined by a medical expert

Such examination shall be conducted by:

(i) A registered medical practitioner employed in a hospital run by Government or local authority, OR

(ii) In absence of such practitioner within 24 hours, by any other registered medical practitioner

Examination shall be with the consent of:

(i) Such woman, OR

(ii) A person competent to give such consent on her behalf

Such woman shall be sent to such registered medical practitioner within twenty-four hours from the time of receiving the information relating to the commission of such offence

The registered medical practitioner shall, without delay, examine her person and prepare a report giving:

(i) Name and address of woman and person who brought her

(ii) Age of woman

(iii) Description of material taken from person of woman for DNA profiling

(iv) Marks of injury, if any, on person of woman

(v) General mental condition of woman

(vi) Other material particulars in reasonable detail

Report shall state precisely reasons for each conclusion

Report shall specifically record that consent of woman or person competent to give such consent had been obtained

Exact time of commencement and completion of examination shall be noted

Registered medical practitioner shall, within a period of seven days, forward the report to investigating officer who shall forward it to Magistrate under section 193 as part of documents referred to in section 193(6)(a)

Nothing in this section renders lawful any examination without consent

Illustration:
A rape is reported at 10 AM. The woman victim is taken to the Government hospital by 11 AM (within 24 hours). A female registered medical practitioner examines her with her consent, takes DNA samples, notes injuries, and notes her mental condition. The report is completed and sent to the investigating officer within 7 days, who includes it in the charge sheet to the Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 185 - SEARCH BY POLICE OFFICER
Core Content:
Whenever an officer in charge of a police station or a police officer making investigation has reasonable grounds for believing that anything necessary for investigation may be found in any place within police station limits and cannot be otherwise obtained without undue delay, such officer may, after recording grounds in case-diary and specifying the thing, search or cause search to be made. The search shall be recorded through audio-video electronic means preferably by mobile phone. Copies of records shall forthwith be sent to the nearest Magistrate within 48 hours.

Procedure: Police Search without Warrant

Officer in charge of police station or police officer making investigation has reasonable grounds for believing that anything necessary for investigation may be found in any place within limits of police station

Such thing cannot in his opinion be otherwise obtained without undue delay

Such officer may, after recording in writing the grounds of his belief in the case-diary and specifying so far as possible the thing for which search is to be made, search or cause search to be made for such thing in any place within limits of such station

Recording of search: Search conducted under this section shall be recorded through audio-video electronic means preferably by mobile phone

If officer unable to conduct search in person and no other competent person present, he may:

(i) Record reasons in writing

(ii) Require any officer subordinate to him to make the search

(iii) Deliver order in writing specifying place to be searched and thing for which search is to be made

Provisions as to search-warrants and general provisions as to searches contained in section 103 (witnesses, list, etc.) apply to search under this section

Copies of any record made under sub-section (1) or (3) shall forthwith, but not later than forty-eight hours, be sent to the nearest Magistrate empowered to take cognizance of the offence

Owner or occupier of place searched shall, on application, be furnished free of cost with a copy of the same by the Magistrate

Illustration:
Investigating officer believes that stolen jewellery is hidden in X's house. Getting a search warrant would take 3 days, by which time X might dispose of the jewellery. The officer records his grounds in the case diary ("belief based on informant's statement, X is known fence of stolen goods"), specifies "stolen jewellery," and searches X's house with two witnesses. The entire search is recorded on a mobile phone. Within 48 hours, the recording and records are sent to the Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 186 - WHEN OFFICER IN CHARGE OF POLICE STATION MAY REQUIRE ANOTHER TO ISSUE SEARCH-WARRANT
Core Content:
An officer in charge of a police station or a police officer not below sub-inspector making investigation may require an officer in charge of another police station (same or different district) to cause a search to be made. If delay might result in evidence being concealed or destroyed, he may search any place in another police station limits as if it were within his own station. Notice of such search shall be sent to the officer in charge of that police station and to the nearest Magistrate.

Procedure: Cross-Jurisdiction Search

Officer in charge of police station or police officer not below rank of sub-inspector making investigation may require an officer in charge of another police station (whether in same or different district) to cause a search to be made in any place

This applies when the former officer might cause such search to be made within limits of his own station

Such officer, on being so required, shall proceed according to section 185 and shall forward the thing found to the officer at whose request the search was made

Emergency search without request: Whenever there is reason to believe that delay occasioned by requiring another police station to cause search might result in evidence being concealed or destroyed, it shall be lawful for officer in charge or investigating officer to search, or cause to be searched, any place in limits of another police station in accordance with section 185, as if such place were within limits of his own police station

Any officer conducting such emergency search shall forthwith send notice of the search to the officer in charge of the police station within whose limits such place is situate

He shall also send with such notice a copy of the list (if any) prepared under section 103

He shall also send to the nearest Magistrate empowered to take cognizance of the offence, copies of the records referred to in section 185(1) and (3)

Owner or occupier of place searched shall, on application, be furnished free of cost with a copy of any record sent to the Magistrate

Illustration:
Investigating officer in Delhi believes stolen goods are in a house in Gurugram (different district). Getting a formal request to Gurugram police might take time. If the officer believes the goods will be destroyed tonight, he can immediately go to Gurugram and search the house as if it were in Delhi. He must then notify the Gurugram SHO and send records to the Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 187 - PROCEDURE WHEN INVESTIGATION CANNOT BE COMPLETED IN TWENTY-FOUR HOURS
Core Content:
When any person is arrested and investigation cannot be completed within 24 hours, the officer in charge shall forthwith transmit a copy of diary entries to the nearest Magistrate and forward the accused. The Magistrate may authorise detention for a total period not exceeding 90 days (for offences punishable with death, life imprisonment, or 10+ years) or 60 days (for other offences). On expiry of this period, the accused shall be released on bail if he furnishes bail (default bail).

Procedure: Remand and Default Bail

Any person is arrested and detained in custody

Investigation cannot be completed within period of 24 hours fixed by section 58

There are grounds for believing that the accusation or information is well-founded

Officer in charge of police station or police officer making investigation (if not below rank of sub-inspector) shall:

(i) Forthwith transmit to the nearest Magistrate a copy of entries in the diary relating to the case

(ii) At the same time forward the accused to such Magistrate

Magistrate to whom accused is forwarded may (irrespective of whether he has jurisdiction to try the case), after considering whether person has not been released on bail or bail has been cancelled, authorise from time to time detention of accused in such custody as Magistrate thinks fit, for a term not exceeding fifteen days in the whole (or in parts) at any time during the initial 40 or 60 days out of detention period of 60 or 90 days as provided in sub-section (3)

If Magistrate has no jurisdiction to try or commit for trial, and considers further detention unnecessary, he may order accused to be forwarded to a Magistrate having such jurisdiction

Magistrate may authorise detention beyond 15 days if satisfied adequate grounds exist, but total period shall not exceed:

(i) 90 days where investigation relates to offence punishable with death, imprisonment for life, or imprisonment for 10 years or more

(ii) 60 days where investigation relates to any other offence

Default bail: On expiry of 90 days or 60 days (as the case may be), the accused person shall be released on bail if he is prepared to and does furnish bail

No Magistrate shall authorise detention of accused in police custody unless accused is produced before him in person for first time and subsequently every time till accused remains in police custody

Magistrate may extend further detention in judicial custody on production of accused either in person or through audio-video electronic means

No Magistrate of second class (not specially empowered by High Court) shall authorise police custody detention

Proviso for woman under 18: Detention shall be authorised to be in custody of a remand home or recognised social institution

No person shall be detained otherwise than in police station under police custody or in prison under judicial custody or a place declared as prison by Central/State Government

Executive Magistrate power when Judicial Magistrate not available: Officer in charge may transmit to nearest Executive Magistrate (on whom powers of Magistrate conferred) and forward accused. Executive Magistrate may authorise detention for a term not exceeding seven days in aggregate. On expiry, accused released on bail unless further detention ordered by competent Judicial Magistrate

Illustration:
X is arrested for a murder case (punishable with death). Police cannot complete investigation within 24 hours. They produce X before Magistrate. Magistrate authorises 14 days police custody. After 14 days, Magistrate extends judicial custody. If no charge sheet is filed within 90 days from arrest, X is entitled to be released on default bail. The 90-day clock stops on the day charge sheet is filed.

BNSS SECTION 188 - REPORT OF INVESTIGATION BY SUBORDINATE POLICE OFFICER
Core Content:
When any subordinate police officer has made any investigation under this Chapter, he shall report the result of such investigation to the officer in charge of the police station.

Procedure: Subordinate Officer Reporting

Any subordinate police officer (below rank of officer in charge) has made any investigation under this Chapter

He shall report the result of such investigation to the officer in charge of the police station

Illustration:
A Sub-Inspector is deputed by the SHO to investigate a theft case. After completing investigation, the Sub-Inspector submits a detailed report to the SHO with his findings, evidence collected, and recommendation on whether to file charge sheet.

BNSS SECTION 189 - RELEASE OF ACCUSED WHEN EVIDENCE DEFICIENT
Core Content:
If upon investigation it appears to the officer in charge of the police station that there is not sufficient evidence or reasonable ground of suspicion to justify forwarding the accused to a Magistrate, such officer shall, if such person is in custody, release him on his executing a bond or bail bond to appear before a Magistrate if and when required.

Procedure: Release for Insufficient Evidence

Upon investigation under this Chapter, it appears to officer in charge of police station that:

(i) There is not sufficient evidence, OR

(ii) There is not reasonable ground of suspicion

to justify forwarding the accused to a Magistrate

If such person is in custody, officer shall release him

Release shall be on his executing a bond or bail bond as such officer may direct

Bond condition: to appear, if and when so required, before a Magistrate empowered to take cognizance of the offence on a police report, and to try the accused or commit him for trial

Illustration:
X is arrested for theft based on a complaint. Investigation reveals the complaint was false and X was not involved. The SHO releases X on his executing a bond of ₹5,000 promising to appear if later required. If no further evidence emerges, X is not called again.

BNSS SECTION 190 - CASES TO BE SENT TO MAGISTRATE, WHEN EVIDENCE IS SUFFICIENT
Core Content:
If upon investigation it appears that there is sufficient evidence or reasonable ground, the officer in charge shall forward the accused under custody to a Magistrate, or if offence is bailable and accused can give security, take security for his appearance. He shall send to the Magistrate any weapon or other article necessary to be produced, and shall require the complainant and witnesses to execute a bond to appear before the Magistrate.

Procedure: Filing Charge Sheet with Accused

Upon investigation, it appears to officer in charge that:

(i) There is sufficient evidence, OR

(ii) There is reasonable ground as aforesaid

Officer in charge shall forward the accused under custody to a Magistrate empowered to take cognizance of the offence upon a police report and to try the accused or commit him for trial

If the offence is bailable and the accused is able to give security, shall take security from him for his appearance before such Magistrate on a day fixed and for his attendance from day to day until otherwise directed

If the accused is not in custody, the police officer shall take security from such person for his appearance before the Magistrate, and the Magistrate to whom such report is forwarded shall not refuse to accept the same on the ground that the accused is not taken in custody

Officer shall send to such Magistrate any weapon or other article which it may be necessary to produce before him

Officer shall require the complainant (if any) and so many of the persons who appear to such officer to be acquainted with the facts as he may think necessary, to execute a bond to appear before the Magistrate as thereby directed and prosecute or give evidence (as the case may be) in the matter of the charge against the accused

If the Court of the Chief Judicial Magistrate is mentioned in the bond, such Court shall be held to include any Court to which such Magistrate may refer the case for inquiry or trial, provided reasonable notice of such reference is given to such complainant or persons

The officer in whose presence the bond is executed shall deliver a copy thereof to one of the persons who executed it, and shall then send to the Magistrate the original with his report

Illustration:
Investigation finds sufficient evidence against X for theft (bailable). The SHO takes a bail bond from X for his appearance before Magistrate on March 1. The SHO sends the stolen items, the complaint, witness statements, and the bond to the Magistrate. The complainant and witnesses execute bonds to appear and give evidence.

BNSS SECTION 191 - COMPLAINANT AND WITNESSES NOT TO BE REQUIRED TO ACCOMPANY POLICE OFFICER AND NOT TO BE SUBJECT TO RESTRAINT
Core Content:
No complainant or witness on his way to any Court shall be required to accompany a police officer, or shall be subjected to unnecessary restraint or inconvenience, or required to give any security for his appearance other than his own bond. If any complainant or witness refuses to attend or to execute a bond as directed, the officer in charge may forward him in custody to the Magistrate, who may detain him until he executes such bond or until the hearing of the case is completed.

Procedure: Protection of Complainants and Witnesses

No complainant or witness on his way to any Court shall be:

(i) Required to accompany a police officer

(ii) Subjected to unnecessary restraint or inconvenience

(iii) Required to give any security for his appearance other than his own bond

If any complainant or witness refuses to attend or to execute a bond as directed in section 190, the officer in charge of the police station may forward him in custody to the Magistrate

The Magistrate may detain him in custody until:

(i) He executes such bond, OR

(ii) The hearing of the case is completed

Illustration:
A witness is travelling to court. A police officer cannot force him to ride in the police vehicle. The witness gives his own bond (no sureties required) to appear. If the witness refuses to give even his own bond and refuses to attend, the SHO can send him in custody to the Magistrate. The Magistrate can keep him in custody until the trial is over or until he gives bond.

BNSS SECTION 192 - DIARY OF PROCEEDINGS IN INVESTIGATION
Core Content:
Every police officer making investigation shall day by day enter his proceedings in a diary, setting forth times, places visited, and circumstances ascertained. The diary shall be a volume and duly paginated. Any Criminal Court may send for the diaries and may use them to aid in inquiry or trial, but not as evidence. Neither the accused nor his agents shall be entitled to call for or see such diaries merely because they are referred to by the Court.

Procedure: Case Diary Maintenance

Every police officer making an investigation under this Chapter shall day by day enter his proceedings in the investigation in a diary, setting forth:

(i) The time at which the information reached him

(ii) The time at which he began and closed his investigation

(iii) The place or places visited by him

(iv) A statement of the circumstances ascertained through his investigation

The statements of witnesses recorded during investigation under section 180 shall be inserted in the case diary

The diary shall be a volume and duly paginated

Any Criminal Court may send for the police diaries of a case under inquiry or trial in such Court

The Court may use such diaries, not as evidence in the case, but to aid it in such inquiry or trial

No right of accused to see diaries: Neither the accused nor his agents shall be entitled to call for such diaries, nor shall he or they be entitled to see them merely because they are referred to by the Court

Exception: If they are used by the police officer who made them to refresh his memory, or if the Court uses them for the purpose of contradicting such police officer, the provisions of section 148 or section 164 of Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023 shall apply

Illustration:
Investigating officer maintains a daily case diary: "Day 1 - 10 AM received information, 11 AM reached crime scene, 2 PM examined witness X." The Court can ask to see this diary to understand the investigation timeline. The Court cannot use the diary as evidence of facts. The accused cannot demand to see the diary just because the Court looked at it. But if the officer uses the diary to refresh his memory in court, the accused can then see relevant parts.

BNSS SECTION 193 - REPORT OF POLICE OFFICER ON COMPLETION OF INVESTIGATION
Core Content:
Every investigation shall be completed without unnecessary delay. For sexual offences under BNS sections 64-68, 70, 71, investigation shall be completed within two months. As soon as investigation is completed, the officer in charge shall forward a report (charge sheet) to the Magistrate stating names of parties, nature of information, whether offence appears committed and by whom, whether accused arrested, etc. The officer shall also forward documents and witness statements. Further investigation after charge sheet is permitted with Court permission, to be completed within 90 days.

Procedure: Filing Charge Sheet (Final Report)

Every investigation under this Chapter shall be completed without unnecessary delay

Time limit for sexual offences: Investigation in relation to offences under BNS sections 64-68, 70, 71 (rape, etc.) or under POCSO sections 4, 6, 8, 10 shall be completed within two months from date on which information was recorded by officer in charge

As soon as investigation is completed, officer in charge shall forward (including through electronic communication) to a Magistrate empowered to take cognizance of the offence on a police report, a report in the form as State Government may by rules provide, stating:

(a) Names of parties

(b) Nature of information

(c) Names of persons who appear to be acquainted with circumstances of case

(d) Whether any offence appears to have been committed and, if so, by whom

(e) Whether accused has been arrested

(f) Whether accused has been released on his bond or bail bond

(g) Whether accused has been forwarded in custody under section 190

(h) Whether report of medical examination of woman has been attached (for sexual offences)

(i) Sequence of custody in case of electronic device

Police officer shall within a period of ninety days inform the progress of investigation by any means including electronic communication to the informant or the victim

Officer shall also communicate action taken to person who first gave information

When report is forwarded, police officer shall forward to Magistrate along with report:

(a) All documents or relevant extracts on which prosecution proposes to rely (other than those already sent)

(b) Statements recorded under section 180 of all persons whom prosecution proposes to examine as its witnesses

If police officer is of opinion that any part of any statement is not relevant or disclosure is not essential in interest of justice and is inexpedient in public interest, he shall indicate that part and append a note requesting Magistrate to exclude that part from copies to be granted to accused, stating reasons

Subject to above, police officer shall submit such number of copies of police report along with other documents duly indexed to Magistrate for supply to accused as required under section 230. Supply by electronic communication shall be considered duly served

Further investigation after charge sheet: Nothing precludes further investigation after report has been forwarded. Where upon such investigation further evidence is obtained, officer shall forward a further report. Further investigation during trial may be conducted with permission of Court trying the case and shall be completed within 90 days (extendable with Court permission)

Illustration:
A rape case (BNS section 64) is registered on January 1. Police must complete investigation and file charge sheet by March 1 (2 months). The charge sheet states: "X is the accused, Y is the victim, witnesses A and B were examined, medical report attached." Police inform the victim of progress within 90 days. If after charge sheet new evidence is found, police can file a supplementary charge sheet with Court permission within 90 days.

BNSS SECTION 194 - POLICE TO ENQUIRE AND REPORT ON SUICIDE, ETC.
Core Content:
When officer in charge receives information that a person has committed suicide, or has been killed by another, animal, machinery, or accident, or has died under circumstances raising suspicion of an offence, he shall immediately give intimation to the nearest Executive Magistrate empowered to hold inquests, and shall proceed to the place where the body is. In presence of two or more respectable inhabitants, he shall investigate and draw up a report of the apparent cause of death. For suspicious deaths (suicide or death of woman within 7 years of marriage), the body shall be forwarded to the nearest Civil Surgeon for examination.

Procedure: Inquest and Inquiry into Unnatural Death

Officer in charge of police station or other police officer specially empowered by State Government receives information that:

(i) A person has committed suicide, OR

(ii) A person has been killed by another, or by an animal, or by machinery, or by an accident, OR

(iii) A person has died under circumstances raising reasonable suspicion that some other person has committed an offence

He shall immediately give intimation thereof to the nearest Executive Magistrate empowered to hold inquests

Unless otherwise directed by State Government rules or District/Sub-divisional Magistrate's order, he shall proceed to the place where the body is

There, in the presence of two or more respectable inhabitants of the neighbourhood, he shall:

(i) Make an investigation

(ii) Draw up a report of the apparent cause of death, describing wounds, fractures, bruises, other marks of injury as may be found on the body

(iii) State in what manner, or by what weapon or instrument (if any), such marks appear to have been inflicted

The report shall be signed by such police officer and other persons, or by so many of them as concur therein

The report shall be forwarded to the District Magistrate or Sub-divisional Magistrate within twenty-four hours

Mandatory forwarding of body for medical examination when:

(i) The case involves suicide by a woman within seven years of her marriage, OR

(ii) The case relates to death of a woman within seven years of her marriage in circumstances raising reasonable suspicion that some other person committed an offence, OR

(iii) The case relates to death of a woman within seven years of her marriage and any relative of the woman has made a request, OR

(iv) There is any doubt regarding the cause of death, OR

(v) The police officer for any other reason considers it expedient

→ He shall subject to State Government rules forward the body to the nearest Civil Surgeon or other qualified medical person appointed by State Government, if the state of weather and distance admit without risk of putrefaction rendering examination useless

The following Magistrates are empowered to hold inquests: District Magistrate, Sub-divisional Magistrate, and any other Executive Magistrate specially empowered by State Government or District Magistrate

Illustration:
A woman dies within 6 months of her marriage under suspicious circumstances. Police receive information. SHO immediately informs the Executive Magistrate, goes to the scene with two neighbours, investigates, and prepares an inquest report. Since it is a woman's death within 7 years of marriage and suspicion exists, the body is sent to the Civil Surgeon for post-mortem examination. All within 24 hours.

BNSS SECTION 195 - POWER TO SUMMON PERSONS
Core Content:
A police officer proceeding under section 194 may, by order in writing, summon two or more persons as witnesses for the investigation, and any other person who appears acquainted with the facts. Every person so summoned shall be bound to attend and to answer truly all questions other than self-incriminating questions. No male under 15, above 60, woman, mentally/physically disabled person, or person with acute illness shall be required to attend at any place other than their residence.

Procedure: Summoning Witnesses for Inquest

Police officer proceeding under section 194 may, by order in writing, summon:

(i) Two or more persons as aforesaid (respectable inhabitants of neighbourhood) for the purpose of the investigation

(ii) Any other person who appears to be acquainted with the facts of the case

Every person so summoned shall be bound to attend and to answer truly all questions other than questions the answers to which would have a tendency to expose him to a criminal charge or to a penalty or forfeiture

Protected persons: No male person under age of 15 years or above age of 60 years or a woman or a mentally or physically disabled person or a person with acute illness shall be required to attend at any place other than the place where such person resides

If such person is willing to attend and answer at the police station, they may be permitted so to do

If the facts do not disclose a cognizable offence to which section 190 applies, such persons shall not be required by the police officer to attend a Magistrate's Court

Illustration:
Police officer investigating a suspicious death summons two neighbours (both adult males) to witness the inquest and give information. A 75-year-old woman who witnessed the incident cannot be required to come to the police station - the officer must go to her residence to record her statement.

BNSS SECTION 196 - INQUIRY BY MAGISTRATE INTO CAUSE OF DEATH
Core Content:
When a person dies or disappears while in police or authorised custody, or rape is alleged to have been committed on a woman in such custody, an inquiry shall be held by the Magistrate within whose jurisdiction the offence has been committed (in addition to police investigation). The Magistrate shall record evidence and may cause the body to be disinterred and examined if necessary. Relatives of the deceased shall be informed and allowed to remain present at the inquiry.

Procedure: Magisterial Inquiry into Custodial Death/Disappearance/Rape

Mandatory Magistrate inquiry in following cases (in addition to police investigation):

(a) Any person dies or disappears while in custody of the police or in any other custody authorised by Magistrate or Court under BNSS

(b) Rape is alleged to have been committed on any woman while such woman is in custody of the police or in any other custody authorised by Magistrate or Court under BNSS

Inquiry shall be held by the Magistrate within whose local jurisdiction the offence has been committed

The Magistrate holding such inquiry shall record the evidence taken by him in connection therewith in any manner specified according to circumstances of the case

Whenever such Magistrate considers it expedient to make an examination of the dead body of any person who has been already interred (buried) in order to discover the cause of his death, the Magistrate may cause the body to be disinterred (dug up) and examined

Where an inquiry is to be held under this section, the Magistrate shall, wherever practicable, inform the relatives of the deceased whose names and addresses are known, and shall allow them to remain present at the inquiry

The Magistrate or Executive Magistrate or police officer holding an inquiry or investigation under sub-section (2) shall, within twenty-four hours of the death of a person, forward the body with a view to its being examined to the nearest Civil Surgeon or other qualified medical person appointed by State Government, unless it is not possible to do so for reasons to be recorded in writing

"Relative" means parents, children, brothers, sisters and spouse

Illustration:
A person dies in police custody. The law requires both a police investigation AND a Magistrate inquiry. The Magistrate informs the deceased's family (parents, spouse) and allows them to attend the inquiry. The Magistrate records evidence from police officers, witnesses, and the doctor. If the body has already been buried, the Magistrate can order it to be exhumed for further examination.

BNSS SECTION 197 - ORDINARY PLACE OF INQUIRY AND TRIAL
Core Content:
Every offence shall ordinarily be inquired into and tried by a Court within whose local jurisdiction it was committed.

Procedure: Determining Jurisdiction

The general rule is that an offence shall be tried by the Court in whose local jurisdiction the offence was committed

"Ordinarily" means this is the default rule, subject to exceptions provided in subsequent sections (198 to 205)

Illustration:
X commits a theft in Pune. The offence is ordinarily to be tried by a Court in Pune having jurisdiction over that area. The Delhi Court cannot try this offence simply because X lives in Delhi.

BNSS SECTION 198 - PLACE OF INQUIRY OR TRIAL
Core Content:
When it is uncertain in which of several local areas an offence was committed, or where an offence is committed partly in one area and partly in another, or where an offence is a continuing one and continues to be committed in more areas than one, or where it consists of several acts done in different local areas, it may be inquired into or tried by a Court having jurisdiction over any of such local areas.

Procedure: Multiple Jurisdiction Scenarios

Any of the following situations exist:

(a) It is uncertain in which of several local areas an offence was committed

(b) An offence is committed partly in one local area and partly in another

(c) An offence is a continuing one, and continues to be committed in more local areas than one

(d) An offence consists of several acts done in different local areas

The offence may be inquired into or tried by a Court having jurisdiction over any of such local areas

Illustration:
X fires a gun from Delhi side of the border and the bullet hits Y in Gurugram (Haryana). The offence is committed partly in Delhi, partly in Gurugram. The Court in either Delhi or Gurugram has jurisdiction. X sends threatening emails from Mumbai to Y in Chennai over several days - a continuing offence. Courts in Mumbai or Chennai both have jurisdiction.

BNSS SECTION 199 - OFFENCE TRIABLE WHERE ACT IS DONE OR CONSEQUENCE ENSUES
Core Content:
When an act is an offence by reason of anything which has been done and of a consequence which has ensued, the offence may be inquired into or tried by a Court within whose local jurisdiction such thing has been done or such consequence has ensued.

Procedure: Jurisdiction Based on Act or Consequence

An act is an offence because:

(i) Something has been done (the act), AND

(ii) A consequence has ensued (the result)

The offence may be inquired into or tried by a Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) Such thing has been done, OR

(ii) Such consequence has ensued

Illustration:
X from Kolkata sends a poisoned parcel to Y in Mumbai. Y receives it in Mumbai and dies. The act (sending poison) was done in Kolkata; the consequence (death) ensued in Mumbai. Courts in both Kolkata and Mumbai have jurisdiction to try X for murder.

BNSS SECTION 200 - PLACE OF TRIAL WHERE ACT IS AN OFFENCE BY REASON OF RELATION TO OTHER OFFENCE
Core Content:
When an act is an offence by reason of its relation to any other act which is also an offence or which would be an offence if the doer were capable of committing an offence, the first-mentioned offence may be inquired into or tried by a Court within whose local jurisdiction either act was done.

Procedure: Jurisdiction for Related Offences

Act A is an offence because of its relation to Act B

Act B is also an offence (or would be an offence if the doer were capable of committing an offence)

The first-mentioned offence (Act A) may be inquired into or tried by a Court within whose local jurisdiction either act was done

Illustration:
X abets Y to commit murder in Delhi. The abetment (Act A) happens in Noida. The murder (Act B) happens in Delhi. The abetment can be tried in either Noida or Delhi.

BNSS SECTION 201 - PLACE OF TRIAL IN CASE OF CERTAIN OFFENCES
Core Content:
Special jurisdiction rules apply to dacoity, kidnapping, theft, extortion, robbery, criminal misappropriation, criminal breach of trust, and offences involving stolen property. These may be tried where the offence was committed, where the accused is found, where the property was possessed, where the kidnapped person was conveyed or detained, or where the property was required to be returned or accounted for.

Procedure: Special Jurisdiction for Property and Kidnapping Offences

Dacoity, dacoity with murder, belonging to gang of dacoits, escaping from custody: May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction the offence was committed OR the accused person is found

Kidnapping or abduction: May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) The person was kidnapped or abducted, OR

(ii) The person was conveyed, OR

(iii) The person was concealed, OR

(iv) The person was detained

Theft, extortion, robbery: May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) The offence was committed, OR

(ii) The stolen property was possessed by any person committing it, OR

(iii) The stolen property was possessed by any person who received or retained it knowing or having reason to believe it to be stolen property

Criminal misappropriation or criminal breach of trust: May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) The offence was committed, OR

(ii) Any part of the property was received or retained, OR

(iii) Any part of the property was required to be returned or accounted for by the accused person

Offence including possession of stolen property: May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) The offence was committed, OR

(ii) The stolen property was possessed by any person who received or retained it knowing or having reason to believe it to be stolen property

Illustration:
X kidnaps a child from Delhi, takes her to Gurugram, keeps her in a house there, and later moves her to Noida. The kidnapping can be tried in Delhi, Gurugram, or Noida. Y steals a laptop from a shop in Pune and sells it to Z in Mumbai who knows it is stolen. The theft can be tried in Pune (where theft occurred) or Mumbai (where stolen property was possessed by Z).

BNSS SECTION 202 - OFFENCES COMMITTED BY MEANS OF ELECTRONIC COMMUNICATIONS, LETTERS, ETC.
Core Content:
Any offence which includes cheating may, if the deception is practised by means of electronic communications or letters or telecommunication messages, be inquired into or tried by any Court within whose local jurisdiction such electronic communications or letters or messages were sent or were received. Cheating and dishonestly inducing delivery of property may be tried where the property was delivered or was received.

Procedure: Jurisdiction for Electronic/Distance Offences

Cheating by electronic communication/letter/message: May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) Such electronic communications were sent, OR

(ii) Such letters were sent, OR

(iii) Such telecommunication messages were sent, OR

(iv) Such electronic communications were received, OR

(v) Such letters were received, OR

(vi) Such telecommunication messages were received

Cheating and dishonestly inducing delivery of property: May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) The property was delivered by the person deceived, OR

(ii) The property was received by the accused person

Offence under BNS section 82 (marrying again during lifetime of spouse): May be tried by Court within whose local jurisdiction:

(i) The offence was committed, OR

(ii) The offender last resided with his or her spouse by the first marriage, OR

(iii) The wife by the first marriage has taken up permanent residence after commission of the offence

Illustration:
X from Chennai sends a phishing email to Y in Bangalore. Y gets deceived and sends money to X's bank account in Mumbai. The cheating offence can be tried in Chennai (email sent), Bangalore (email received), or Mumbai (money received by accused).

BNSS SECTION 203 - OFFENCE COMMITTED ON JOURNEY OR VOYAGE
Core Content:
When an offence is committed whilst the person by or against whom, or the thing in respect of which, the offence is committed is in the course of performing a journey or voyage, the offence may be inquired into or tried by a Court through or into whose local jurisdiction that person or thing passed in the course of that journey or voyage.

Procedure: Jurisdiction for Offences During Travel

An offence is committed while:

(i) The person by whom the offence is committed is in the course of performing a journey or voyage, OR

(ii) The person against whom the offence is committed is in the course of performing a journey or voyage, OR

(iii) The thing in respect of which the offence is committed is in the course of performing a journey or voyage

The offence may be inquired into or tried by a Court through or into whose local jurisdiction that person or thing passed during that journey or voyage

Illustration:
X steals Y's wallet on a train travelling from Mumbai to Delhi. The train passes through Nashik, Bhopal, Jhansi, Agra, and Delhi. The theft can be tried by any Court in any of these cities. X murders Y on a ship from Chennai to Singapore while in Indian waters. The Court in Chennai (departure) or Port Blair (if passed through) may have jurisdiction.

BNSS SECTION 204 - PLACE OF TRIAL FOR OFFENCES TRIABLE TOGETHER
Core Content:
Where the offences committed by any person are such that he may be charged with and tried at one trial for each such offence by virtue of sections 242, 243, or 244, or where the offences committed by several persons are such that they may be charged with and tried together by virtue of section 246, the offences may be inquired into or tried by any Court competent to inquire into or try any of the offences.

Procedure: Jurisdiction for Joint Trial

Situation A: Offences committed by a single person are such that he may be charged with and tried at one trial for each offence under:

Section 242 (offences of same kind within year)

Section 243 (more than one offence in same transaction)

Section 244 (doubtful which offence committed)

Situation B: Offences committed by several persons are such that they may be charged with and tried together under section 246 (joint trial provisions)

The offences may be inquired into or tried by any Court competent to inquire into or try any of the offences

Illustration:
X commits theft in Delhi and fraud in Gurugram. These are offences of same kind within one year, so they can be tried together. The Delhi Court (competent for theft) can try both theft and fraud. The Gurugram Court (competent for fraud) can also try both. Y and Z commit robbery together in Noida and also commit dacoity together in Ghaziabad. Any Court in Noida or Ghaziabad can try both.

BNSS SECTION 205 - POWER TO ORDER CASES TO BE TRIED IN DIFFERENT SESSIONS DIVISIONS
Core Content:
Notwithstanding anything contained in the preceding provisions of this Chapter, the State Government may direct that any case or class of cases committed for trial in any district may be tried in any sessions division, provided that such direction is not repugnant to any direction previously issued by the High Court or the Supreme Court under the Constitution, or under BNSS or any other law.

Procedure: State Government Transfer of Sessions Cases

State Government has power to direct that any case or class of cases committed for trial in any district may be tried in any sessions division

This power exists notwithstanding anything in sections 197 to 204

Limitation: Such direction is not repugnant to any direction previously issued by:

(i) The High Court under the Constitution or under BNSS or any other law, OR

(ii) The Supreme Court under the Constitution

Illustration:
A high-profile murder case is committed for trial in District A. The State Government believes a fair trial cannot be held there due to local tensions. The State Government directs that the case be tried in sessions division of District B instead. This is valid as long as the High Court has not previously issued a contrary direction.

BNSS SECTION 206 - HIGH COURT TO DECIDE, IN CASE OF DOUBT, DISTRICT WHERE INQUIRY OR TRIAL SHALL TAKE PLACE
Core Content:
Where two or more Courts have taken cognizance of the same offence and a question arises as to which of them ought to inquire into or try that offence, the question shall be decided: (a) if the Courts are subordinate to the same High Court, by that High Court; (b) if the Courts are not subordinate to the same High Court, by the High Court within the local limits of whose appellate criminal jurisdiction the proceedings were first commenced. Thereupon all other proceedings in respect of that offence shall be discontinued.

Procedure: Resolving Jurisdictional Conflicts

Two or more Courts have taken cognizance of the same offence

A question arises as to which of them ought to inquire into or try that offence

If Courts are subordinate to the same High Court: The question shall be decided by that High Court

If Courts are not subordinate to the same High Court: The question shall be decided by the High Court within the local limits of whose appellate criminal jurisdiction the proceedings were first commenced

After the decision, all other proceedings in respect of that offence shall be discontinued

Illustration:
Both Delhi Court and Gurugram Court take cognizance of the same cheating case. Both are subordinate to Punjab and Haryana High Court. The High Court decides that Delhi Court should try the case. The Gurugram Court proceedings are discontinued. If Delhi Court (under Delhi High Court) and Mumbai Court (under Bombay High Court) both take cognizance, the High Court where proceedings were first commenced decides the issue.

BNSS SECTION 207 - POWER TO ISSUE SUMMONS OR WARRANT FOR OFFENCE COMMITTED BEYOND LOCAL JURISDICTION
Core Content:
When a Magistrate of the first class sees reason to believe that any person within his local jurisdiction has committed outside such jurisdiction (whether within or outside India) an offence which cannot be inquired into or tried within such jurisdiction but is triable in India, such Magistrate may inquire into the offence as if it had been committed within such jurisdiction, compel the person to appear, and send him to the Magistrate having jurisdiction, or take a bond for his appearance before such Magistrate.

Procedure: Magistrate's Power for Extra-Jurisdictional Offences

Magistrate of the first class sees reason to believe that any person within his local jurisdiction has committed outside such jurisdiction (whether within or outside India) an offence

Such offence cannot under sections 197 to 205 or any other law be inquired into or tried within such jurisdiction

Such offence is under any law for the time being in force triable in India

Such Magistrate may:

(i) Inquire into the offence as if it had been committed within such local jurisdiction

(ii) Compel such person to appear before him

(iii) Send such person to the Magistrate having jurisdiction to inquire into or try such offence, OR

(iv) If such offence is not punishable with death or imprisonment for life and such person is ready and willing to give bail, take a bond or bail bond for his appearance before the Magistrate having such jurisdiction

When there are more Magistrates than one having such jurisdiction and the Magistrate acting cannot satisfy himself as to which Magistrate to send or bind the person, the case shall be reported for the orders of the High Court

Illustration:
X is in Mumbai. Magistrate has reason to believe X committed an offence in Dubai which is triable in India (e.g., an Indian citizen committing crime abroad). The Mumbai Magistrate can inquire as if the offence happened in Mumbai, compel X to appear, and then send X to the Court in Delhi (which has jurisdiction over such matters) or take a bond from X to appear in Delhi Court.

BNSS SECTION 208 - OFFENCE COMMITTED OUTSIDE INDIA
Core Content:
When an offence is committed outside India by a citizen of India (whether on high seas or elsewhere), or by a person (not being such citizen) on any ship or aircraft registered in India, he may be dealt with in respect of such offence as if it had been committed at any place within India at which he may be found or where the offence is registered in India. No such offence shall be inquired into or tried in India except with the previous sanction of the Central Government.

Procedure: Jurisdiction over Offences Committed Abroad

Offence committed outside India in either of following circumstances:

(a) By a citizen of India, whether on the high seas or elsewhere, OR

(b) By a person (not being a citizen of India) on any ship or aircraft registered in India

Such person may be dealt with in respect of such offence as if it had been committed at any place within India at which he may be found or where the offence is registered in India

Sanction requirement: Notwithstanding anything in preceding sections, no such offence shall be inquired into or tried in India except with the previous sanction of the Central Government

Illustration:
X, an Indian citizen, commits murder in Dubai. He returns to India and is found in Mumbai. He can be tried in Mumbai as if the murder happened there. However, the trial cannot begin without prior sanction from the Central Government. A foreign national working on an Indian-registered ship commits theft while the ship is in international waters. He can be tried in India with Central Government sanction.

BNSS SECTION 209 - RECEIPT OF EVIDENCE RELATING TO OFFENCES COMMITTED OUTSIDE INDIA
Core Content:
When any offence alleged to have been committed in a territory outside India is being inquired into or tried under section 208, the Central Government may, if it thinks fit, direct that copies of depositions made or exhibits produced (either in physical form or in electronic form) before a judicial officer in or for that territory or before a diplomatic or consular representative of India in or for that territory shall be received as evidence by the Court holding such inquiry or trial in any case in which such Court might issue a commission for taking evidence.

Procedure: Using Foreign Evidence in Indian Courts

An offence alleged to have been committed in a territory outside India is being inquired into or tried under section 208

The Central Government may, if it thinks fit, direct that certain materials shall be received as evidence

Such materials include:

(i) Copies of depositions made before a judicial officer in or for that territory

(ii) Exhibits produced before a judicial officer in or for that territory

(iii) Copies of depositions made before a diplomatic or consular representative of India in or for that territory

(iv) Exhibits produced before a diplomatic or consular representative of India in or for that territory

Such materials may be in physical form or in electronic form

This applies in any case in which such Court might issue a commission for taking evidence

Illustration:
X, an Indian citizen, is being tried in Mumbai for murder committed in Dubai. The Central Government directs that the deposition of a witness recorded before an Indian consular officer in Dubai and the forensic report (electronic form) from Dubai police shall be received as evidence by the Mumbai Court. The Court can rely on these documents without issuing a commission to Dubai.

BNSS SECTION 210 - COGNIZANCE OF OFFENCES BY MAGISTRATE
Core Content:
Any Magistrate of the first class, and any Magistrate of the second class specially empowered by the Chief Judicial Magistrate, may take cognizance of any offence upon receiving a complaint of facts (including complaint filed by person authorised under special law) which constitutes such offence, or upon a police report (submitted in any mode including electronic mode) of such facts.

Procedure: Taking Cognizance

Magistrate of the first class may take cognizance of any offence

Magistrate of the second class may take cognizance only if specially empowered by Chief Judicial Magistrate under sub-section (2)

Cognizance can be taken in two ways:

(a) Upon receiving a complaint of facts (including complaint filed by a person authorised under any special law) which constitutes such offence

(b) Upon a police report (submitted in any mode including electronic mode) of such facts

The Chief Judicial Magistrate may empower any Magistrate of the second class to take cognizance of such offences as are within his competence to inquire into or try

Illustration:
A first class Magistrate receives a complaint from X about theft. He can take cognizance directly. A second class Magistrate can only take cognizance if the Chief Judicial Magistrate has specially empowered him to do so for that type of offence. A police report filed electronically is treated the same as a physical report for taking cognizance.

BNSS SECTION 211 - TRANSFER ON APPLICATION OF ACCUSED
Core Content:
When a Magistrate takes cognizance of an offence under clause (c) of section 210(1) (upon receiving a complaint of facts), the accused shall, before any evidence is taken, be informed that he is entitled to have the case inquired into or tried by another Magistrate. If the accused objects to further proceedings before the Magistrate taking cognizance, the case shall be transferred to such other Magistrate as the Chief Judicial Magistrate specifies.

Procedure: Accused's Right to Transfer

Magistrate takes cognizance of an offence under section 210(1)(c) (complaint case, not police report)

Before any evidence is taken, the accused shall be informed that he is entitled to have the case inquired into or tried by another Magistrate

If the accused (or any of the accused if more than one) objects to further proceedings before the Magistrate taking cognizance

The case shall be transferred to such other Magistrate as the Chief Judicial Magistrate specifies

Illustration:
A first class Magistrate takes cognizance of a complaint case against X. Before any evidence is recorded, the Magistrate informs X: "You have the right to have this case transferred to another Magistrate." X objects and requests transfer. The Chief Judicial Magistrate assigns the case to another first class Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 212 - MAKING OVER OF CASES TO MAGISTRATES
Core Content:
Any Chief Judicial Magistrate may, after taking cognizance of an offence, make over the case for inquiry or trial to any competent Magistrate subordinate to him. Any Magistrate of the first class empowered by the Chief Judicial Magistrate may, after taking cognizance, make over the case to such other competent Magistrate as the Chief Judicial Magistrate specifies.

Procedure: Assignment of Cases

Chief Judicial Magistrate takes cognizance of an offence

He may make over (assign) the case for inquiry or trial to any competent Magistrate subordinate to him

A Magistrate of the first class who has been empowered by the Chief Judicial Magistrate in this behalf:

(i) Takes cognizance of an offence

(ii) May make over the case for inquiry or trial to such other competent Magistrate as the Chief Judicial Magistrate specifies (by general or special order)

The other Magistrate may then hold the inquiry or trial

Illustration:
The Chief Judicial Magistrate takes cognizance of a large fraud case. Due to workload, he assigns it to a first class Magistrate subordinate to him for trial. A first class Magistrate empowered by CJM takes cognizance of a theft case and assigns it to a second class Magistrate as specified by the CJM.

BNSS SECTION 213 - COGNIZANCE OF OFFENCES BY COURT OF SESSION
Core Content:
Except as otherwise expressly provided by BNSS or by any other law for the time being in force, no Court of Session shall take cognizance of any offence as a Court of original jurisdiction unless the case has been committed to it by a Magistrate under BNSS.

Procedure: Session Court Cognizance

General rule: Court of Session cannot take cognizance of an offence directly as a Court of original jurisdiction

Exception: If BNSS or any other law expressly provides otherwise

The case must first be committed (sent) to the Court of Session by a Magistrate under BNSS

Only after such commitment can the Court of Session take cognizance

Illustration:
A murder case (exclusively triable by Court of Session) is filed before a Magistrate. The Magistrate conducts committal proceedings and commits the case to the Court of Session. The Sessions Judge then takes cognizance. The Sessions Judge cannot directly take cognizance of the murder case without the Magistrate's committal order.

BNSS SECTION 214 - ADDITIONAL SESSIONS JUDGES TO TRY CASES MADE OVER TO THEM
Core Content:
An Additional Sessions Judge shall try such cases as the Sessions Judge of the division may, by general or special order, make over to him for trial or as the High Court may, by special order, direct him to try.

Procedure: Assignment to Additional Sessions Judge

Sessions Judge of the division may by general or special order make over cases to Additional Sessions Judge for trial

High Court may by special order direct an Additional Sessions Judge to try a particular case

The Additional Sessions Judge shall try those cases so assigned

Illustration:
The Sessions Judge of Pune division makes a general order: "All theft cases committed to Session Court shall be made over to Additional Sessions Judge A." Or a special order: "Case No. 123/2024 is made over to Additional Sessions Judge B." The High Court may also direct: "Additional Sessions Judge C shall try the XYZ murder case."

BNSS SECTION 215 - PROSECUTION FOR CONTEMPT OF LAWFUL AUTHORITY OF PUBLIC SERVANTS, FOR OFFENCES AGAINST PUBLIC JUSTICE AND FOR OFFENCES RELATING TO DOCUMENTS GIVEN IN EVIDENCE
Core Content:
No Court shall take cognizance of offences under BNS sections 206-223 (excluding section 209), or abetment/attempt/criminal conspiracy thereof, except on complaint in writing of the public servant concerned or his administrative superior or authorised person. For offences under sections 229-233, 236, 237, 242-248, 267 committed in or in relation to court proceedings, or offences under sections 336(1), 340(2), 342 committed in respect of documents in court proceedings, cognizance requires complaint in writing of that Court or its authorised officer.

Procedure: Complaint Required for Specified Offences

Offences against public servants (BNS 206-223 excluding 209), their abetment, attempt, or criminal conspiracy:

Cognizance only on complaint in writing of:

(i) The public servant concerned, OR

(ii) Some other public servant to whom he is administratively subordinate, OR

(iii) Some other public servant authorised by the concerned public servant

Offences in relation to Court proceedings (BNS 229-233, 236, 237, 242-248, 267) or offences under BNS 336(1), 340(2), 342 regarding documents in Court, or criminal conspiracy/attempt/abetment thereof:

Cognizance only on complaint in writing of:

(i) That Court, OR

(ii) Such officer of the Court as that Court may authorise in writing, OR

(iii) Some other Court to which that Court is subordinate

Illustration:
A person threatens a public servant (BNS section 224). The Court cannot take cognizance unless the public servant himself files a written complaint. A witness gives false evidence in Court (BNS section 229). The Court cannot take cognizance unless the Court itself (or its authorised officer) files a written complaint.

BNSS SECTION 216 - PROCEDURE FOR WITNESSES IN CASE OF THREATENING, ETC.
Core Content:
A witness or any other person may file a complaint in relation to an offence under section 232 of the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023.

Procedure: Complaint for Threatening Witness

Section 232 of BNS deals with threatening any person to give false evidence

A witness who has been threatened may file a complaint

Any other person who has knowledge of such threatening may also file a complaint

Illustration:
X, a witness in a murder trial, is threatened by Y to give false evidence. X can directly file a complaint before the Magistrate. A neighbour who overheard the threat can also file a complaint on X's behalf.

BNSS SECTION 217 - PROSECUTION FOR OFFENCES AGAINST STATE AND FOR CRIMINAL CONSPIRACY TO COMMIT SUCH OFFENCE
Core Content:
No Court shall take cognizance of offences under Chapter VII (offences against State) or sections 196, 299, 353(1) of BNS, or criminal conspiracy/abetment thereof, except with previous sanction of Central Government or State Government. For sections 197, 353(2)(3), sanction of Central/State Government or District Magistrate required. For criminal conspiracy under BNS section 61(2) (other than those punishable with death/life/2+ years rigorous imprisonment), consent of State Government or District Magistrate in writing required.

Procedure: Sanction for State Offences

Offences under Chapter VII (waging war, sedition, etc.), BNS 196 (promoting enmity), 299 (outraging religious feelings), 353(1) (false statement causing mutiny), and criminal conspiracy/abetment thereof:

Cognizance only with previous sanction of Central Government OR State Government

Offences under BNS 197 (imputations prejudicial to national integration), 353(2)(3) (false statement creating enmity in place of worship):

Cognizance only with previous sanction of Central Government OR State Government OR District Magistrate

Criminal conspiracy under BNS 61(2) (punishable with death/life/2+ years rigorous imprisonment):

Cognizance only with consent in writing of State Government or District Magistrate

Exception: If section 215 applies (complaint by Court/public servant), no consent necessary

Preliminary investigation: Central/State Government or District Magistrate may, before according sanction/consent, order preliminary investigation by police officer not below Inspector, who shall have powers under section 174(3)

Illustration:
X is accused of waging war against India (Chapter VII offence). Court cannot take cognizance without Central Government sanction. Y is accused of criminal conspiracy to commit murder (BNS 61(2)). District Magistrate's written consent is required before cognizance.

BNSS SECTION 218 - PROSECUTION OF JUDGES AND PUBLIC SERVANTS
Core Content:
No Court shall take cognizance of any offence alleged to have been committed by a Judge, Magistrate, or public servant not removable from office save by or with sanction of Government, while acting or purporting to act in discharge of official duty, except with previous sanction of Central Government (for Union employees) or State Government (for State employees). Such Government shall take a decision within 120 days from receipt of request; if it fails, sanction shall be deemed to have been accorded. No sanction required for certain sexual offences, trafficking, etc. under BNS.

Procedure: Sanction for Prosecuting Public Servants

Who is covered: Any person who is or was:

(i) A Judge or Magistrate

(ii) A public servant not removable from office save by or with sanction of Government

Accused of any offence alleged to have been committed while acting or purporting to act in discharge of official duty

Sanction authority:

(a) For Union government employees: Central Government

(b) For State government employees: State Government

Deemed sanction (120-day rule): Such Government shall take a decision within 120 days from date of receipt of request for sanction. If it fails to do so, sanction shall be deemed to have been accorded by such Government

No sanction required for certain offences under BNS: Sections 64-71, 74-79, 143, 199, 200 (sexual offences, trafficking, certain other offences) - prosecution can proceed without sanction

Armed Forces: For members of Armed Forces acting in discharge of official duty, cognizance only with previous sanction of Central Government (or State Government for State forces as notified)

Illustration:
A police officer (public servant) is accused of assault during arrest. The prosecution must obtain State Government sanction. The State Government receives the request on Jan 1. If no decision by April 30 (120 days), sanction is deemed granted. If the officer is accused of rape (BNS section 64), no sanction is required at all.

BNSS SECTION 219 - PROSECUTION FOR OFFENCES AGAINST MARRIAGE
Core Content:
No Court shall take cognizance of offences under BNS sections 81-84 (offences relating to marriage) except upon complaint by some person aggrieved by the offence. Special provisions allow complaints by others on behalf of child, person of unsound mind, disabled person, or woman who ought not to appear in public, with leave of Court. For husband in armed forces, authorised person may complain. For BNS section 64 (rape of wife under 18), cognizance barred if more than one year has elapsed.

Procedure: Complaint Required for Marriage Offences

General rule: Cognizance of BNS sections 81-84 (marriage offences) only on complaint by some person aggrieved by the offence

Complaint by others with Court leave (Proviso (a)): Where aggrieved person is:

(i) a child, OR

(ii) of unsound mind, OR

(iii) having intellectual disability requiring higher support needs, OR

(iv) from sickness or infirmity unable to make complaint, OR

(v) a woman who according to local customs ought not to be compelled to appear in public

→ Some other person may, with leave of Court, make complaint on his/her behalf

Complaint for husband in armed forces (Proviso (b)): Where husband is serving in Armed Forces and his Commanding Officer certifies he cannot obtain leave to make complaint in person, some other person authorised by husband may make complaint

Complaint for wife under BNS 82 (Proviso (c)): Complaint may be made on wife's behalf by her father, mother, brother, sister, son, daughter, father's/mother's brother/sister, or with Court leave, any other person related by blood/marriage/adoption

Person aggrieved for BNS 84: Only the husband of the woman shall be deemed to be aggrieved by BNS 84 (enticing married woman)

Limitation for BNS 64 (rape of wife under 18): No Court shall take cognizance if more than one year has elapsed from date of commission of the offence

Illustration:
X commits bigamy (BNS 82). His first wife can file a complaint. If the wife is in a coma, her brother can apply to Court for leave to file complaint on her behalf. If X rapes his own wife who is 17 years old (BNS 64), the complaint must be filed within 1 year of the incident, otherwise Court cannot take cognizance.
