BNSS SECTION 220 - PROSECUTION OF OFFENCES UNDER SECTION 85 OF BHARATIYA NYAYA SANHITA, 2023
Core Content:
No Court shall take cognizance of an offence punishable under section 85 of BNS (cruelty against married woman) except upon a police report of facts which constitute such offence or upon a complaint made by the person aggrieved by the offence or by her father, mother, brother, sister, father's/mother's brother/sister, or with leave of Court, by any other person related to her by blood, marriage or adoption.

Procedure: Complaint for Cruelty Against Married Woman

Section 85 BNS deals with subjecting a married woman to cruelty (dowry harassment, etc.)

Cognizance only upon:

(i) A police report of facts which constitute such offence, OR

(ii) A complaint made by the person aggrieved (the woman herself), OR

(iii) Complaint by her father, mother, brother, sister, or father's/mother's brother/sister, OR

(iv) With leave of Court, by any other person related to her by blood, marriage or adoption

Illustration:
A married woman is subjected to cruelty by her husband for dowry. She can file a complaint. If she is unable to do so, her mother can file a complaint. If none of these relatives are available, any other blood relative can apply to the Court for leave to file a complaint on her behalf.

BNSS SECTION 221 - COGNIZANCE OF OFFENCE
Core Content:
No Court shall take cognizance of an offence punishable under section 67 of the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023 where the persons are in a marital relationship, except upon prima facie satisfaction of the facts which constitute the offence upon a complaint having been filed or made by the wife against the husband.

Procedure: Cognizance of Sexual Intercourse by Husband During Separation (BNS 67)

BNS section 67 deals with sexual intercourse by husband with his wife during separation (judicial separation or separation by mutual agreement)

Where the persons are in a marital relationship

No Court shall take cognizance except:

(i) Upon prima facie satisfaction of the facts which constitute the offence

(ii) Upon a complaint having been filed or made by the wife against the husband

Illustration:
A husband and wife are living separately under a judicial separation order. The husband forces sexual intercourse on the wife. The wife files a complaint. The Magistrate, upon being prima facie satisfied that the facts constitute the offence, can take cognizance. No one else (e.g., parents, police on their own) can initiate this prosecution - only the wife can file the complaint.

BNSS SECTION 222 - PROSECUTION FOR DEFAMATION
Core Content:
No Court shall take cognizance of defamation (BNS 356) except upon complaint by person aggrieved, with exceptions for child, person of unsound mind, disabled, or woman who ought not to appear in public (with Court leave). For defamation against President, Vice-President, Governor, Administrator, or Minister in respect of public functions, Court of Session may take cognizance directly upon complaint by Public Prosecutor with previous sanction of State Government or Central Government, within six months from the date of offence.

Procedure: Defamation Prosecution

General rule: Cognizance of BNS 356 (defamation) only on complaint by some person aggrieved by the offence

Complaint by others with Court leave (Proviso): Where aggrieved person is child, of unsound mind, intellectually disabled, sick/infirm unable to complain, or woman who ought not to appear in public, some other person may with Court leave make complaint

Special procedure for high dignitaries (sub-section (2)): When defamation is alleged against:

President of India, Vice-President of India, Governor of a State, Administrator of a Union territory, or a Minister of Union/State/Union territory

In respect of his conduct in discharge of public functions

A Court of Session may take cognizance directly (without committal) upon complaint in writing by Public Prosecutor

Sanction for Public Prosecutor complaint (sub-section (4)): Public Prosecutor can make such complaint only with previous sanction:

(a) of State Government for Governor or State Minister, or other State public servant

(b) of Central Government in any other case

Limitation (sub-section (5)): Complaint must be made within six months from date on which offence is alleged to have been committed

Complainant's right unaffected (sub-section (6)): Nothing affects right of the defamed person to make complaint before Magistrate having jurisdiction

Illustration:
X defames the President of India in a speech. The Public Prosecutor, with Central Government sanction, can file a complaint directly before the Court of Session within 6 months. The defamed President can also file a regular complaint before a Magistrate. If a common citizen is defamed, only the defamed person (or authorised representative) can file complaint before Magistrate.

BNSS SECTION 223 - EXAMINATION OF COMPLAINANT
Core Content:
A Magistrate having jurisdiction while taking cognizance of an offence on complaint shall examine upon oath the complainant and the witnesses present, if any. The substance of such examination shall be reduced to writing and signed by the complainant, the witnesses, and the Magistrate. No cognizance shall be taken without giving the accused an opportunity of being heard. For complaint against public servant for official acts, the public servant must be given opportunity to make assertions and a report from his superior officer must be received.

Procedure: Examination of Complainant

Magistrate having jurisdiction takes cognizance of an offence on complaint

Magistrate shall examine upon oath:

(i) The complainant

(ii) The witnesses present, if any

The substance of such examination shall be reduced to writing

Shall be signed by:

(i) The complainant

(ii) The witnesses

(iii) The Magistrate

Mandatory hearing to accused: No cognizance of an offence shall be taken by the Magistrate without giving the accused an opportunity of being heard

Exceptions where examination of complainant/witnesses not required:

(a) If a public servant acting or purporting to act in discharge of official duties OR a Court has made the complaint

(b) If the Magistrate makes over the case for inquiry or trial to another Magistrate under section 212

If Magistrate makes over case to another Magistrate under section 212 after examining complainant and witnesses, the latter Magistrate need not re-examine them

Complaint against public servant for official acts (sub-section (2)): Magistrate shall not take cognizance unless:

(a) Such public servant is given an opportunity to make assertions as to the situation that led to the incident so alleged

(b) A report containing facts and circumstances of the incident from the officer superior to such public servant is received

Illustration:
X files a complaint of theft against Y before a Magistrate. The Magistrate examines X on oath, writes down X's statement, and X signs it. The Magistrate gives Y an opportunity to be heard before taking cognizance. If a police officer (public servant) is accused of assault during arrest, the Magistrate must first get a report from the officer's superior and give the officer a chance to explain before taking cognizance.

BNSS SECTION 224 - PROCEDURE BY MAGISTRATE NOT COMPETENT TO TAKE COGNIZANCE OF CASE
Core Content:
If the complaint is made to a Magistrate who is not competent to take cognizance of the offence, he shall: (a) if the complaint is in writing, return it for presentation to the proper Court with an endorsement to that effect; (b) if the complaint is not in writing, direct the complainant to the proper Court.

Procedure: Return of Complaint

Complaint is made to a Magistrate

Such Magistrate is not competent to take cognizance of the offence

If complaint is in writing: Magistrate shall return it for presentation to the proper Court with an endorsement to that effect

If complaint is not in writing: Magistrate shall direct the complainant to the proper Court

Illustration:
X files a written complaint about a murder (exclusively triable by Court of Session) before a second class Magistrate who has no jurisdiction. The Magistrate endorses "Returned - present before Court of Session" and returns the complaint to X. X then presents it to the proper Court.

BNSS SECTION 225 - POSTPONEMENT OF ISSUE OF PROCESS
Core Content:
Any Magistrate, on receipt of a complaint of an offence of which he is authorised to take cognizance or which has been made over to him, may if he thinks fit postpone issue of process and either inquire into the case himself or direct investigation by police officer or other person. No such direction for investigation shall be made where it appears to the Magistrate that the offence is triable exclusively by Court of Session. In an inquiry, if offence is triable exclusively by Court of Session, he shall call upon complainant to produce all his witnesses and examine them on oath.

Procedure: Pre-Process Inquiry/Investigation

Magistrate receives complaint of an offence of which:

(i) He is authorised to take cognizance, OR

(ii) Which has been made over to him under section 212

Magistrate may, if he thinks fit, postpone issue of process against the accused

And either:

(i) Inquire into the case himself, OR

(ii) Direct an investigation to be made by a police officer or by such other person as he thinks fit

Purpose: To decide whether or not there is sufficient ground for proceeding

Prohibition on investigation direction: No such direction for investigation shall be made where it appears to the Magistrate that the offence complained of is triable exclusively by the Court of Session

In an inquiry under sub-section (1), Magistrate may, if he thinks fit, take evidence of witnesses on oath

If offence exclusively triable by Court of Session: Magistrate shall call upon the complainant to produce all his witnesses and examine them on oath

If investigation is made by a person not being a police officer, such person shall have for that investigation all the powers conferred by BNSS on an officer in charge of a police station except the power to arrest without warrant

Illustration:
Magistrate receives a complaint of cheating. He is unsure if there is sufficient ground. He postpones issuing summons to accused and instead directs a police officer to investigate. After receiving the investigation report, he decides whether to issue process. If the complaint alleges murder (exclusively Session Court triable), he cannot direct police investigation - he must examine all complainant's witnesses himself.

BNSS SECTION 226 - DISMISSAL OF COMPLAINT
Core Content:
If, after considering the statements on oath (if any) of the complainant and of the witnesses and the result of the inquiry or investigation (if any) under section 225, the Magistrate is of opinion that there is no sufficient ground for proceeding, he shall dismiss the complaint, and in every such case he shall briefly record his reasons for so doing.

Procedure: Dismissal of Complaint

Magistrate has considered:

(i) The statements on oath (if any) of the complainant

(ii) The statements on oath (if any) of the witnesses

(iii) The result of the inquiry or investigation (if any) under section 225

Magistrate is of opinion that there is no sufficient ground for proceeding

Magistrate shall dismiss the complaint

Magistrate shall briefly record his reasons for doing so

Illustration:
Magistrate examines complainant X and his witnesses. The statements are contradictory and lack credibility. The police investigation under section 225 finds no evidence. Magistrate records: "Complainant's statements inconsistent with witness statements. No corroborating evidence found. Complaint dismissed." X can challenge this dismissal.

This completes Sections 223 to 226 (Chapter XVI - Complaints to Magistrates).

BNSS SECTION 227 - ISSUE OF PROCESS
Core Content:
If in the opinion of a Magistrate taking cognizance of an offence there is sufficient ground for proceeding, and the case appears to be a summons-case, he shall issue summons to the accused; if a warrant-case, he may issue a warrant or summons. Summons or warrants may also be issued through electronic means. No summons or warrant shall be issued until a list of prosecution witnesses has been filed. In a complaint case, every summons or warrant shall be accompanied by a copy of the complaint.

Procedure: Issuing Process

Magistrate taking cognizance of an offence is of opinion there is sufficient ground for proceeding

If case is summons-case: Magistrate shall issue summons to the accused for his attendance

If case is warrant-case: Magistrate may issue a warrant, or if he thinks fit, a summons, for causing the accused to be brought or to appear

Summons or warrants may also be issued through electronic means

No summons or warrant shall be issued against the accused until a list of the prosecution witnesses has been filed

In a proceeding instituted upon a complaint made in writing, every summons or warrant shall be accompanied by a copy of such complaint

If any process-fees or other fees are payable by law, no process shall be issued until the fees are paid. If such fees are not paid within a reasonable time, the Magistrate may dismiss the complaint

Nothing in this section affects the provisions of section 90 (issue of warrant in lieu of summons)

Illustration:
Magistrate finds sufficient ground to proceed against X for theft (warrant-case). He issues summons to X to appear. The summons includes a copy of the complaint filed by Y. X receives it electronically via email. X appears on the specified date.

BNSS SECTION 228 - MAGISTRATE MAY DISPENSE WITH PERSONAL ATTENDANCE OF ACCUSED
Core Content:
Whenever a Magistrate issues a summons, he may, if he sees reason so to do, dispense with the personal attendance of the accused and permit him to appear by his advocate. But the Magistrate inquiring into or trying the case may, in his discretion, at any stage of the proceedings, direct the personal attendance of the accused, and if necessary, enforce such attendance.

Procedure: Appearance by Advocate

Magistrate issues a summons

Magistrate sees reason to dispense with personal attendance of accused

Magistrate may permit the accused to appear by his advocate

However: The Magistrate inquiring into or trying the case may, in his discretion, at any stage of the proceedings, direct the personal attendance of the accused

If necessary, enforce such attendance

Illustration:
X is a busy doctor summoned in a minor case. Magistrate permits X to appear through his lawyer. However, on the trial date, the Magistrate decides X's personal presence is needed for identification. The Magistrate directs X to attend personally and enforces it.

BNSS SECTION 229 - SPECIAL SUMMONS IN CASES OF PETTY OFFENCE
Core Content:
If in the opinion of a Magistrate taking cognizance of a petty offence (punishable only with fine not exceeding ₹5,000, excluding Motor Vehicles Act offences), the case may be summarily disposed of, the Magistrate shall issue summons requiring the accused either to appear in person/by advocate, or to plead guilty by transmitting plea in writing and the amount of fine specified. The amount of fine specified shall not exceed ₹5,000. State Government may specially empower any Magistrate to exercise this power for compoundable offences or offences punishable with imprisonment up to 3 months where fine only would meet the ends of justice.

Procedure: Petty Offence Summons

Magistrate taking cognizance of a petty offence

Magistrate is of opinion the case may be summarily disposed of under section 283 or 284

Magistrate shall (except where he records reasons for contrary opinion) issue summons to the accused

Summons shall require the accused to either:

(i) Appear in person or by advocate before Magistrate on specified date, OR

(ii) If he desires to plead guilty without appearing, transmit before specified date by post or messenger his plea in writing and the amount of fine specified in the summons, OR

(iii) If he desires to appear by advocate and plead guilty through such advocate, authorise in writing the advocate to plead guilty on his behalf and pay fine through such advocate

Amount of fine specified in such summons shall not exceed ₹5,000

"Petty offence" means any offence punishable only with fine not exceeding ₹5,000, but does not include any offence so punishable under Motor Vehicles Act, 1988 or any other law which provides for convicting accused in his absence on a plea of guilty

State Government may by notification specially empower any Magistrate to exercise these powers for:

Any offence which is compoundable under section 359, OR

Any offence punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding three months, or with fine, or with both

Where Magistrate is of opinion that imposition of fine only would meet the ends of justice

Illustration:
X is summoned for a petty traffic offence (fine ₹500). The summons says: "Appear on March 1, OR send ₹500 by post with a written plea of guilty." X sends ₹500 by post with a letter saying "I plead guilty." Magistrate convicts X in absentia. No need for X to travel to court.

BNSS SECTION 230 - SUPPLY TO ACCUSED OF COPY OF POLICE REPORT AND OTHER DOCUMENTS
Core Content:
In a case instituted on a police report, the Magistrate shall without delay, and in no case beyond fourteen days from the date of production or appearance of the accused, furnish to the accused and the victim (if represented by an advocate) free of cost, copies of the police report, FIR, statements recorded under section 180, confessions and statements under section 183, and other documents forwarded with the police report. Supply of documents in electronic form shall be considered duly furnished.

Procedure: Supply of Documents (Section 207 CrPC equivalent)

Proceeding has been instituted on a police report

Magistrate shall without delay furnish to the accused and victim (if represented by an advocate) free of cost

Time limit: in no case beyond fourteen days from the date of production or appearance of the accused

Documents to be furnished:

(i) The police report

(ii) The first information report recorded under section 173

(iii) The statements recorded under section 180(3) of all persons whom the prosecution proposes to examine as its witnesses (excluding any part for which police officer requested exclusion under section 193(7))

(iv) The confessions and statements, if any, recorded under section 183

(v) Any other document or relevant extract forwarded to the Magistrate with the police report under section 193(6)

If Magistrate peruses a part of a statement for which exclusion was requested, he may direct that a copy of that part or such portion as he thinks proper shall be furnished to the accused

If any document is voluminous, Magistrate may instead of furnishing a copy:

Furnish copies through electronic means, OR

Direct that the accused/victim will only be allowed to inspect it either personally or through an advocate in Court

Supply of documents in electronic form shall be considered as duly furnished

Illustration:
X is produced before Magistrate on a police report for theft. Within 14 days, the Magistrate provides X with copies of the FIR, police report, statements of 5 witnesses, and X's confession (if any). All documents are sent by email. X's lawyer reviews them.

BNSS SECTION 231 - SUPPLY OF COPIES OF STATEMENTS AND DOCUMENTS TO ACCUSED IN OTHER CASES TRIABLE BY COURT OF SESSION
Core Content:
Where, in a case instituted otherwise than on a police report (complaint case), it appears to the Magistrate issuing process under section 227 that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session, the Magistrate shall forthwith furnish to the accused, free of cost, copies of statements recorded under section 223 or 225, statements and confessions recorded under section 180 or 183, and any documents produced before the Magistrate on which prosecution proposes to rely. For voluminous documents, inspection may be allowed instead of copies.

Procedure: Supply of Documents in Complaint Cases Committed to Session Court

Case instituted otherwise than on a police report (complaint case)

Magistrate issues process under section 227

It appears to the Magistrate that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session

Magistrate shall forthwith furnish to the accused, free of cost:

(i) The statements recorded under section 223 or section 225, of all persons examined by the Magistrate

(ii) The statements and confessions, if any, recorded under section 180 or section 183

(iii) Any documents produced before the Magistrate on which the prosecution proposes to rely

If any document is voluminous, Magistrate may instead of furnishing a copy:

Direct that the accused will only be allowed to inspect it either personally or through an advocate in Court

Supply of documents in electronic form shall be considered as duly furnished

Illustration:
X is accused in a complaint case of murder (exclusively Session Court triable). Magistrate issues process and immediately provides X with copies of all statements recorded during the complaint inquiry, any confession recorded by Magistrate, and all documents relied upon by prosecution. The documents are sent electronically.

BNSS SECTION 232 - COMMITMENT OF CASE TO COURT OF SESSION WHEN OFFENCE IS TRIABLE EXCLUSIVELY BY IT
Core Content:
When in a case instituted on a police report or otherwise, the accused appears or is brought before the Magistrate and it appears that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session, the Magistrate shall commit the case to the Court of Session after complying with section 230 or 231, remand the accused to custody, send the record and documents/articles to the Session Court, and notify the Public Prosecutor. Proceedings shall be completed within 90 days from taking cognizance, extendable to 180 days for reasons recorded.

Procedure: Committal to Session Court

In a case instituted on a police report or otherwise, the accused appears or is brought before the Magistrate

It appears to the Magistrate that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session

Magistrate shall:

(a) After complying with section 230 (police report cases) or section 231 (complaint cases), commit the case to the Court of Session

(b) Subject to bail provisions, remand the accused to custody until such commitment has been made and until conclusion of trial

(c) Send to that Court the record of the case and the documents and articles, if any, which are to be produced in evidence

(d) Notify the Public Prosecutor of the commitment of the case to the Court of Session

Time limit for committal proceedings: Proceedings under this section shall be completed within a period of 90 days from the date of taking cognizance

Such period may be extended by the Magistrate for a period not exceeding 180 days (total) for reasons to be recorded in writing

Any application filed before the Magistrate by the accused or the victim or any person authorised by such person in a case triable by Court of Session shall be forwarded to the Court of Session with the committal of the case

Illustration:
X is accused of murder (exclusively Session Court triable). Magistrate takes cognizance on Jan 1. X is produced. Magistrate provides documents under section 230, commits the case to Session Court by March 31 (within 90 days), and sends all records to Sessions Judge. X remains in custody. An application filed by X before Magistrate is forwarded to Session Court along with the committal order.

BNSS SECTION 233 - PROCEDURE TO BE FOLLOWED WHEN THERE IS A COMPLAINT CASE AND POLICE INVESTIGATION IN RESPECT OF SAME OFFENCE
Core Content:
When in a complaint case it is made to appear that a police investigation is in progress in relation to the same offence, the Magistrate shall stay the proceedings and call for a report from the police officer. If a police report is filed and cognizance is taken against any accused in the complaint case, the Magistrate shall inquire into or try both together as if instituted on a police report. If the police report does not relate to any accused in the complaint case or cognizance is not taken, the Magistrate shall proceed with the stayed complaint case.

Procedure: Overlapping Complaint and Police Investigation

A case instituted otherwise than on a police report (complaint case) is pending

During the course of inquiry or trial, it is made to appear to the Magistrate that an investigation by the police is in progress in relation to the same offence

Magistrate shall:

(i) Stay the proceedings of such inquiry or trial

(ii) Call for a report on the matter from the police officer conducting the investigation

If police report is filed under section 193 and cognizance is taken against any person who is an accused in the complaint case:

Magistrate shall inquire into or try together the complaint case and the case arising out of the police report

As if both the cases were instituted on a police report

If police report does not relate to any accused in the complaint case OR Magistrate does not take cognizance of any offence on the police report:

Magistrate shall proceed with the inquiry or trial which was stayed

In accordance with the provisions of BNSS

Illustration:
X files a complaint case against Y for assault. The Magistrate learns that police are also investigating the same incident. Magistrate stays the complaint case and asks police for a report. Police file charge sheet against Y. Magistrate now tries both the complaint case and the police case together as if both were police cases. If police file charge sheet against Z (not Y), Magistrate proceeds with X's complaint case against Y.

BNSS CHAPTER XVII: COMMENCEMENT OF PROCEEDINGS BEFORE MAGISTRATES (Sections 227-233)
SECTION 227 - ISSUE OF PROCESS
Core Content:
If in the opinion of a Magistrate taking cognizance of an offence there is sufficient ground for proceeding, and the case appears to be a summons-case, he shall issue summons to the accused for his attendance; if a warrant-case, he may issue a warrant, or if he thinks fit, a summons, for causing the accused to be brought or to appear at a certain time before such Magistrate or (if he has no jurisdiction himself) some other Magistrate having jurisdiction. Summons or warrants may also be issued through electronic means.

Procedure:

Magistrate taking cognizance of an offence is of opinion there is sufficient ground for proceeding

If case is summons-case: Magistrate shall issue summons to the accused for his attendance

If case is warrant-case: Magistrate may issue a warrant, OR if he thinks fit, a summons

Summons or warrants may be issued through electronic means

No summons or warrant shall be issued until a list of the prosecution witnesses has been filed

In a proceeding instituted upon a complaint made in writing, every summons or warrant issued shall be accompanied by a copy of such complaint

If any process-fees or other fees are payable by law, no process shall be issued until the fees are paid. If such fees are not paid within a reasonable time, the Magistrate may dismiss the complaint

Nothing in this section shall be deemed to affect the provisions of section 90 (issue of warrant in lieu of or in addition to summons)

Illustration:
Magistrate finds sufficient ground to proceed against X for theft (warrant-case). He issues summons to X to appear. The summons includes a copy of the complaint filed by Y. X receives it electronically via email. X appears on the specified date.

SECTION 228 - MAGISTRATE MAY DISPENSE WITH PERSONAL ATTENDANCE OF ACCUSED
Core Content:
Whenever a Magistrate issues a summons, he may, if he sees reason so to do, dispense with the personal attendance of the accused and permit him to appear by his advocate. But the Magistrate inquiring into or trying the case may, in his discretion, at any stage of the proceedings, direct the personal attendance of the accused, and if necessary, enforce such attendance.

Procedure:

Magistrate issues a summons

Magistrate sees reason to dispense with personal attendance of accused

Magistrate may permit the accused to appear by his advocate

However: The Magistrate inquiring into or trying the case may, in his discretion, at any stage of the proceedings, direct the personal attendance of the accused

If necessary, enforce such attendance

Illustration:
X is a busy doctor summoned in a minor case. Magistrate permits X to appear through his lawyer. However, on the trial date, the Magistrate decides X's personal presence is needed for identification. The Magistrate directs X to attend personally and enforces it.

SECTION 229 - SPECIAL SUMMONS IN CASES OF PETTY OFFENCE
Core Content:
If, in the opinion of a Magistrate taking cognizance of a petty offence, the case may be summarily disposed of, the Magistrate shall, except where he is for reasons to be recorded in writing of a contrary opinion, issue summons to the accused requiring him either to appear in person or by an advocate before the Magistrate on a specified date, or if he desires to plead guilty to the charge without appearing, to transmit before the specified date by post or by messenger to the Magistrate the said plea in writing and the amount of fine specified in the summons.

Procedure:

Magistrate taking cognizance of a petty offence

Magistrate is of opinion the case may be summarily disposed of under section 283 or 284

Magistrate shall (except where he records reasons for contrary opinion) issue summons to the accused

Summons shall require the accused to either:

(i) Appear in person or by advocate before Magistrate on specified date, OR

(ii) If he desires to plead guilty without appearing, transmit before specified date by post or messenger his plea in writing and the amount of fine specified in the summons, OR

(iii) If he desires to appear by advocate and plead guilty through such advocate, authorise in writing the advocate to plead guilty on his behalf and pay fine through such advocate

Amount of fine specified in such summons shall not exceed ₹5,000

"Petty offence" means any offence punishable only with fine not exceeding ₹5,000, but does not include any offence so punishable under Motor Vehicles Act, 1988 or any other law which provides for convicting accused in his absence on a plea of guilty

State Government may by notification specially empower any Magistrate to exercise these powers for:

Any offence which is compoundable under section 359, OR

Any offence punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding three months, or with fine, or with both

Where Magistrate is of opinion that imposition of fine only would meet the ends of justice

Illustration:
X is summoned for a petty traffic offence (fine ₹500). The summons says: "Appear on March 1, OR send ₹500 by post with a written plea of guilty." X sends ₹500 by post with a letter saying "I plead guilty." Magistrate convicts X in absentia. No need for X to travel to court.

SECTION 230 - SUPPLY TO ACCUSED OF COPY OF POLICE REPORT AND OTHER DOCUMENTS
Core Content:
In any case where the proceeding has been instituted on a police report, the Magistrate shall without delay, and in no case beyond fourteen days from the date of production or appearance of the accused, furnish to the accused and the victim (if represented by an advocate) free of cost, a copy of each of the following: the police report, the FIR recorded under section 173, the statements recorded under section 180 of all persons whom the prosecution proposes to examine as its witnesses, the confessions and statements recorded under section 183, and any other document or relevant extract forwarded to the Magistrate with the police report under section 193.

Procedure:

Proceeding has been instituted on a police report

Magistrate shall without delay furnish to the accused and victim (if represented by an advocate) free of cost

Time limit: in no case beyond fourteen days from the date of production or appearance of the accused

Documents to be furnished:

(i) The police report

(ii) The first information report recorded under section 173

(iii) The statements recorded under section 180(3) of all persons whom the prosecution proposes to examine as its witnesses (excluding any part for which police officer requested exclusion under section 193(7))

(iv) The confessions and statements, if any, recorded under section 183

(v) Any other document or relevant extract forwarded to the Magistrate with the police report under section 193(6)

If Magistrate peruses a part of a statement for which exclusion was requested, he may direct that a copy of that part or such portion thereof as the Magistrate thinks proper shall be furnished to the accused

If any document is voluminous, Magistrate may instead of furnishing a copy:

Furnish copies through electronic means, OR

Direct that the accused/victim will only be allowed to inspect it either personally or through an advocate in Court

Supply of documents in electronic form shall be considered as duly furnished

Key Time Limit: 14 days from production/appearance of accused

Illustration:
X is produced before Magistrate on a police report for theft. Within 14 days, the Magistrate provides X with copies of the FIR, police report, statements of 5 witnesses, and X's confession (if any). All documents are sent by email. X's lawyer reviews them.

SECTION 231 - SUPPLY OF COPIES OF STATEMENTS AND DOCUMENTS TO ACCUSED IN OTHER CASES TRIABLE BY COURT OF SESSION
Core Content:
Where, in a case instituted otherwise than on a police report (complaint case), it appears to the Magistrate issuing process under section 227 that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session, the Magistrate shall forthwith furnish to the accused, free of cost, a copy of the statements recorded under section 223 or section 225 of all persons examined by the Magistrate, the statements and confessions recorded under section 180 or section 183, and any documents produced before the Magistrate on which the prosecution proposes to rely.

Procedure:

Case instituted otherwise than on a police report (complaint case)

Magistrate issues process under section 227

It appears to the Magistrate that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session

Magistrate shall forthwith furnish to the accused, free of cost:

(i) The statements recorded under section 223 or section 225, of all persons examined by the Magistrate

(ii) The statements and confessions, if any, recorded under section 180 or section 183

(iii) Any documents produced before the Magistrate on which the prosecution proposes to rely

If any document is voluminous, Magistrate may instead of furnishing a copy:

Direct that the accused will only be allowed to inspect it either personally or through an advocate in Court

Supply of documents in electronic form shall be considered as duly furnished

Illustration:
X is accused in a complaint case of murder (exclusively Session Court triable). Magistrate issues process and immediately provides X with copies of all statements recorded during the complaint inquiry, any confession recorded by Magistrate, and all documents relied upon by prosecution. The documents are sent electronically.

SECTION 232 - COMMITMENT OF CASE TO COURT OF SESSION WHEN OFFENCE IS TRIABLE EXCLUSIVELY BY IT
Core Content:
When in a case instituted on a police report or otherwise, the accused appears or is brought before the Magistrate and it appears to the Magistrate that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session, he shall commit the case to the Court of Session after complying with the provisions of section 230 or section 231, remand the accused to custody, send to that Court the record of the case and the documents and articles to be produced in evidence, and notify the Public Prosecutor of the commitment. Proceedings shall be completed within 90 days from taking cognizance, extendable to 180 days.

Procedure:

In a case instituted on a police report or otherwise, the accused appears or is brought before the Magistrate

It appears to the Magistrate that the offence is triable exclusively by the Court of Session

Magistrate shall:

(a) After complying with section 230 (police report cases) or section 231 (complaint cases), commit the case to the Court of Session

(b) Subject to bail provisions, remand the accused to custody until such commitment has been made and until conclusion of trial

(c) Send to that Court the record of the case and the documents and articles, if any, which are to be produced in evidence

(d) Notify the Public Prosecutor of the commitment of the case to the Court of Session

Time limit for committal proceedings: Proceedings under this section shall be completed within a period of 90 days from the date of taking cognizance

Such period may be extended by the Magistrate for a period not exceeding 180 days (total) for reasons to be recorded in writing

Any application filed before the Magistrate by the accused or the victim or any person authorised by such person in a case triable by Court of Session shall be forwarded to the Court of Session with the committal of the case

Key Time Limit: 90 days (extendable to 180 days)

Illustration:
X is accused of murder (exclusively Session Court triable). Magistrate takes cognizance on Jan 1. X is produced. Magistrate provides documents under section 230, commits the case to Session Court by March 31 (within 90 days), and sends all records to Sessions Judge. X remains in custody. An application filed by X before Magistrate is forwarded to Session Court along with the committal order.

SECTION 233 - PROCEDURE TO BE FOLLOWED WHEN THERE IS A COMPLAINT CASE AND POLICE INVESTIGATION IN RESPECT OF SAME OFFENCE
Core Content:
When in a case instituted otherwise than on a police report (complaint case), it is made to appear to the Magistrate during the course of the inquiry or trial held by him that an investigation by the police is in progress in relation to the same offence, the Magistrate shall stay the proceedings of such inquiry or trial and call for a report on the matter from the police officer conducting the investigation.

Procedure:

A case instituted otherwise than on a police report (complaint case) is pending

During the course of inquiry or trial, it is made to appear to the Magistrate that an investigation by the police is in progress in relation to the same offence

Magistrate shall:

(i) Stay the proceedings of such inquiry or trial

(ii) Call for a report on the matter from the police officer conducting the investigation

If police report is filed under section 193 and cognizance is taken against any person who is an accused in the complaint case:

Magistrate shall inquire into or try together the complaint case and the case arising out of the police report

As if both the cases were instituted on a police report

If police report does not relate to any accused in the complaint case OR Magistrate does not take cognizance of any offence on the police report:

Magistrate shall proceed with the inquiry or trial which was stayed

In accordance with the provisions of BNSS

Illustration:
X files a complaint case against Y for assault. The Magistrate learns that police are also investigating the same incident. Magistrate stays the complaint case and asks police for a report. Police file charge sheet against Y. Magistrate now tries both the complaint case and the police case together as if both were police cases. If police file charge sheet against Z (not Y), Magistrate proceeds with X's complaint case against Y.

BNSS CHAPTER XVIII: THE CHARGE (Sections 234-247)
SECTION 234 - CONTENTS OF CHARGE
Core Content:
Every charge under this Sanhita shall state the offence with which the accused is charged. If the law which creates the offence gives it any specific name, the offence may be described in the charge by that name only. If the law does not give it any specific name, so much of the definition of the offence must be stated as to give the accused notice of the matter with which he is charged. The law and section of the law against which the offence is said to have been committed shall be mentioned in the charge. The fact that the charge is made is equivalent to a statement that every legal condition required by law to constitute the offence charged was fulfilled in the particular case. The charge shall be written in the language of the Court. If the accused, having been previously convicted of any offence, is liable to enhanced punishment, the fact, date and place of the previous conviction shall be stated in the charge.

Procedure:

Charge shall state the offence with which accused is charged

If law gives specific name, offence may be described by that name only

If law does not give specific name, state so much of definition as gives accused notice

Mention law and section

Charge in language of Court

If previous conviction for enhanced punishment, state fact, date, place. Court may add at any time before sentence

Illustrations:

A charged with murder → equivalent to statement that A's act fell within definition of murder, did not fall within general exceptions, etc.

A charged under section 118(2) BNS with voluntarily causing grievous hurt by instrument for shooting → equivalent to statement that case not provided for by section 122(2) BNS and general exceptions did not apply

Charge may state "A committed murder" without reference to definitions, but sections must be referred to

SECTION 235 - PARTICULARS AS TO TIME, PLACE AND PERSON
Core Content:
The charge shall contain such particulars as to the time and place of the alleged offence, and the person (if any) against whom, or the thing (if any) in respect of which, it was committed, as are reasonably sufficient to give the accused notice of the matter with which he is charged. When the accused is charged with criminal breach of trust or dishonest misappropriation of money or other movable property, it shall be sufficient to specify the gross sum or describe the movable property and the dates between which the offence is alleged to have been committed, without specifying particular items or exact dates. The time included between the first and last of such dates shall not exceed one year.

Procedure:

State time, place, person, thing as sufficient to give accused notice

For criminal breach of trust/dishonest misappropriation: specify gross sum/describe property and dates between (period not exceeding 1 year) - deemed one offence under section 242

Key Time Limit: Period between first and last dates not exceeding 1 year

SECTION 236 - WHEN MANNER OF COMMITTING OFFENCE MUST BE STATED
Core Content:
When the nature of the case is such that the particulars mentioned in sections 234 and 235 do not give the accused sufficient notice of the matter with which he is charged, the charge shall also contain such particulars of the manner in which the alleged offence was committed as will be sufficient for that purpose.

Illustrations:

(a) Theft of article at certain time and place - charge need not set out manner

(b) Cheating B at given time and place - charge must set out manner

(c) Giving false evidence at given time and place - charge must set out portion of evidence alleged false

(d) Obstructing public servant - charge must set out manner

(e) Murder - charge need not state manner

(f) Disobeying direction of law with intent to save B from punishment - charge must set out disobedience and law infringed

SECTION 237 - WORDS IN CHARGE TAKEN IN SENSE OF LAW UNDER WHICH OFFENCE IS PUNISHABLE
Core Content:
In every charge words used in describing an offence shall be deemed to have been used in the sense attached to them respectively by the law under which such offence is punishable.

SECTION 238 - EFFECT OF ERRORS
Core Content:
No error in stating either the offence or the particulars required to be stated in the charge, and no omission to state the offence or those particulars, shall be regarded at any stage of the case as material, unless the accused was in fact misled by such error or omission, and it has occasioned a failure of justice.

Illustrations:

(a) A charged with possession of counterfeit coin, "fraudulently" omitted - not material unless A misled

(b) A charged with cheating B, manner not set out - A defends himself, calls witnesses - not material

(c) A charged with cheating B, manner not set out - many transactions between A and B, A had no means to know which charge referred - material error

(d) A charged with murder of Khoda Baksh on 21st Jan - actual name Haidar Baksh, date 20th Jan - A never charged with any murder but one, heard inquiry exclusive to Haidar Baksh - not material

(e) A charged with murdering Haidar Baksh on 20th Jan and Khoda Baksh on 21st Jan - tried for murder of Khoda Baksh when charged for Haidar Baksh - material error

SECTION 239 - COURT MAY ALTER CHARGE
Core Content:
Any Court may alter or add to any charge at any time before judgment is pronounced. Every such alteration or addition shall be read and explained to the accused. If the alteration or addition to a charge is such that proceeding immediately with the trial is not likely to prejudice the accused or the prosecutor, the Court may proceed with the trial as if the altered or added charge had been the original charge. If it is likely to prejudice, the Court may either direct a new trial or adjourn the trial. If the altered or added charge requires previous sanction, the case shall not be proceeded with until such sanction is obtained.

Procedure:

Alter/add any time before judgment

Read and explain to accused

If not likely to prejudice - proceed with trial

If likely to prejudice - direct new trial or adjourn

If altered charge requires previous sanction - not proceed until sanction obtained (unless already had for same facts)

SECTION 240 - RECALL OF WITNESSES WHEN CHARGE ALTERED
Core Content:
Whenever a charge is altered or added to by the Court after the commencement of the trial, the prosecutor and the accused shall be allowed to recall or re-summon, and examine with reference to such alteration or addition, any witness who may have been examined (unless the Court considers it for vexation or delay), and also to call any further witness whom the Court may think to be material.

Procedure:

Charge altered/added after trial commencement

Prosecutor and accused allowed:

(a) recall/resummon and examine any witness already examined (unless Court considers for vexation/delay/defeating justice)

(b) call any further witness Court thinks material

SECTION 241 - SEPARATE CHARGES FOR DISTINCT OFFENCES
Core Content:
For every distinct offence of which any person is accused there shall be a separate charge, and every such charge shall be tried separately. Exception: where the accused person, by an application in writing, so desires and the Magistrate is of opinion that such person is not likely to be prejudiced thereby, the Magistrate may try together all or any number of the charges framed against such person.

Procedure:

Separate charge for each distinct offence

Separate trial for each charge

Exception: accused applies in writing, Magistrate of opinion no prejudice → may try together

Illustration:
A is accused of theft on one occasion and causing grievous hurt on another occasion. A must be separately charged and separately tried for theft and causing grievous hurt.

SECTION 242 - OFFENCES OF SAME KIND WITHIN YEAR MAY BE CHARGED TOGETHER
Core Content:
When a person is accused of more offences than one of the same kind committed within the space of twelve months from the first to the last of such offences, whether in respect of the same person or not, he may be charged with, and tried at one trial for, any number of them not exceeding five. Offences are of the same kind when they are punishable with the same amount of punishment under the same section of BNS or of any special or local law.

Procedure:

Offences of same kind (same punishment under same section)

Committed within 12 months from first to last

May be charged and tried together for any number not exceeding five

SECTION 243 - TRIAL FOR MORE THAN ONE OFFENCE
Core Content:
If, in one series of acts so connected together as to form the same transaction, more offences than one are committed by the same person, he may be charged with, and tried at one trial for, every such offence. When a person charged with criminal breach of trust or dishonest misappropriation is accused of committing falsification of accounts for facilitating or concealing that offence, he may be charged with and tried at one trial for every such offence. If acts constitute an offence falling within two or more separate definitions, the person may be charged with and tried at one trial for each. If several acts, singly or combined, constitute different offences, the person may be charged with and tried for the combined offence and for any constituent offence.

Procedure:

Same transaction: one series of connected acts → may charge and try all offences at one trial

Criminal breach of trust/dishonest misappropriation + falsification of accounts to facilitate/conceal → may charge and try together

Acts falling within two or more separate definitions → may charge and try each offence

Several acts which singly or combined constitute different offence → may charge for combined offence and for constituent offences

Illustrations to sub-section (1):

(a) A rescues B from lawful custody, causing grievous hurt to constable C → may be charged with offences under section 121(2) and section 263 BNS

(b) A commits house-breaking with intent to commit rape, and commits rape → may be separately charged with offences under section 64 and section 331(3) BNS

SECTION 244 - WHERE IT IS DOUBTFUL WHAT OFFENCE HAS BEEN COMMITTED
Core Content:
If a single act or series of acts is of such a nature that it is doubtful which of several offences the facts which can be proved will constitute, the accused may be charged with having committed all or any of such offences, and any number of such charges may be tried at once; or he may be charged in the alternative. If in such a case the accused is charged with one offence, and it appears in evidence that he committed a different offence for which he might have been charged, he may be convicted of the offence which he is shown to have committed, although he was not charged with it.

Procedure:

Doubtful which of several offences facts constitute

May charge with all or any, or in alternative

If charged with one offence but evidence shows different offence for which could have been charged → may be convicted of that offence

Illustrations:

(a) Act may amount to theft, or receiving stolen property, or criminal breach of trust, or cheating → may be charged with all, or in alternative

(b) A only charged with theft, evidence shows criminal breach of trust or receiving stolen goods → may be convicted of criminal breach of trust or receiving stolen goods

(c) A states before Magistrate he saw B hit C with club; before Sessions Court states B never hit C → may be charged in alternative and convicted of intentionally giving false evidence

SECTION 245 - WHEN OFFENCE PROVED INCLUDED IN OFFENCE CHARGED
Core Content:
When a person is charged with an offence consisting of several particulars, a combination of some only of which constitutes a complete minor offence, and such combination is proved, he may be convicted of the minor offence. When facts are proved which reduce the offence to a minor offence, he may be convicted of the minor offence. When charged with an offence, he may be convicted of an attempt to commit such offence although the attempt is not separately charged.

Procedure:

Offence with several particulars, combination of some = complete minor offence proved → may convict of minor offence

Facts reduce offence to minor offence → may convict of minor offence

May convict of attempt (though attempt not separately charged)

Cannot convict of minor offence if conditions for initiation of proceedings for that minor offence not satisfied

Illustrations:

(a) A charged under section 316(3) BNS with criminal breach of trust as carrier. Evidence shows criminal breach of trust under section 316(2) but not as carrier → may be convicted under section 316(2)

(b) A charged under section 117(2) BNS with causing grievous hurt. He proves grave and sudden provocation → may be convicted under section 122(2) BNS

SECTION 246 - WHAT PERSONS MAY BE CHARGED JOINTLY
Core Content:
The following persons may be charged and tried together: (a) persons accused of the same offence committed in the course of the same transaction; (b) persons accused of an offence and persons accused of abetment of, or attempt to commit, such offence; (c) persons accused of more than one offence of the same kind committed by them jointly within twelve months; (d) persons accused of different offences committed in the course of the same transaction; (e) persons accused of theft/extortion/cheating/criminal misappropriation and persons accused of receiving/retaining/assisting in disposal of property transferred by such offence; (f) persons accused of offences under sections 317(2) and 317(5) BNS in respect of same stolen property; (g) persons accused of any offence under Chapter X BNS relating to counterfeit coin and persons accused of any other offence under that Chapter relating to the same coin.

Procedure: As above categories. Also, if persons charged with separate offences not falling in categories, may by written application and if Court satisfied no prejudice and expedient, try all together.

SECTION 247 - WITHDRAWAL OF REMAINING CHARGES ON CONVICTION ON ONE OF SEVERAL CHARGES
Core Content:
When a charge containing more heads than one is framed against the same person, and when a conviction has been had on one or more of them, the complainant, or the officer conducting the prosecution, may, with the consent of the Court, withdraw the remaining charge or charges, or the Court of its own accord may stay the inquiry into, or trial of, such charge or charges. Such withdrawal shall have the effect of an acquittal on such charge or charges, unless the conviction be set aside, in which case the Court may proceed with the inquiry into, or trial of, the charge or charges so withdrawn.

Procedure:

Conviction on one or more heads of charge

With Court consent, complainant/prosecutor may withdraw remaining charges

OR Court may stay inquiry/trial on remaining charges

Withdrawal = acquittal on those charges unless conviction set aside (then may proceed)

BNSS CHAPTER XIX: TRIAL BEFORE A COURT OF SESSION (Sections 248-260)
SECTION 248 - TRIAL TO BE CONDUCTED BY PUBLIC PROSECUTOR
Core Content:
In every trial before a Court of Session, the prosecution shall be conducted by a Public Prosecutor.

SECTION 249 - OPENING CASE FOR PROSECUTION
Core Content:
When the accused appears or is brought before the Court, in pursuance of a commitment of the case under section 232, or under any other law for the time being in force, the prosecutor shall open his case by describing the charge brought against the accused and stating by what evidence he proposes to prove the guilt of the accused.

SECTION 250 - DISCHARGE
Core Content:
The accused may prefer an application for discharge within a period of sixty days from the date of commitment of the case under section 232. If, upon consideration of the record of the case and the documents submitted therewith, and after hearing the submissions of the accused and the prosecution in this behalf, the Judge considers that there is not sufficient ground for proceeding against the accused, he shall discharge the accused and record his reasons for so doing.

Key Time Limit: 60 days from date of commitment

Procedure:

Accused may apply for discharge within 60 days from commitment under section 232

Judge considers record, documents, hears submissions

If no sufficient ground, discharge with reasons

SECTION 251 - FRAMING OF CHARGE
Core Content:
If, after such consideration and hearing as aforesaid, the Judge is of opinion that there is ground for presuming that the accused has committed an offence which is not exclusively triable by the Court of Session, he may frame a charge against the accused and transfer the case to the Chief Judicial Magistrate or any other Judicial Magistrate of the first class. If the offence is exclusively triable by the Court, he shall frame in writing a charge within a period of sixty days from the date of first hearing on charge. The charge shall be read and explained to the accused present either physically or through audio-video electronic means and the accused shall be asked whether he pleads guilty of the offence charged or claims to be tried.

Key Time Limit: 60 days from first hearing on charge

Procedure:

Judge considers record, documents, hears submissions

If offence not exclusively Session Court triable: frame charge, transfer to CJM/first class Magistrate

If offence exclusively Session Court triable: frame written charge within 60 days from first hearing on charge

Charge read and explained to accused (physically or by audio-video)

Ask: "Do you plead guilty or claim trial?"

SECTION 252 - CONVICTION ON PLEA OF GUILTY
Core Content:
If the accused pleads guilty, the Judge shall record the plea and may, in his discretion, convict him thereon.

SECTION 253 - DATE FOR PROSECUTION EVIDENCE
Core Content:
If the accused refuses to plead, or does not plead, or claims to be tried or is not convicted under section 252, the Judge shall fix a date for the examination of witnesses, and may, on the application of the prosecution, issue any process for compelling the attendance of any witness or the production of any document or other thing.

SECTION 254 - EVIDENCE FOR PROSECUTION
Core Content:
On the date so fixed, the Judge shall proceed to take all such evidence as may be produced in support of the prosecution. Evidence of a witness may be recorded by audio-video electronic means. The deposition of evidence of any public servant may be taken through audio-video electronic means. The Judge may, in his discretion, permit the cross-examination of any witness to be deferred until any other witness or witnesses have been examined or recall any witness for further cross-examination.

Procedure:

On fixed date, take all prosecution evidence

Evidence may be recorded by audio-video electronic means

Public servant's deposition may be by audio-video electronic means

Judge may defer cross-examination until other witnesses examined, or recall witness for further cross-examination

SECTION 255 - ACQUITTAL
Core Content:
If, after taking the evidence for the prosecution, examining the accused and hearing the prosecution and the defence on the point, the Judge considers that there is no evidence that the accused committed the offence, the Judge shall record an order of acquittal.

SECTION 256 - ENTERING UPON DEFENCE
Core Content:
Where the accused is not acquitted under section 255, he shall be called upon to enter on his defence and adduce any evidence he may have in support thereof. If the accused puts in any written statement, the Judge shall file it with the record. If the accused applies for the issue of any process for compelling the attendance of any witness or the production of any document or thing, the Judge shall issue such process unless he considers, for reasons to be recorded, that such application should be refused on the ground that it is made for the purpose of vexation or delay or for defeating the ends of justice.

Procedure:

Accused called upon to enter defence and adduce evidence

Written statement filed with record

Accused applies for process for witnesses/documents → Judge shall issue unless refuses for vexation/delay/defeating justice (reasons recorded)

SECTION 257 - ARGUMENTS
Core Content:
When the examination of the witnesses (if any) for the defence is complete, the prosecutor shall sum up his case and the accused or his advocate shall be entitled to reply. Where any point of law is raised by the accused or his advocate, the prosecution may, with the permission of the Judge, make his submissions with regard to such point of law.

SECTION 258 - JUDGMENT OF ACQUITTAL OR CONVICTION
Core Content:
After hearing arguments and points of law (if any), the Judge shall give a judgment in the case, as soon as possible, within a period of thirty days from the date of completion of arguments, which may be extended to a period of forty-five days for reasons to be recorded in writing. If the accused is convicted, the Judge shall, unless he proceeds in accordance with the provisions of section 401, hear the accused on the questions of sentence, and then pass sentence on him according to law.

Key Time Limit: 30 days from completion of arguments; extendable to 45 days

SECTION 259 - PREVIOUS CONVICTION
Core Content:
In a case where a previous conviction is charged under the provisions of sub-section (7) of section 234, and the accused does not admit that he has been previously convicted as alleged in the charge, the Judge may, after he has convicted the said accused under section 252 or section 258, take evidence in respect of the alleged previous conviction, and shall record a finding thereon. No such charge shall be read out by the Judge nor shall the accused be asked to plead thereto nor shall the previous conviction be referred to by the prosecution or in any evidence adduced by it, unless and until the accused has been convicted under section 252 or section 258.

SECTION 260 - PROCEDURE IN CASES INSTITUTED UNDER SUB-SECTION (2) OF SECTION 222
Core Content:
A Court of Session taking cognizance of an offence under sub-section (2) of section 222 (defamation against President, Vice-President, Governor, Administrator, or Minister in respect of public functions) shall try the case in accordance with the procedure for the trial of warrant-cases instituted otherwise than on a police report before a Court of Magistrate. The person against whom the offence is alleged to have been committed shall, unless the Court otherwise directs, be examined as a witness for the prosecution. Every trial under this section shall be held in camera if either party desires or if the Court thinks fit. If the Court discharges or acquits the accused and is of opinion that there was no reasonable cause for making the accusation, it may order the complainant (except high dignitaries) to pay compensation up to five thousand rupees.

Procedure:

Session Court takes cognizance under section 222(2)

Try as warrant-case (non-police report) before Magistrate

Person against whom offence alleged (except President, VP, Governor, Administrator) examined as prosecution witness unless Court otherwise directs

Trial in camera if either party desires or Court thinks fit

If discharged/acquitted and no reasonable cause, Court may order complainant (except high dignitaries) to show cause why compensation not paid

If satisfied no reasonable cause, order compensation up to ₹5,000 to accused

Compensation recovered as fine

Person ordered to pay may appeal to High Court (only re compensation)

BNSS CHAPTER XX: TRIAL OF WARRANT-CASES BY MAGISTRATES (Sections 261-273)
SECTION 261 - COMPLIANCE WITH SECTION 230
Core Content:
When, in any warrant-case instituted on a police report, the accused appears or is brought before a Magistrate at the commencement of the trial, the Magistrate shall satisfy himself that he has complied with the provisions of section 230.

SECTION 262 - WHEN ACCUSED SHALL BE DISCHARGED
Core Content:
The accused may prefer an application for discharge within a period of sixty days from the date of supply of copies of documents under section 230. If, upon considering the police report and the documents sent with it under section 193 and making such examination, if any, of the accused, either physically or through audio-video electronic means, as the Magistrate thinks necessary and after giving the prosecution and the accused an opportunity of being heard, the Magistrate considers the charge against the accused to be groundless, he shall discharge the accused, and record his reasons for so doing.

Key Time Limit: 60 days from supply of documents under section 230

Procedure:

Accused may apply for discharge within 60 days from supply of documents under section 230

Magistrate considers police report, section 193 documents, examines accused (physically or by audio-video)

Gives prosecution and accused opportunity to be heard

If charge groundless, discharge with reasons

SECTION 263 - FRAMING OF CHARGE
Core Content:
If, upon such consideration, examination, if any, and hearing, the Magistrate is of opinion that there is ground for presuming that the accused has committed an offence triable under this Chapter, which such Magistrate is competent to try and which, in his opinion, could be adequately punished by him, he shall frame in writing a charge against the accused within a period of sixty days from the date of first hearing on charge. The charge shall then be read and explained to the accused, and he shall be asked whether he pleads guilty of the offence charged or claims to be tried.

Key Time Limit: 60 days from first hearing on charge

Procedure:

Magistrate considers, examines, hears

Opinion: ground to presume accused committed offence triable under Chapter XX, competent to try, adequately punishable

Frame written charge within 60 days from first hearing on charge

Read and explain to accused

Ask: "Do you plead guilty or claim trial?"

SECTION 264 - CONVICTION ON PLEA OF GUILTY
Core Content:
If the accused pleads guilty, the Magistrate shall record the plea and may, in his discretion, convict him thereon.

SECTION 265 - EVIDENCE FOR PROSECUTION
Core Content:
If the accused refuses to plead or does not plead, or claims to be tried or the Magistrate does not convict the accused under section 264, the Magistrate shall fix a date for the examination of witnesses. The Magistrate shall supply in advance to the accused the statement of witnesses recorded during investigation by the police. The Magistrate may, on the application of the prosecution, issue a summons to any of its witnesses directing him to attend or to produce any document or other thing. On the date so fixed, the Magistrate shall proceed to take all such evidence as may be produced in support of the prosecution. The Magistrate may permit the cross-examination of any witness to be deferred or recall any witness. The examination of a witness may be done by audio-video electronic means at the designated place to be notified by the State Government.

Procedure:

Accused refuses to plead, does not plead, claims trial, or not convicted under section 264

Magistrate fixes date for examination of witnesses

Supply in advance to accused statements of witnesses recorded during investigation

On prosecution application, issue summons to witnesses

On fixed date, take all prosecution evidence

May defer cross-examination or recall witnesses

Examination may be by audio-video electronic means at designated place notified by State Government

SECTION 266 - EVIDENCE FOR DEFENCE
Core Content:
The accused shall then be called upon to enter upon his defence and produce his evidence; and if the accused puts in any written statement, the Magistrate shall file it with the record. If the accused, after he has entered upon his defence, applies to the Magistrate to issue any process for compelling the attendance of any witness for the purpose of examination or cross-examination, or the production of any document or other thing, the Magistrate shall issue such process unless he considers that such application should be refused on the ground that it is made for the purpose of vexation or delay or for defeating the ends of justice and such ground shall be recorded by him in writing. When the accused has cross-examined or had the opportunity of cross-examining any witness before entering on his defence, the attendance of such witness shall not be compelled unless the Magistrate is satisfied that it is necessary for the ends of justice. The examination of a witness may be done by audio-video electronic means at the designated place to be notified by the State Government. The Magistrate may, before summoning any witness, require that the reasonable expenses incurred by the witness be deposited in Court.

Procedure:

Accused called upon to enter defence and produce evidence

Written statement filed with record

Accused applies for process for witnesses/documents → Magistrate shall issue unless refuses for vexation/delay/defeating justice (reasons recorded)

If witness already cross-examined before defence, attendance not compelled unless necessary for justice

Examination may be by audio-video electronic means at designated place

Magistrate may require deposit of reasonable expenses before summoning witness

SECTION 267 - EVIDENCE FOR PROSECUTION (Non-Police Report Cases)
Core Content:
When, in any warrant-case instituted otherwise than on a police report, the accused appears or is brought before a Magistrate, the Magistrate shall proceed to hear the prosecution and take all such evidence as may be produced in support of the prosecution. The Magistrate may, on the application of the prosecution, issue a summons to any of its witnesses directing him to attend or to produce any document or other thing.

SECTION 268 - WHEN ACCUSED SHALL BE DISCHARGED (Non-Police Report)
Core Content:
If, upon taking all the evidence referred to in section 267, the Magistrate considers, for reasons to be recorded, that no case against the accused has been made out which, if unrebutted, would warrant his conviction, the Magistrate shall discharge him. Nothing in this section shall be deemed to prevent a Magistrate from discharging the accused at any previous stage of the case if, for reasons to be recorded, he considers the charge to be groundless.

SECTION 269 - PROCEDURE WHERE ACCUSED IS NOT DISCHARGED (Non-Police Report)
Core Content:
If, when such evidence has been taken, or at any previous stage of the case, the Magistrate is of opinion that there is ground for presuming that the accused has committed an offence triable under this Chapter, which such Magistrate is competent to try and which, in his opinion, could be adequately punished by him, he shall frame in writing a charge against the accused. The charge shall then be read and explained to the accused, and he shall be asked whether he pleads guilty or has any defence to make. If the accused pleads guilty, the Magistrate shall record the plea, and may, in his discretion, convict him thereon. If the accused refuses to plead, or does not plead or claims to be tried or if the accused is not convicted, he shall be required to state, at the commencement of the next hearing, whether he wishes to cross-examine any, and if so, which, of the witnesses for the prosecution whose evidence has been taken. If he says he does so wish, the witnesses named by him shall be recalled and, after cross-examination and re-examination, they shall be discharged. The evidence of any remaining witnesses for the prosecution shall next be taken, and after cross-examination and re-examination, they shall also be discharged. Where, despite giving opportunity to the prosecution and after taking all reasonable measures, if the attendance of the prosecution witnesses cannot be secured for cross-examination, it shall be deemed that such witness has not been examined for not being available, and the Magistrate may close the prosecution evidence for reasons to be recorded in writing and proceed with the case on the basis of the materials on record.

Procedure:

Magistrate frames written charge

Read and explained to accused

Ask: "Do you plead guilty or have defence to make?"

If pleads guilty, may convict

If refuses/does not plead/claims trial/not convicted → accused required to state if he wishes to cross-examine any prosecution witness whose evidence taken

If yes, those witnesses recalled, cross-examined, discharged

Remaining prosecution witnesses examined, cross-examined, discharged

If attendance cannot be secured for cross-examination despite reasonable measures, deemed witness not examined, Magistrate may close prosecution evidence with reasons

SECTION 270 - EVIDENCE FOR DEFENCE (Non-Police Report)
Core Content:
The accused shall then be called upon to enter upon his defence and produce his evidence; and the provisions of section 266 shall apply to the case.

SECTION 271 - ACQUITTAL OR CONVICTION
Core Content:
If, in any case under this Chapter in which a charge has been framed, the Magistrate finds the accused not guilty, he shall record an order of acquittal. Where the Magistrate finds the accused guilty, but does not proceed in accordance with the provisions of section 364 or section 401, he shall, after hearing the accused on the question of sentence, pass sentence upon him according to law. Where a previous conviction is charged under section 234(7) and the accused does not admit it, the Magistrate may, after he has convicted the said accused, take evidence in respect of the alleged previous conviction, and shall record a finding thereon. No such charge shall be read out nor shall the accused be asked to plead thereto nor shall the previous conviction be referred to by the prosecution unless and until the accused has been convicted.

SECTION 272 - ABSENCE OF COMPLAINANT
Core Content:
When the proceedings have been instituted upon complaint, and on any day fixed for the hearing of the case, the complainant is absent, and the offence may be lawfully compounded or is not a cognizable offence, the Magistrate may after giving thirty days' time to the complainant to be present, acquit the accused, unless for some reason he thinks it proper to adjourn the hearing to some other day. Where the complainant is represented by an advocate or where the Magistrate is of opinion that the personal attendance of the complainant is not necessary, the Magistrate may dispense with his attendance and proceed with the case. The provisions apply also to cases where the non-appearance of the complainant is due to his death.

Key Time Limit: 30 days' time to complainant to appear

SECTION 273 - COMPENSATION FOR ACCUSATION WITHOUT REASONABLE CAUSE
Core Content:
If, in any case instituted upon complaint or upon information given to a police officer or to a Magistrate, the Magistrate discharges or acquits all or any of the accused, and is of opinion that there was no reasonable ground for making the accusation against them, the Magistrate may call upon the complainant or informant to show cause why he should not pay compensation to such accused. After hearing, if satisfied, the Magistrate may order compensation not exceeding the amount of fine he is empowered to impose. In default of payment, the person may undergo simple imprisonment for a period not exceeding thirty days.

Procedure:

Magistrate discharges/acquits all or any accused

Opinion: no reasonable ground for accusation

If complainant/informant present, call upon forthwith to show cause

If not present, issue summons to appear and show cause

Record and consider cause

If satisfied, order compensation (not exceeding fine amount Magistrate can impose) to accused

May order in default simple imprisonment up to 30 days

Compensation paid not exempt from civil/criminal liability (but deducted from subsequent civil award)

Appeal by complainant/informant from second class Magistrate if compensation >₹2,000 as if convicted

Compensation not paid before appeal period expires (1 month if no appeal)

BNSS CHAPTER XXI: TRIAL OF SUMMONS-CASES BY MAGISTRATES (Sections 274-282)
SECTION 274 - SUBSTANCE OF ACCUSATION TO BE STATED
Core Content:
When in a summons-case the accused appears or is brought before the Magistrate, the particulars of the offence of which he is accused shall be stated to him, and he shall be asked whether he pleads guilty or has any defence to make, but it shall not be necessary to frame a formal charge. If the Magistrate considers the accusation as groundless, he shall, after recording reasons in writing, release the accused and such release shall have the effect of discharge.

SECTION 275 - CONVICTION ON PLEA OF GUILTY
Core Content:
If the accused pleads guilty, the Magistrate shall record the plea as nearly as possible in the words used by the accused and may, in his discretion, convict him thereon.

SECTION 276 - CONVICTION ON PLEA OF GUILTY IN ABSENCE OF ACCUSED IN PETTY CASES
Core Content:
Where a summons has been issued under section 229 and the accused desires to plead guilty to the charge without appearing before the Magistrate, he shall transmit to the Magistrate, by post or by messenger, a letter containing his plea and also the amount of fine specified in the summons. The Magistrate may, in his discretion, convict the accused in his absence, on his plea of guilty and sentence him to pay the fine specified in the summons.

SECTION 277 - PROCEDURE WHEN NOT CONVICTED
Core Content:
If the Magistrate does not convict the accused under section 275 or section 276, the Magistrate shall proceed to hear the prosecution and take all such evidence as may be produced in support of the prosecution, and also to hear the accused and take all such evidence as he produces in his defence. The Magistrate may, if he thinks fit, on the application of the prosecution or the accused, issue a summons to any witness directing him to attend or to produce any document or other thing. The Magistrate may, before summoning any witness, require that the reasonable expenses of the witness be deposited in Court.

SECTION 278 - ACQUITTAL OR CONVICTION
Core Content:
If the Magistrate, upon taking the evidence referred to in section 277 and such further evidence as he may cause to be produced, finds the accused not guilty, he shall record an order of acquittal. Where the Magistrate does not proceed in accordance with the provisions of section 364 or section 401, he shall, if he finds the accused guilty, pass sentence upon him according to law. A Magistrate may, under section 275 or section 278, convict the accused of any offence triable under this Chapter which from the facts admitted or proved he appears to have committed, whatever may be the nature of the complaint or summons, if the Magistrate is satisfied that the accused would not be prejudiced thereby.

SECTION 279 - NON-APPEARANCE OR DEATH OF COMPLAINANT
Core Content:
If the summons has been issued on complaint, and on the day appointed for the appearance of the accused, or any day subsequent thereto to which the hearing may be adjourned, the complainant does not appear, the Magistrate shall, after giving thirty days' time to the complainant to be present, acquit the accused, unless for some reason he thinks it proper to adjourn the hearing to some other day. Where the complainant is represented by an advocate or where the Magistrate is of opinion that the personal attendance of the complainant is not necessary, the Magistrate may dispense with his attendance and proceed with the case. The provisions apply also to cases where the non-appearance of the complainant is due to his death.

Key Time Limit: 30 days' time to complainant

SECTION 280 - WITHDRAWAL OF COMPLAINT
Core Content:
