If a complainant, at any time before a final order is passed in any case under this Chapter, satisfies the Magistrate that there are sufficient grounds for permitting him to withdraw his complaint against the accused, or if there be more than one accused, against all or any of them, the Magistrate may permit him to withdraw the same, and shall thereupon acquit the accused against whom the complaint is so withdrawn.

SECTION 281 - POWER TO STOP PROCEEDINGS IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
In any summons-case instituted otherwise than upon complaint, a Magistrate of the first class or, with the previous sanction of the Chief Judicial Magistrate, any other Judicial Magistrate, may, for reasons to be recorded by him, stop the proceedings at any stage without pronouncing any judgment. Where such stoppage of proceedings is made after the evidence of the principal witnesses has been recorded, he shall pronounce a judgment of acquittal, and in any other case, release the accused, and such release shall have the effect of discharge.

SECTION 282 - POWER OF COURT TO CONVERT SUMMONS-CASES INTO WARRANT-CASES
Core Content:
When in the course of the trial of a summons-case relating to an offence punishable with imprisonment for a term exceeding six months, it appears to the Magistrate that in the interests of justice, the offence should be tried in accordance with the procedure for the trial of warrant-cases, such Magistrate may proceed to re-hear the case in the manner provided by this Sanhita for the trial of warrant-cases and may recall any witness who may have been examined.

BNSS CHAPTER XXII: SUMMARY TRIALS (Sections 283-288)
SECTION 283 - POWER TO TRY SUMMARILY
Core Content:
Notwithstanding anything contained in this Sanhita, any Chief Judicial Magistrate or Magistrate of the first class shall try in a summary way all or any of the following offences: theft where value of property stolen does not exceed twenty thousand rupees; receiving or retaining stolen property where value does not exceed twenty thousand rupees; assisting in concealment or disposal of stolen property where value does not exceed twenty thousand rupees; offences under sections 331(2) and (3) BNS; insult with intent to provoke breach of peace under section 352 BNS; criminal intimidation under sections 351(2) and (3) BNS; abetment of any of the foregoing offences; attempt to commit any of the foregoing offences; any offence under the Cattle-trespass Act, 1871. The Magistrate may, after giving the accused a reasonable opportunity of being heard, for reasons to be recorded in writing, try in a summary way all or any of the offences not punishable with death or imprisonment for life or imprisonment for a term exceeding three years. No appeal shall lie against the decision of a Magistrate to try a case in a summary way. When, in the course of a summary trial it appears to the Magistrate that the nature of the case is such that it is undesirable to try it summarily, the Magistrate shall recall any witnesses who may have been examined and proceed to re-hear the case in the manner provided by this Sanhita.

Key Limits: Theft value ≤₹20,000

SECTION 284 - SUMMARY TRIAL BY MAGISTRATE OF SECOND CLASS
Core Content:
The High Court may confer on any Magistrate invested with the powers of a Magistrate of the second class power to try summarily any offence which is punishable only with fine or with imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months with or without fine, and any abetment of or attempt to commit any such offence.

SECTION 285 - PROCEDURE FOR SUMMARY TRIALS
Core Content:
In trials under this Chapter, the procedure specified in this Sanhita for the trial of summons-case shall be followed except as hereinafter mentioned. No sentence of imprisonment for a term exceeding three months shall be passed in the case of any conviction under this Chapter.

SECTION 286 - RECORD IN SUMMARY TRIALS
Core Content:
In every case tried summarily, the Magistrate shall enter, in such form as the State Government may direct, the following particulars: (a) the serial number of the case; (b) the date of the commission of the offence; (c) the date of the report or complaint; (d) the name of the complainant (if any); (e) the name, parentage and residence of the accused; (f) the offence complained of and the offence (if any) proved, and in cases under section 283(1)(i),(ii),(iii), the value of the property; (g) the plea of the accused and his examination (if any); (h) the finding; (i) the sentence or other final order; (j) the date on which proceedings terminated.

SECTION 287 - JUDGMENT IN CASES TRIED SUMMARILY
Core Content:
In every case tried summarily in which the accused does not plead guilty, the Magistrate shall record the substance of the evidence and a judgment containing a brief statement of the reasons for the finding.

SECTION 288 - LANGUAGE OF RECORD AND JUDGMENT
Core Content:
Every such record and judgment shall be written in the language of the Court. The High Court may authorise any Magistrate empowered to try offences summarily to prepare the aforesaid record or judgment or both by means of an officer appointed in this behalf by the Chief Judicial Magistrate, and the record or judgment so prepared shall be signed by such Magistrate.

BNSS CHAPTER XXIII: PLEA BARGAINING (Sections 289-300)
SECTION 289 - APPLICATION OF CHAPTER
Core Content:
This Chapter shall apply in respect of an accused against whom the report has been forwarded by the police officer under section 193 alleging an offence other than an offence for which the punishment of death or of imprisonment for life or of imprisonment for a term exceeding seven years has been provided, or a Magistrate has taken cognizance of an offence on complaint (other than death/life/>7 years), and after examining complainant and witnesses under section 223, issued process under section 227. This Chapter does not apply where such offence affects the socio-economic condition of the country or has been committed against a woman or a child. The Central Government shall, by notification, determine the offences affecting the socio-economic condition of the country.

SECTION 290 - APPLICATION FOR PLEA BARGAINING
Core Content:
A person accused of an offence may file an application for plea bargaining within a period of thirty days from the date of framing of charge. The application shall contain a brief description of the case including the offence, and shall be accompanied by an affidavit sworn by the accused stating that he has voluntarily preferred, after understanding the nature and extent of punishment, the plea bargaining, and that he has not previously been convicted for the same offence. After receiving the application, the Court shall issue notice to the Public Prosecutor or complainant and to the accused. When they appear, the Court shall examine the accused in camera to satisfy itself that the application has been filed voluntarily. If satisfied, it shall provide time, not exceeding sixty days, to work out a mutually satisfactory disposition. If the Court finds the application was filed involuntarily or he has previously been convicted for the same offence, it shall proceed further in accordance with BNSS from the stage such application was filed.

Key Time Limits: 30 days from framing of charge; up to 60 days for disposition

SECTION 291 - GUIDELINES FOR MUTUALLY SATISFACTORY DISPOSITION
Core Content:
In a case instituted on a police report, the Court shall issue notice to the Public Prosecutor, the police officer who investigated, the accused, and the victim to participate in a meeting to work out a satisfactory disposition. Throughout the process, it shall be the duty of the Court to ensure it is completed voluntarily. The accused may participate with his advocate. In a case instituted otherwise than on police report, the Court shall issue notice to the accused and the victim to participate. If the victim or accused so desires, they may participate with their advocate.

SECTION 292 - REPORT OF MUTUALLY SATISFACTORY DISPOSITION
Core Content:
Where a satisfactory disposition has been worked out, the Court shall prepare a report of such disposition which shall be signed by the presiding officer and all other persons who participated in the meeting. If no such disposition has been worked out, the Court shall record such observation and proceed further from the stage the application under section 290(1) was filed.

SECTION 293 - DISPOSAL OF CASE
Core Content:
Where a satisfactory disposition has been worked out, the Court shall award compensation to the victim and hear the parties on the quantum of punishment. If the Court is of the view that section 401 or the Probation of Offenders Act applies, it may release the accused on probation. If the Court finds that minimum punishment has been provided, it may sentence the accused to half of such minimum punishment (first-time offender: one-fourth). If no minimum punishment is provided, the Court may sentence the accused to one-fourth of the punishment provided (first-time offender: one-sixth).

SECTION 294 - JUDGMENT OF COURT
Core Content:
The Court shall deliver its judgment in terms of section 293 in open Court and the same shall be signed by the presiding officer.

SECTION 295 - FINALITY OF JUDGMENT
Core Content:
The judgment delivered shall be final and no appeal (except special leave petition under Article 136 and writ petition under Articles 226 and 227 of the Constitution) shall lie in any Court against such judgment.

SECTION 296 - POWER OF COURT IN PLEA BARGAINING
Core Content:
A Court shall have, for the purposes of discharging its functions under this Chapter, all the powers vested in respect of bail, trial of offences and other matters relating to the disposal of a case under this Sanhita.

SECTION 297 - PERIOD OF DETENTION UNDERGONE BY ACCUSED TO BE SET OFF AGAINST SENTENCE
Core Content:
The provisions of section 468 shall apply for setting off the period of detention undergone by the accused against the sentence of imprisonment imposed under this Chapter.

SECTION 298 - SAVINGS
Core Content:
The provisions of this Chapter shall have effect notwithstanding anything inconsistent therewith contained in any other provisions of this Sanhita.

SECTION 299 - STATEMENTS OF ACCUSED NOT TO BE USED
Core Content:
Notwithstanding anything contained in any law for the time being in force, the statements or facts stated by an accused in an application for plea bargaining filed under section 290 shall not be used for any other purpose except for the purpose of this Chapter.

SECTION 300 - NON-APPLICATION OF CHAPTER
Core Content:
Nothing in this Chapter shall apply to any juvenile or child as defined in section 2 of the Juvenile Justice (Care and Protection of Children) Act, 2015.

BNSS CHAPTER XXIV: ATTENDANCE OF PERSONS CONFINED OR DETAINED IN PRISONS (Sections 301-306)
SECTION 301 - DEFINITIONS
Core Content:
In this Chapter, "detained" includes detained under any law providing for preventive detention; "prison" includes any place declared by State Government to be a subsidiary jail, and any reformatory, Borstal institution or other institution of a like nature.

SECTION 302 - POWER TO REQUIRE ATTENDANCE OF PRISONERS
Core Content:
Whenever, in the course of an inquiry, trial or proceeding, it appears to a Criminal Court that a person confined or detained in a prison should be brought before the Court for answering to a charge or for any proceedings against him, or that it is necessary to examine such person as a witness, the Court may make an order requiring the officer in charge of the prison to produce such person. Where such order is made by a Magistrate of the second class, it shall not be acted upon unless countersigned by the Chief Judicial Magistrate.

Procedure:

Court may order officer in charge of prison to produce prisoner for answering charge, proceedings, or as witness

Second class Magistrate's order requires countersignature of CJM

Order submitted for countersigning shall be accompanied by statement of facts rendering order necessary

CJM may decline to countersign after considering statement

SECTION 303 - POWER TO EXCLUDE CERTAIN PERSONS
Core Content:
The State Government or Central Government may, at any time, having regard to the nature of the offence, the likelihood of disturbance of public order, and public interest, direct that any person or class of persons shall not be removed from prison. So long as the order remains in force, no order under section 302 shall have effect in respect of such person or class.

SECTION 304 - OFFICER IN CHARGE TO ABSTAIN IN CERTAIN CONTINGENCIES
Core Content:
Where the person in respect of whom an order is made under section 302 is by reason of sickness or infirmity unfit to be removed, or is under committal for trial or under remand, or is in custody for a period which would expire before the time required for complying with the order, or is a person to whom a Government order under section 303 applies, the officer in charge shall abstain from carrying out the order and shall send a statement of reasons. Exception: where attendance required for giving evidence at a place not more than 25 kilometres distance, the officer shall not abstain for the reason of being under committal/remand.

Key Distance: 25 kilometres

SECTION 305 - PRISONER TO BE BROUGHT TO COURT IN CUSTODY
Core Content:
Subject to section 304, the officer in charge of the prison shall, upon delivery of an order under section 302(1) and duly countersigned where necessary, cause the person named to be taken to the Court so as to be present at the time mentioned, and shall cause him to be kept in custody in or near the Court until examined or until the Court authorises him to be taken back.

SECTION 306 - POWER TO ISSUE COMMISSION FOR EXAMINATION OF WITNESS IN PRISON
Core Content:
The provisions of this Chapter shall be without prejudice to the power of the Court to issue, under section 319, a commission for the examination, as a witness, of any person confined or detained in a prison; and the provisions of Part B of Chapter XXV shall apply in relation to the examination on commission of any such person in the prison.

BNSS CHAPTER XXV: EVIDENCE IN INQUIRIES AND TRIALS (Sections 307-336)
SECTION 307 - LANGUAGE OF COURTS
Core Content:
The State Government may determine what shall be, for purposes of this Sanhita, the language of each Court within the State other than the High Court.

SECTION 308 - EVIDENCE TO BE TAKEN IN PRESENCE OF ACCUSED
Core Content:
Except as otherwise expressly provided, all evidence taken in the course of the trial or other proceeding shall be taken in the presence of the accused, or, when his personal attendance is dispensed with, in the presence of his advocate including through audio-video electronic means at the designated place to be notified by the State Government. Where the evidence of a woman below the age of eighteen years who is alleged to have been subjected to rape or any other sexual offence is to be recorded, the Court may take appropriate measures to ensure that such woman is not confronted by the accused while at the same time ensuring the right of cross-examination of the accused.

Procedure:

Evidence taken in presence of accused or his advocate (including by audio-video)

For woman below 18 subjected to rape/sexual offence, Court may ensure she is not confronted by accused while ensuring right of cross-examination

SECTION 309 - RECORD IN SUMMONS-CASES AND INQUIRIES
Core Content:
In all summons-cases tried before a Magistrate, in all inquiries under sections 164 to 167, and in all proceedings under section 491 otherwise than in the course of a trial, the Magistrate shall, as the examination of each witness proceeds, make a memorandum of the substance of the evidence in the language of the Court. If the Magistrate is unable to make such memorandum himself, he shall, after recording the reason of his inability, cause such memorandum to be made in writing or from his dictation in open Court. Such memorandum shall be signed by the Magistrate and shall form part of the record.

SECTION 310 - RECORD IN WARRANT-CASES
Core Content:
In all warrant-cases tried before a Magistrate, the evidence of each witness shall, as his examination proceeds, be taken down in writing either by the Magistrate himself or by his dictation in open Court or, where he is unable to do so owing to a physical or other incapacity, under his direction and superintendence, by an officer of the Court appointed by him. Evidence may also be recorded by audio-video electronic means in the presence of the advocate of the accused. Where the Magistrate causes the evidence to be taken down, he shall record a certificate that the evidence could not be taken down by himself. Such evidence shall ordinarily be taken down in the form of a narrative; but the Magistrate may take down any part in the form of question and answer. The evidence so taken down shall be signed by the Magistrate and shall form part of the record.

SECTION 311 - RECORD IN TRIAL BEFORE COURT OF SESSION
Core Content:
In all trials before a Court of Session, the evidence of each witness shall, as his examination proceeds, be taken down in writing either by the presiding Judge himself or by his dictation in open Court, or under his direction and superintendence, by an officer of the Court appointed by him. Such evidence shall ordinarily be taken down in the form of a narrative, but the presiding Judge may take down any part in the form of question and answer. The evidence so taken down shall be signed by the presiding Judge and shall form part of the record.

SECTION 312 - LANGUAGE OF RECORD OF EVIDENCE
Core Content:
If the witness gives evidence in the language of the Court, it shall be taken down in that language. If he gives evidence in any other language, it may, if practicable, be taken down in that language, and if not practicable, a true translation in the language of the Court shall be prepared as the examination proceeds, signed by the Magistrate or presiding Judge, and shall form part of the record. Where evidence is taken down in a language other than the language of the Court, a true translation shall be prepared as soon as practicable, signed, and form part of the record. When evidence is taken down in English and a translation in the language of the Court is not required by any party, the Court may dispense with such translation.

SECTION 313 - PROCEDURE IN REGARD TO SUCH EVIDENCE WHEN COMPLETED
Core Content:
As the evidence of each witness taken under section 310 or section 311 is completed, it shall be read over to him in the presence of the accused, if in attendance, or of his advocate, and shall, if necessary, be corrected. If the witness denies the correctness of any part, the Magistrate or presiding Judge may, instead of correcting the evidence, make a memorandum thereon of the objection and shall add such remarks as he thinks necessary. If the record of evidence is in a language different from that in which it has been given and the witness does not understand that language, the record shall be interpreted to him in the language in which it was given, or in a language which he understands.

SECTION 314 - INTERPRETATION OF EVIDENCE TO ACCUSED OR HIS ADVOCATE
Core Content:
Whenever any evidence is given in a language not understood by the accused, and he is present in Court in person, it shall be interpreted to him in open Court in a language understood by him. If he appears by an advocate and the evidence is given in a language other than the language of the Court, and not understood by the advocate, it shall be interpreted to such advocate in that language. When documents are put for the purpose of formal proof, it shall be in the discretion of the Court to interpret as much thereof as appears necessary.

SECTION 315 - REMARKS RESPECTING DEMEANOUR OF WITNESS
Core Content:
When a presiding Judge or Magistrate has recorded the evidence of a witness, he shall also record such remarks (if any) as he thinks material respecting the demeanour of such witness whilst under examination.

SECTION 316 - RECORD OF EXAMINATION OF ACCUSED
Core Content:
Whenever the accused is examined by any Magistrate, or by a Court of Session, the whole of such examination, including every question put to him and every answer given by him, shall be recorded in full by the presiding Judge or Magistrate himself or where he is unable to do so owing to a physical or other incapacity, under his direction and superintendence by an officer of the Court. The record shall, if practicable, be in the language in which the accused is examined or, if that is not practicable, in the language of the Court. The record shall be shown or read to the accused, or, if he does not understand the language, interpreted to him in a language which he understands, and he shall be at liberty to explain or add to his answers. It shall thereafter be signed by the accused and by the Magistrate or presiding Judge, who shall certify under his own hand that the examination was taken in his presence and hearing and that the record contains a full and true account of the statement made by the accused. Where the accused is in custody and is examined through electronic communication, his signature shall be taken within seventy-two hours of such examination.

Key Time Limit: Signature within 72 hours of electronic examination

SECTION 317 - INTERPRETER TO BE BOUND TO INTERPRET TRUTHFULLY
Core Content:
When the services of an interpreter are required by any Criminal Court for the interpretation of any evidence or statement, he shall be bound to state the true interpretation of such evidence or statement.

SECTION 318 - RECORD IN HIGH COURT
Core Content:
Every High Court may, by general rule, prescribe the manner in which the evidence of witnesses and the examination of the accused shall be taken down in cases coming before it, and such evidence and examination shall be taken down in accordance with such rule.

SECTION 319 - WHEN ATTENDANCE OF WITNESS MAY BE DISPENSED WITH AND COMMISSION ISSUED
Core Content:
Whenever, in the course of any inquiry, trial or other proceeding, it appears to a Court or Magistrate that the examination of a witness is necessary for the ends of justice, and that the attendance of such witness cannot be procured without an amount of delay, expense or inconvenience which would be unreasonable, the Court or Magistrate may dispense with such attendance and may issue a commission for the examination of the witness. Where the examination of the President or the Vice-President of India or the Governor of a State or the Administrator of a Union territory as a witness is necessary for the ends of justice, a commission shall be issued for the examination of such a witness. The Court may, when issuing a commission for the examination of a witness for the prosecution, direct that such amount as the Court considers reasonable to meet the expenses of the accused, including the advocate's fees, be paid by the prosecution.

SECTION 320 - COMMISSION TO WHOM TO BE ISSUED
Core Content:
If the witness is within the territories to which this Sanhita extends, the commission shall be directed to the Chief Judicial Magistrate within whose local jurisdiction the witness is to be found. If the witness is in India but in a State or area to which this Sanhita does not extend, the commission shall be directed to such Court or officer as the Central Government may specify. If the witness is in a country or place outside India and arrangements have been made, the commission shall be issued in such form, directed to such Court or officer, and sent to such authority as the Central Government may prescribe.

SECTION 321 - EXECUTION OF COMMISSIONS
Core Content:
Upon receipt of the commission, the Chief Judicial Magistrate or such Magistrate as he may appoint shall summon the witness before him or proceed to the place where the witness is, and shall take down his evidence in the same manner, and may exercise the same powers, as in trials of warrant-cases under this Sanhita.

SECTION 322 - PARTIES MAY EXAMINE WITNESSES
Core Content:
The parties to any proceeding in which a commission is issued may respectively forward any interrogatories in writing which the Court directing the commission may think relevant. It shall be lawful for the Magistrate, Court or officer to whom the commission is directed to examine the witness upon such interrogatories. Any such party may appear before such Magistrate, Court or Officer by an advocate, or if not in custody, in person, and may examine, cross-examine and re-examine the said witness.

SECTION 323 - RETURN OF COMMISSION
Core Content:
After any commission issued under section 319 has been duly executed, it shall be returned, together with the deposition of the witness examined, to the Court or Magistrate issuing the commission. The commission, the return and the deposition shall be open to inspection of the parties, and may be read in evidence, and shall form part of the record. Any deposition so taken, if it satisfies the conditions specified by section 27 of the Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, may also be received in evidence at any subsequent stage before another Court.

SECTION 324 - ADJOURNMENT OF PROCEEDING
Core Content:
In every case in which a commission is issued under section 319, the inquiry, trial or other proceeding may be adjourned for a specified time reasonably sufficient for the execution and return of the commission.

SECTION 325 - EXECUTION OF FOREIGN COMMISSIONS
Core Content:
The provisions of section 321 and so much of sections 322 and 323 as relate to execution of a commission and its return shall apply to commissions issued by any Court, Judge or Magistrate exercising jurisdiction within an area in India to which this Sanhita does not extend, or in any country or place outside India, as the Central Government may specify.

SECTION 326 - DEPOSITION OF MEDICAL WITNESS
Core Content:
The deposition of a civil surgeon or other medical witness, taken and attested by a Magistrate in the presence of the accused, or taken on commission under this Chapter, may be given in evidence in any inquiry, trial or other proceeding, although the deponent is not called as a witness. The Court may, if it thinks fit, and shall, on the application of the prosecution or the accused, summon and examine any such deponent as to the subject-matter of his deposition.

SECTION 327 - IDENTIFICATION REPORT OF MAGISTRATE
Core Content:
Any document purporting to be a report of identification under the hand of an Executive Magistrate in respect of a person or property may be used as evidence in any inquiry, trial or other proceeding, although such Magistrate is not called as a witness. Where such report contains a statement of any suspect or witness to which the provisions of section 19, 26, 27, 158 or 160 of the Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023 apply, such statement shall not be used except in accordance with those sections. The Court may, if it thinks fit, and shall, on the application of the prosecution or of the accused, summon and examine such Magistrate as to the subject-matter of the said report.

BNSS SECTION 328 - EVIDENCE OF OFFICERS OF MINT
Core Content:
Any document purporting to be a report under the hand of a gazetted officer of any Mint, Note Printing Press, Security Printing Press, Forensic Department, Forensic Science Laboratory, Government Examiner of Questioned Documents, or State Examiner of Questioned Documents (as Central Government notifies) upon any matter duly submitted for examination and report may be used as evidence in any inquiry, trial or proceeding under BNSS, although such officer is not called as a witness.

Procedure:

Document purporting to be report by specified gazetted officer is admissible in evidence

Court may, if it thinks fit, summon and examine such officer as to subject-matter of his report

However, such officer shall not be summoned to produce any records on which the report is based

Without prejudice to BSA sections 129 and 130, no such officer shall except with permission of General Manager or officer in charge be permitted:

(a) to give any evidence derived from unpublished official records on which report is based

(b) to disclose nature or particulars of any test applied

Illustration:
A report from the Director of the Forensic Science Laboratory on fingerprints found at the crime scene is admissible without calling the Director to court. The court may call him if needed, but cannot ask him to produce the laboratory's internal records or disclose testing methods without permission.

BNSS SECTION 329 - REPORTS OF CERTAIN GOVERNMENT SCIENTIFIC EXPERTS
Core Content:
Any document purporting to be a report under the hand of a Government scientific expert (Chemical Examiner, Chief Controller of Explosives, Director of Finger Print Bureau, Director of Forensic Science Laboratory, Serologist to Government, or other notified expert) upon any matter submitted for examination may be used as evidence. Court may summon and examine such expert. If unable to attend personally, expert may depute a responsible officer conversant with the facts.

Procedure:

Report of Government scientific expert admissible as evidence

Court may summon and examine expert

If expert unable to attend personally, may depute responsible officer working with him who is conversant with facts and can satisfactorily depose

Experts covered:

(a) Chemical Examiner or Assistant Chemical Examiner to Government

(b) Chief Controller of Explosives

(c) Director of Finger Print Bureau

(d) Director, Haffkeine Institute, Bombay

(e) Director, Deputy Director or Assistant Director of Central/State Forensic Science Laboratory

(f) Serologist to Government

(g) Any other scientific expert specified by State/Central Government notification

Illustration:
A report from the Chemical Examiner analyzing a white powder found on the accused as cocaine is admissible without calling him. If the court wants to examine him and he is busy, he can send a senior assistant who knows the case.

BNSS SECTION 330 - NO FORMAL PROOF OF CERTAIN DOCUMENTS
Core Content:
Where any document is filed before Court by prosecution or accused, particulars of every such document shall be included in a list. Prosecution/accused/advocate shall be called upon to admit or deny genuineness soon after supply of documents, and in no case later than 30 days after such supply. Court may relax time limit with reasons. No expert shall be called unless his report is disputed. If genuineness not disputed, document may be read in evidence without proof of signature.

Procedure:

Document filed before Court by prosecution or accused

Particulars of every such document included in a list (form as State Government rules)

Parties called upon to admit or deny genuineness:

Soon after supply of documents

In no case later than 30 days after such supply

Court may relax time limit with reasons recorded

No expert shall be called to appear unless his report is disputed by any party

If genuineness not disputed, document may be read in evidence without proof of signature

Court may in its discretion require signature to be proved

Key Time Limit: 30 days from supply of documents to admit/deny genuineness

Illustration:
Prosecution files 10 documents with the court and serves copies on accused. Accused has 30 days to say which documents he admits as genuine and which he disputes. If he does not dispute a document, it can be read in evidence without calling any witness to prove it. If the forensic report is not disputed, the expert need not come to court.

BNSS SECTION 331 - AFFIDAVIT IN PROOF OF CONDUCT OF PUBLIC SERVANTS
Core Content:
When any application is made to any Court in the course of any inquiry, trial or other proceeding under BNSS, and allegations are made therein respecting the conduct of any public servant, the Court may, in its discretion, require the applicant to give security for the payment of any costs that may be incurred by the public servant. The Court may also, before issuing process, require the applicant to file an affidavit in support of the allegations.

Procedure:

Application made in course of inquiry/trial/proceeding

Allegations made respecting conduct of any public servant

Court may in its discretion require applicant to give security for payment of any costs that may be incurred by the public servant

Court may before issuing process require applicant to file an affidavit in support of allegations

Illustration:
X files an application in court alleging that a police officer fabricated evidence. The court may require X to give security to cover the officer's costs if the allegations are false, and may also require X to file an affidavit swearing to the truth of the allegations before issuing notice to the officer.

BNSS SECTION 332 - EVIDENCE OF FORMAL CHARACTER ON AFFIDAVIT
Core Content:
The evidence of any person whose evidence is of a formal character may be given by affidavit and may, subject to all just exceptions, be read in evidence in any inquiry, trial or other proceeding under BNSS. The Court may, if it thinks fit, and shall, on the application of the prosecution or the accused, summon and examine any such person as to the facts contained in his affidavit.

Procedure:

Person's evidence is of a formal character (e.g., certifying documents, chain of custody)

Such evidence may be given by affidavit

Affidavit may be read in evidence subject to just exceptions

Court may (on its own) summon and examine such person

Court shall (on application of prosecution or accused) summon and examine such person

Illustration:
A bank manager needs to certify that certain bank statements are authentic. Instead of coming to court in person, he files an affidavit. The affidavit is read in evidence. If the accused disputes the affidavit, the court will summon the bank manager for cross-examination.

BNSS SECTION 333 - AUTHORITIES BEFORE WHOM AFFIDAVITS MAY BE SWORN
Core Content:
Affidavits to be used before any Court under BNSS may be sworn or affirmed before: (a) any Judge or Judicial or Executive Magistrate; (b) any Commissioner of Oaths appointed by a High Court or Court of Session; (c) any notary appointed under the Notaries Act, 1952. Affidavits shall be confined to facts deponent can prove from his own knowledge and facts he has reasonable ground to believe true (with grounds stated). Court may strike out scandalous/irrelevant matter.

Procedure:

Affidavit may be sworn/affirmed before:

(a) Any Judge or Judicial or Executive Magistrate

(b) Any Commissioner of Oaths appointed by High Court or Court of Session

(c) Any notary under Notaries Act, 1952

Affidavit shall state separately:

Facts deponent can prove from his own knowledge

Facts he has reasonable ground to believe true (with grounds stated)

Court may order any scandalous and irrelevant matter to be struck out or amended

Illustration:
X wants to file an affidavit in a criminal case. He can swear it before a Judicial Magistrate, an Executive Magistrate, a Commissioner of Oaths, or a notary. In the affidavit, he must separately list what he personally saw versus what he heard from others, explaining why he believes the hearsay to be true.

BNSS SECTION 334 - PREVIOUS CONVICTION OR ACQUITTAL HOW PROVED
Core Content:
A previous conviction or acquittal may be proved in any inquiry, trial or proceeding by: (a) an extract certified under the hand of the officer having custody of the records of the Court where such conviction or acquittal was held; or (b) in case of conviction, either by a certificate signed by the officer in charge of the jail where punishment was undergone, or by production of the warrant of commitment. In each case, evidence as to identity of the accused with the person so convicted or acquitted must be provided.

Procedure:

Two methods of proof:

(a) Certified extract from the Court where conviction/acquittal occurred (signed by officer with custody of records)

(b) For conviction only: certificate from jail officer in charge where punishment was undergone, OR production of warrant of commitment

In all cases, additional evidence required as to identity of accused with the person previously convicted/acquitted

Illustration:
The prosecution wants to prove X has a previous conviction for theft. They produce a certified copy of the judgment from the court where X was convicted, plus a police officer who identifies X as the same person. Alternatively, they produce a certificate from the jail where X served time.

BNSS SECTION 335 - RECORD OF EVIDENCE IN ABSENCE OF ACCUSED
Core Content:
If it is proved that an accused person has absconded and there is no immediate prospect of arresting him, the Court competent to try or commit him may examine prosecution witnesses in his absence and record their depositions. Such depositions may be given in evidence against him on his arrest if the deponent is dead or incapable of giving evidence or cannot be found or his presence cannot be procured without unreasonable delay/expense/inconvenience.

Procedure:

Accused has absconded

No immediate prospect of arresting him

Court competent to try/commit may examine prosecution witnesses in his absence

Record their depositions

On arrest of accused, such depositions may be given in evidence against him if:

(i) deponent is dead, OR

(ii) deponent is incapable of giving evidence, OR

(iii) deponent cannot be found, OR

(iv) deponent's presence cannot be procured without unreasonable delay/expense/inconvenience

Illustration:
X absconds after murder. The court proceeds to record statements of witnesses Y and Z in X's absence. Six months later, X is arrested. By then, Y has died. Y's deposition recorded in X's absence is admissible in evidence against X. Z is still alive and can be called to testify.

BNSS SECTION 336 - EVIDENCE OF PUBLIC SERVANTS, EXPERTS, POLICE OFFICERS IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
Where any document or report prepared by a public servant, scientific expert or medical officer is purported to be used as evidence, and such person is transferred/retired/died, or cannot be found/is incapable, or securing his presence would cause delay, the Court shall secure presence of his successor officer who is holding that post at the time of such deposition to give deposition on such document or report. No such person shall be called unless his report is disputed. Successor's deposition may be allowed through audio-video electronic means.

Procedure:

Document/report prepared by public servant, scientific expert, or medical officer is to be used as evidence

One of following situations exists:

(i) Such person is transferred, retired, or died

(ii) Such person cannot be found or is incapable of giving deposition

(iii) Securing presence of such person is likely to cause delay in holding inquiry/trial/proceeding

Court shall secure presence of successor officer of such person who is holding that post at the time of deposition

Successor officer shall give deposition on such document or report

No public servant, scientific expert, or medical officer shall be called to appear unless his report is disputed by any party

Deposition of successor may be allowed through audio-video electronic means

Illustration:
The Chemical Examiner who analyzed the drug sample has retired and moved abroad. The prosecution wants to use his report. The court calls the current Chemical Examiner (his successor) to depose on the report. The successor can testify by video conference. The report is admissible without calling the original examiner.

SECTION 337 - PERSON ONCE CONVICTED OR ACQUITTED NOT TO BE TRIED FOR SAME OFFENCE
Core Content:
A person who has once been tried by a Court of competent jurisdiction for an offence and convicted or acquitted of such offence shall, while such conviction or acquittal remains in force, not be liable to be tried again for the same offence, nor on the same facts for any other offence for which a different charge might have been made under section 244(1), or for which he might have been convicted under section 244(2). This is the principle of double jeopardy (autrefois convict/acquit).

Procedure:

Person has been tried by competent Court for an offence

Convicted or acquitted of such offence

Conviction or acquittal remains in force

Such person cannot be tried again for:

(i) The same offence

(ii) On the same facts for any other offence for which a different charge might have been made under section 244(1)

(iii) On the same facts for any other offence for which he might have been convicted under section 244(2)

Exception: Person acquitted/convicted may be afterwards tried, with consent of State Government, for any distinct offence for which separate charge might have been made at former trial under section 243(1)

Exception: Person convicted of offence constituted by act causing consequences which together with such act constituted a different offence, may be afterwards tried for the last-mentioned offence if consequences had not happened or were not known to Court at time of conviction

Exception: Person acquitted/convicted of offence constituted by any acts may be subsequently charged with and tried for any other offence constituted by same acts if the first Court was not competent to try the subsequent offence

Person discharged under section 281 shall not be tried again for same offence except with consent of Court which discharged him or other Court to which first Court is subordinate

Dismissal of complaint or discharge of accused is NOT an acquittal for this section

Illustrations:

A tried for theft as servant and acquitted. Cannot afterwards be charged with theft as servant, or upon same facts with theft simply or criminal breach of trust.

A tried for causing grievous hurt and convicted. Person injured afterwards dies. A may be tried again for culpable homicide.

A charged before Court of Session and convicted of culpable homicide of B. A may not afterwards be tried on same facts for murder of B.

SECTION 338 - APPEARANCE BY PUBLIC PROSECUTORS
Core Content:
The Public Prosecutor or Assistant Public Prosecutor in charge of a case may appear and plead without any written authority before any Court in which that case is under inquiry, trial or appeal. If in any such case any private person instructs his advocate to prosecute any person in any Court, the Public Prosecutor or Assistant Public Prosecutor in charge of the case shall conduct the prosecution, and the advocate so instructed shall act therein under the directions of the Public Prosecutor or Assistant Public Prosecutor, and may, with the permission of the Court, submit written arguments after the evidence is closed.

Procedure:

Public Prosecutor/Assistant Public Prosecutor may appear and plead without written authority

If private person instructs advocate to prosecute, Public Prosecutor/Assistant Public Prosecutor shall conduct the prosecution

Private advocate acts under directions of Public Prosecutor/Assistant Public Prosecutor

Private advocate may, with Court permission, submit written arguments after evidence closed

SECTION 339 - PERMISSION TO CONDUCT PROSECUTION
Core Content:
Any Magistrate inquiring into or trying a case may permit the prosecution to be conducted by any person other than a police officer below the rank of inspector; but no person, other than the Advocate-General or Government Advocate or a Public Prosecutor or Assistant Public Prosecutor, shall be entitled to do so without such permission. No police officer shall be permitted to conduct the prosecution if he has taken part in the investigation into the offence. Any person conducting the prosecution may do so personally or by an advocate.

Procedure:

Magistrate may permit prosecution to be conducted by any person (other than police officer below inspector)

Advocate-General, Government Advocate, Public Prosecutor, Assistant Public Prosecutor entitled to conduct without permission

All others require Magistrate's permission

Police officer who took part in investigation cannot conduct prosecution

Person conducting prosecution may do so personally or by advocate

SECTION 340 - RIGHT OF PERSON AGAINST WHOM PROCEEDINGS ARE INSTITUTED TO BE DEFENDED
Core Content:
Any person accused of an offence before a Criminal Court, or against whom proceedings are instituted under this Sanhita, may of right be defended by an advocate of his choice.

SECTION 341 - LEGAL AID TO ACCUSED AT STATE EXPENSE IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
Where, in a trial or appeal before a Court, the accused is not represented by an advocate, and where it appears to the Court that the accused has not sufficient means to engage an advocate, the Court shall assign an advocate for his defence at the expense of the State. The High Court may, with previous approval of State Government, make rules for mode of selecting advocates, facilities to be allowed, fees payable. State Government may extend these provisions to any class of trials before other Courts.

Procedure:

In trial or appeal before Court, accused not represented by advocate

Court finds accused has not sufficient means to engage advocate

Court shall assign an advocate for his defence at State expense

High Court may make rules with State Government approval for selection, facilities, fees

State Government may extend to other Courts by notification

SECTION 342 - PROCEDURE WHEN CORPORATION OR REGISTERED SOCIETY IS AN ACCUSED
Core Content:
Where a corporation (incorporated company or other body corporate, including society registered under Societies Registration Act, 1860) is the accused person, it may appoint a representative for the purpose of the inquiry or trial. Such appointment need not be under the seal of the corporation. Where a representative appears, any requirement that anything shall be done in the presence of the accused shall be construed as a requirement that it shall be done in the presence of the representative. Where a representative does not appear, such requirement shall not apply.

Procedure:

Corporation may appoint a representative for inquiry/trial (need not be under seal)

Where representative appears: requirements of presence of accused = presence of representative; examination of accused = examination of representative

Where representative does not appear: such requirements do not apply

Statement in writing signed by managing director or person duly authorised that named person appointed as representative: Court shall presume such person appointed unless contrary proved

Court determines any question whether person appearing is representative

SECTION 343 - TENDER OF PARDON TO ACCOMPLICE
Core Content:
With a view to obtaining the evidence of any person supposed to have been directly or indirectly concerned in or privy to an offence triable exclusively by Court of Session or by Court of Special Judge, or any offence punishable with imprisonment which may extend to seven years or with more severe sentence, the Chief Judicial Magistrate at any stage of investigation/inquiry/trial, and the Magistrate of first class inquiring into or trying the offence at any stage of inquiry/trial, may tender a pardon to such person on condition of his making a full and true disclosure of the whole circumstances within his knowledge relative to the offence and to every other person concerned.

Procedure:

Applies to: (a) offence triable exclusively by Court of Session or Special Judge; (b) offence punishable with imprisonment up to 7 years or more severe sentence

Chief Judicial Magistrate (any stage) or first class Magistrate (inquiry/trial stage) may tender pardon

Condition: full and true disclosure of whole circumstances within his knowledge relative to offence and every other person concerned

Magistrate shall record: (a) his reasons; (b) whether tender was accepted

On application by accused, furnish copy of record free of cost

Person accepting pardon: (a) shall be examined as witness in Magistrate's Court and subsequent trial; (b) shall unless already on bail be detained in custody until termination of trial

After examination, Magistrate without further inquiry shall commit case to Court of Session/Special Judge or make over to Chief Judicial Magistrate who shall try himself

SECTION 344 - POWER TO DIRECT TENDER OF PARDON
Core Content:
At any time after commitment of a case but before judgment is passed, the Court to which the commitment is made may, with a view to obtaining at the trial the evidence of any person supposed to have been directly or indirectly concerned in, or privy to, any such offence, tender a pardon on the same condition to such person.

Procedure:

After commitment but before judgment

Court of Session may tender pardon on same condition

SECTION 345 - TRIAL OF PERSON NOT COMPLYING WITH CONDITIONS OF PARDON
Core Content:
Where the Public Prosecutor certifies that a person who accepted pardon has, either by wilfully concealing anything essential or by giving false evidence, not complied with the condition, such person may be tried for the offence in respect of which pardon was tendered or for any other offence of which he appears guilty in connection with the same matter, and also for giving false evidence. He shall not be tried jointly with other accused. He shall not be tried for giving false evidence except with sanction of High Court.

Procedure:

Public Prosecutor certifies non-compliance (wilful concealment or false evidence)

Such person may be tried for:

(i) The offence for which pardon was tendered

(ii) Any other offence in connection with same matter

(iii) Offence of giving false evidence (requires High Court sanction)

Shall not be tried jointly with other accused

Statement made accepting pardon may be given in evidence against him

Accused may plead that he has complied - prosecution must prove non-compliance

Court shall ask accused whether he pleads compliance

If he so pleads, Court shall find whether he has complied; if found complied, pass judgment of acquittal

SECTION 346 - POWER TO POSTPONE OR ADJOURN PROCEEDINGS
Core Content:
In every inquiry or trial the proceedings shall be continued from day-to-day basis until all witnesses in attendance have been examined, unless the Court finds adjournment necessary for reasons to be recorded. For offences under BNS sections 64-68, 70, 71 (rape, etc.), inquiry/trial shall be completed within two months from filing of charge sheet. No Court shall remand accused to custody for term exceeding fifteen days at a time. No adjournment shall be granted when witnesses are in attendance without examining them except for special reasons. No adjournment shall be granted at request of a party except where circumstances beyond control; not more than two adjournments may be granted. Advocate engaged in another Court not a ground for adjournment. If witness present but party/advocate not ready, Court may record statement and dispense with examination/cross-examination.

Key Time Limits:

Day-to-day proceedings

Rape/sexual offences: 2 months from charge sheet for completion

Remand: not exceeding 15 days at a time

Maximum 2 adjournments per party

SECTION 347 - LOCAL INSPECTION
Core Content:
Any Judge or Magistrate may, at any stage of any inquiry, trial or other proceeding, after due notice to the parties, visit and inspect any place in which an offence is alleged to have been committed, or any other place which it is in his opinion necessary to view for the purpose of properly appreciating the evidence. He shall without unnecessary delay record a memorandum of any relevant facts observed. Such memorandum shall form part of the record and a copy shall be furnished free of cost to any party who so desires.

Procedure:

After due notice to parties

Visit and inspect place of offence or any other place necessary for appreciating evidence

Without unnecessary delay record memorandum of relevant facts observed

Memorandum forms part of record

Free copy to prosecutor/complainant/accused/any party on request

SECTION 348 - POWER TO SUMMON MATERIAL WITNESS, OR EXAMINE PERSON PRESENT
Core Content:
Any Court may, at any stage of any inquiry, trial or other proceeding, summon any person as a witness, or examine any person in attendance though not summoned, or recall and re-examine any person already examined; and the Court shall summon and examine or recall and re-examine any such person if his evidence appears to it to be essential to the just decision of the case.

SECTION 349 - POWER OF MAGISTRATE TO ORDER PERSON TO GIVE SPECIMEN SIGNATURES OR HANDWRITING, ETC.
Core Content:
If a Magistrate of the first class is satisfied that, for the purposes of any investigation or proceeding, it is expedient to direct any person, including an accused person, to give specimen signatures or finger impressions or handwriting or voice sample, he may make an order to that effect. The person shall be produced or attend at the time and place specified and shall give his specimen. No order shall be made unless the person has at some time been arrested in connection with such investigation or proceeding. Magistrate may, for reasons recorded, order any person to give such specimen or sample without him being arrested.

Procedure:

First class Magistrate satisfied expedient for investigation/proceeding

May order any person (including accused) to give:

(i) Specimen signatures

(ii) Finger impressions

(iii) Handwriting

(iv) Voice sample

Person shall be produced or attend at specified time and place

No order unless person has been arrested in connection with investigation/proceeding

Exception: Magistrate may for reasons recorded order without arrest

SECTION 350 - EXPENSES OF COMPLAINANTS AND WITNESSES
Core Content:
Subject to any rules made by the State Government, any Criminal Court may, if it thinks fit, order payment, on the part of the Government, of the reasonable expenses of any complainant or witness attending for the purposes of any inquiry, trial or other proceeding before such Court under this Sanhita.

SECTION 351 - POWER TO EXAMINE ACCUSED
Core Content:
In every inquiry or trial, for the purpose of enabling the accused personally to explain any circumstances appearing in the evidence against him, the Court may at any stage put such questions to him as the Court considers necessary, and shall, after the witnesses for the prosecution have been examined and before he is called on for his defence, question him generally on the case. No oath shall be administered to the accused. The accused shall not render himself liable to punishment by refusing to answer or giving false answers. The answers may be taken into consideration in such inquiry or trial, and put in evidence for or against him in any other inquiry into or trial for any other offence which such answers may tend to show he has committed. The Court may take help of Prosecutor and Defence Counsel in preparing relevant questions and may permit filing of written statement by accused as sufficient compliance.

Procedure:

Court may at any stage put questions to accused to explain circumstances in evidence

Court shall after prosecution evidence and before defence question accused generally on the case

No oath administered to accused

Accused not liable for punishment for refusing to answer or giving false answers

Answers may be taken into consideration and used in other proceedings

Court may take help of Prosecutor and Defence Counsel to prepare questions

Court may permit written statement as sufficient compliance

SECTION 352 - ORAL ARGUMENTS AND MEMORANDUM OF ARGUMENTS
Core Content:
Any party to a proceeding may, as soon as may be after the close of his evidence, address concise oral arguments, and may, before he concludes the oral arguments, submit a memorandum to the Court setting forth concisely and under distinct headings, the arguments in support of his case. A copy shall be simultaneously furnished to the opposite party. No adjournment shall be granted for filing written arguments unless Court for reasons recorded considers it necessary. The Court may regulate oral arguments if not concise or relevant.

Procedure:

Party may address concise oral arguments after close of his evidence

May submit memorandum of arguments before concluding oral arguments

Copy to opposite party simultaneously

No adjournment for written arguments unless Court records reasons

Court may regulate oral arguments if not concise or relevant

SECTION 353 - ACCUSED PERSON TO BE COMPETENT WITNESS
Core Content:
Any person accused of an offence before a Criminal Court shall be a competent witness for the defence and may give evidence on oath in disproof of the charges made against him or any person charged together with him at the same trial. He shall not be called as a witness except on his own request in writing. His failure to give evidence shall not be made the subject of any comment by any of the parties or the Court or give rise to any presumption against himself or any person charged together with him.

Procedure:

Accused is competent witness for defence

May give evidence on oath in disproof of charges

Shall not be called except on his own request in writing

Failure to give evidence: no comment by parties or Court, no presumption

SECTION 354 - NO INFLUENCE TO BE USED TO INDUCE DISCLOSURE
Core Content:
Except as provided in sections 343 and 344 (tender of pardon), no influence, by means of any promise or threat or otherwise, shall be used to an accused person to induce him to disclose or withhold any matter within his knowledge.

SECTION 355 - PROVISION FOR INQUIRIES AND TRIAL BEING HELD IN ABSENCE OF ACCUSED IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
At any stage of an inquiry or trial, if the Judge or Magistrate is satisfied, for reasons recorded, that the personal attendance of the accused is not necessary in the interests of justice, or that the accused persistently disturbs the proceedings, the Judge or Magistrate may, if the accused is represented by an advocate, dispense with his attendance and proceed in his absence, and may at any subsequent stage direct personal attendance. Personal attendance includes attendance through audio-video electronic means.

Procedure:

Judge/Magistrate satisfied personal attendance not necessary OR accused persistently disturbs proceedings

Accused represented by advocate

May dispense with attendance and proceed in his absence

May at any subsequent stage direct personal attendance

"Personal attendance" includes audio-video electronic means

SECTION 356 - INQUIRY, TRIAL OR JUDGMENT IN ABSENTIA OF PROCLAIMED OFFENDER
Core Content:
When a person declared as a proclaimed offender has absconded to evade trial and there is no immediate prospect of arresting him, it shall be deemed to operate as a waiver of the right of such person to be present and tried in person. The Court shall, after recording reasons in writing, in the interest of justice, proceed with the trial and pronounce judgment. Court shall not commence trial unless 90 days have lapsed from date of framing of charge.

Procedure:

Person declared proclaimed offender (under section 84(4))

Has absconded to evade trial, no immediate prospect of arrest

Deemed waiver of right to be present

Court shall record reasons and proceed with trial

Condition: trial not commence unless 90 days have lapsed from framing of charge

Pre-trial procedure required:

(i) Two consecutive warrants of arrest within interval of at least 30 days

(ii) Publication in national/local daily newspaper in place of last known address requiring appearance within 30 days, informing that trial will commence in absentia if fails to appear

(iii) Inform relative/friend if any about commencement of trial

(iv) Affix information on conspicuous part of his house and display in police station of last known address

If not represented by advocate, provided advocate at State expense

Depositions of witnesses recorded in his absence may be given in evidence against him

If arrested/produced during trial, Court may allow him to examine evidence taken in his absence

Deposition and examination may be recorded by audio-video electronic means

Voluntary absence after trial commenced does not prevent continuing trial including judgment even if arrested/produced at conclusion

No appeal against judgment unless proclaimed offender presents himself before Court of appeal

No appeal against conviction after expiry of 3 years from judgment

Key Time Limits: 90 days from charge framing; 30 days between warrants; 30 days for newspaper appearance; 3 years for appeal

SECTION 357 - PROCEDURE WHERE ACCUSED DOES NOT UNDERSTAND PROCEEDINGS
Core Content:
If the accused, though not a person of unsound mind, cannot be made to understand the proceedings, the Court may proceed with the inquiry or trial; and, in the case of a Court other than a High Court, if such proceedings result in a conviction, the proceedings shall be forwarded to the High Court with a report of the circumstances of the case, and the High Court shall pass thereon such order as it thinks fit.

SECTION 358 - POWER TO PROCEED AGAINST OTHER PERSONS APPEARING TO BE GUILTY OF OFFENCE
Core Content:
Where, in the course of any inquiry into, or trial of, an offence, it appears from the evidence that any person not being the accused has committed any offence for which such person could be tried together with the accused, the Court may proceed against such person for the offence which he appears to have committed. If such person is not attending, he may be arrested or summoned. Any person attending may be detained. Where the Court proceeds against any such person, the proceedings in respect of such person shall be commenced afresh, and the witnesses re-heard.

Procedure:

During inquiry/trial, evidence shows person not accused committed offence for which he could be tried together with accused

Court may proceed against such person

If not attending, arrest or summon

If attending, may detain

When proceeding against such person:

(a) Proceedings commenced afresh

(b) Witnesses re-heard

Case proceeds as if such person was accused when Court took cognizance

SECTION 359 - COMPOUNDING OF OFFENCES
Core Content:
The offences punishable under BNS specified in the Table may be compounded by the persons mentioned in the Table. Certain offences may be compounded with permission of Court. When an offence is compoundable, the abetment of such offence or attempt to commit such offence may be compounded in like manner. When the person competent to compound is a child or of unsound mind, any person competent to contract on his behalf may with Court permission compound. When such person is dead, legal representative may with Court consent compound. Composition of an offence shall have the effect of an acquittal of the accused.

Procedure:

Offences specified in Table (first two columns) may be compounded by persons in third column

Offences in second Table may be compounded with Court permission

Abetment or attempt of compoundable offence may be compounded in like manner

Child/unsound mind: person competent to contract on his behalf may with Court permission compound

Person dead: legal representative may with Court consent compound

If accused committed for trial or conviction appealed: composition requires leave of Court to which committed or where appeal pending

High Court or Court of Session in revision may allow compounding

No compounding if accused by reason of previous conviction liable to enhanced punishment

Composition = acquittal

Table of Compoundable Offences (Partial - BNS sections):

84 (enticing married woman) - by husband and woman

115(2) (voluntarily causing hurt) - person to whom hurt caused

122(1) (hurt on provocation) - person to whom hurt caused

126(2),127(2) (wrongful restraint/confine) - person restrained/confined

131,133,136 (assault/criminal force) - person assaulted

303(2) (theft) - owner of property stolen

314 (dishonest misappropriation) - owner of property

316(3) (criminal breach of trust by carrier) - owner of property

317(2) (receiving stolen property) - owner of property stolen

318(2) (cheating) - person cheated

351(2),(3) (criminal intimidation) - person intimidated

352 (insult) - person insulted

356(2) (defamation) - person defamed

SECTION 360 - WITHDRAWAL FROM PROSECUTION
Core Content:
The Public Prosecutor or Assistant Public Prosecutor in charge of a case may, with the consent of the Court, at any time before the judgment is pronounced, withdraw from the prosecution of any person either generally or in respect of any one or more of the offences for which he is tried. If withdrawal before charge framed, accused discharged. If after charge framed, accused acquitted. Where the offence was against Union executive power, or investigated under Central Act, or involved Central Government property, or committed by Central Government servant, and Prosecutor not appointed by Central Government, he must have Central Government permission. No Court shall allow withdrawal without giving opportunity of being heard to the victim.

Procedure:

Public Prosecutor/Assistant Public Prosecutor may with Court consent withdraw from prosecution at any time before judgment

Before charge framed → accused discharged

After charge framed (or no charge required) → accused acquitted

For specified categories (Union executive power, Central Act investigation, Central Government property, Central Government servant) and Prosecutor not appointed by Central Government → need Central Government permission

Court shall not allow withdrawal without hearing victim

SECTION 361 - PROCEDURE IN CASES WHICH MAGISTRATE CANNOT DISPOSE OF
Core Content:
If, in the course of any inquiry or trial before a Magistrate, the evidence appears to him to warrant a presumption that he has no jurisdiction, or that the case should be tried by another Magistrate in the district, or that it should be tried by the Chief Judicial Magistrate, he shall stay the proceedings and submit the case with a brief report to the Chief Judicial Magistrate or to such other Magistrate having jurisdiction as the Chief Judicial Magistrate directs. The Magistrate to whom the case is submitted may, if so empowered, either try the case himself, or refer it to any Magistrate subordinate to him having jurisdiction, or commit the accused for trial.

SECTION 362 - PROCEDURE WHEN AFTER COMMENCEMENT OF INQUIRY OR TRIAL, MAGISTRATE FINDS CASE SHOULD BE COMMITTED
Core Content:
If, in any inquiry into an offence or a trial before a Magistrate, it appears to him at any stage of the proceedings before signing the judgment that the case is one which ought to be tried by the Court of Session, he shall commit it to that Court under the provisions hereinbefore contained and thereupon the provisions of Chapter XIX shall apply to the commitment so made.

SECTION 363 - TRIAL OF PERSONS PREVIOUSLY CONVICTED OF OFFENCES AGAINST COINAGE, STAMP-LAW OR PROPERTY
Core Content:
Where a person, having been convicted of an offence punishable under Chapter X or Chapter XVII of BNS with imprisonment for a term of three years or upwards, is again accused of any offence punishable under either of those Chapters with imprisonment for a term of three years or upwards, and the Magistrate is satisfied that there is ground for presuming that such person has committed the offence, he shall be sent for trial to the Chief Judicial Magistrate or committed to the Court of Session, unless the Magistrate is competent to try the case and can himself pass an adequate sentence. Any other person accused jointly shall be similarly sent or committed, unless discharged.

SECTION 364 - PROCEDURE WHEN MAGISTRATE CANNOT PASS SENTENCE SUFFICIENTLY SEVERE
Core Content:
Whenever a Magistrate is of opinion, after hearing the evidence for the prosecution and the accused, that the accused is guilty, and that he ought to receive a punishment different in kind from, or more severe than, that which such Magistrate is empowered to inflict, he may record the opinion and submit his proceedings, and forward the accused, to the Chief Judicial Magistrate. When more accused persons than one are being tried together, and the Magistrate considers it necessary to proceed under this section in regard to any of such accused, he shall forward all the accused who are in his opinion guilty to the Chief Judicial Magistrate. The Chief Judicial Magistrate may examine parties, recall witnesses, take further evidence, and pass such judgment, sentence or order as he thinks fit according to law.

SECTION 365 - CONVICTION OR COMMITMENT ON EVIDENCE PARTLY RECORDED BY ONE MAGISTRATE AND PARTLY BY ANOTHER
Core Content:
Whenever any Judge or Magistrate, after having heard and recorded the whole or any part of the evidence in any inquiry or trial, ceases to exercise jurisdiction therein and is succeeded by another Judge or Magistrate who has and who exercises such jurisdiction, the succeeding Judge or Magistrate may act on the evidence so recorded by his predecessor, or partly recorded by his predecessor and partly recorded by himself. If the succeeding Judge or Magistrate is of opinion that further examination of any witness whose evidence has already been recorded is necessary in the interests of justice, he may re-summon any such witness, and after such further examination, cross-examination and re-examination, the witness shall be discharged. When a case is transferred from one Judge to another Judge or from one Magistrate to another Magistrate, the former shall be deemed to cease to exercise jurisdiction and to be succeeded by the latter. This section does not apply to summary trials or to cases where proceedings stayed under section 361 or submitted under section 364.

SECTION 366 - COURT TO BE OPEN
Core Content:
The place in which any Criminal Court is held for the purpose of inquiring into or trying any offence shall be deemed to be an open Court, to which the public generally may have access, so far as the same can conveniently contain them. The presiding Judge or Magistrate may order at any stage that the public generally, or any particular person, shall not have access. The inquiry into and trial of rape or offence under BNS sections 64-71 or under POCSO sections 4,6,8,10 shall be conducted in camera. In camera trial shall be conducted as far as practicable by a woman Judge or Magistrate. It shall not be lawful for any person to print or publish any matter in relation to any such proceedings except with previous permission of the Court. The ban on printing or publication of trial proceedings in relation to rape may be lifted, subject to maintaining confidentiality of name and address of the parties.

Procedure:

Court is open to public generally

Presiding Judge/Magistrate may order exclusion of public or any particular person

Rape/sexual offences/POCSO: trial shall be in camera

In camera trial as far as practicable by woman Judge/Magistrate

No printing/publishing of such proceedings without Court permission

Ban on printing/publishing rape proceedings may be lifted while maintaining confidentiality of names and addresses

BNSS CHAPTER XXVII: PROVISIONS AS TO ACCUSED PERSONS OF UNSOUND MIND (Sections 367-378)
SECTION 367 - PROCEDURE IN CASE OF ACCUSED BEING PERSON OF UNSOUND MIND
Core Content:
When a Magistrate holding an inquiry has reason to believe that the person against whom the inquiry is being held is a person of unsound mind and consequently incapable of making his defence, the Magistrate shall inquire into the fact of such unsoundness of mind, and shall cause such person to be examined by the civil surgeon of the district or such other medical officer as the State Government may direct. If the civil surgeon finds the accused to be a person of unsound mind, he shall refer such person to a psychiatrist or clinical psychologist for care, treatment and prognosis. The psychiatrist or clinical psychologist shall inform the Magistrate whether the accused is suffering from unsoundness of mind or intellectual disability. The accused may appeal to the Medical Board (head of psychiatry unit in nearest Government hospital and a faculty member in psychiatry in nearest Government medical college) if aggrieved.

Procedure:

Magistrate believes accused of unsound mind, incapable of defence

Inquire into fact of unsoundness

Cause examination by civil surgeon or other medical officer

If civil surgeon finds unsound mind, refer to psychiatrist/clinical psychologist for care, treatment, prognosis

Psychiatrist/clinical psychologist informs Magistrate whether accused suffering from unsoundness of mind or intellectual disability

Accused may appeal to Medical Board

Pending examination, Magistrate may deal with accused under section 369

If informed accused is person of unsound mind, Magistrate determines whether incapable of entering defence

If found incapable, Magistrate examines record of prosecution evidence, hears advocate without questioning accused

If no prima facie case, discharge accused and deal under section 369

If prima facie case, postpone proceedings for treatment period and order under section 369

If intellectual disability renders accused incapable of entering defence, Magistrate shall order closure of inquiry and deal under section 369

SECTION 368 - PROCEDURE IN CASE OF PERSON OF UNSOUND MIND TRIED BEFORE COURT
Core Content:
If at the trial of any person before a Magistrate or Court of Session, it appears that such person is of unsound mind and consequently incapable of making his defence, the Magistrate or Court shall try the fact of such unsoundness and incapacity. If satisfied, he or it shall record a finding to that effect and postpone further proceedings. If during trial the accused is found to be of unsound mind, refer to psychiatrist/clinical psychologist for care and treatment. If found incapable of entering defence, examine record of prosecution evidence, hear advocate without questioning accused. If no prima facie case, discharge accused and deal under section 369. If prima facie case, postpone trial for treatment period. If intellectual disability renders accused incapable of entering defence, shall not hold trial and order accused to be dealt with under section 369.

SECTION 369 - RELEASE OF PERSON OF UNSOUND MIND PENDING INVESTIGATION OR TRIAL
Core Content:
Whenever a person is found under section 367 or 368 to be incapable of entering defence by reason of unsoundness of mind or intellectual disability, the Magistrate or Court shall order release of such person on bail, provided the accused is suffering from unsoundness of mind or intellectual disability which does not mandate in-patient treatment and a friend or relative undertakes to obtain regular out-patient psychiatric treatment and to prevent injury to himself or others. If bail cannot be granted or appropriate undertaking not given, order accused to be kept in a place where regular psychiatric treatment can be provided. If the Magistrate or Court decides to order discharge of the accused, such release may be ordered if sufficient security is given. If discharge cannot be ordered, transfer of accused to a residential facility may be ordered.

SECTION 370 - RESUMPTION OF INQUIRY OR TRIAL
Core Content:
Whenever an inquiry or trial is postponed under section 367 or 368, the Magistrate or Court may at any time after the person concerned has ceased to be of unsound mind, resume the inquiry or trial and require the accused to appear or be brought before such Magistrate or Court. When the accused has been released under section 369, and the sureties for his appearance produce him to the officer whom the Magistrate or Court appoints, the certificate of such officer that the accused is capable of making his defence shall be receivable in evidence.

SECTION 371 - PROCEDURE ON ACCUSED APPEARING BEFORE MAGISTRATE OR COURT
Core Content:
If, when the accused appears or is again brought before the Magistrate or Court, the Magistrate or Court considers him capable of making his defence, the inquiry or trial shall proceed. If the Magistrate or Court considers the accused to be still incapable, the Magistrate or Court shall act according to section 367 or 368, and if found to be of unsound mind and incapable, shall deal with such accused in accordance with section 369.

SECTION 372 - WHEN ACCUSED APPEARS TO HAVE BEEN OF SOUND MIND
Core Content:
When the accused appears to be of sound mind at the time of inquiry or trial, and the Magistrate is satisfied from the evidence given before him that there is reason to believe that the accused committed an act which, if he had been of sound mind, would have been an offence, and that he was, at the time when the act was committed, by reason of unsoundness of mind, incapable of knowing the nature of the act or that it was wrong or contrary to law, the Magistrate shall proceed with the case, and, if the accused ought to be tried by the Court of Session, commit him for trial before the Court of Session.

SECTION 373 - JUDGMENT OF ACQUITTAL ON GROUND OF UNSOUNDNESS OF MIND
Core Content:
Whenever any person is acquitted upon the ground that, at the time at which he is alleged to have committed an offence, he was, by reason of unsoundness of mind, incapable of knowing the nature of the act alleged as constituting the offence, or that it was wrong or contrary to law, the finding shall state specifically whether he committed the act or not.

SECTION 374 - PERSON ACQUITTED ON GROUND OF UNSOUNDNESS OF MIND TO BE DETAINED IN SAFE CUSTODY
Core Content:
Whenever the finding states that the accused person committed the act alleged, the Magistrate or Court shall, if such act would, but for the incapacity found, have constituted an offence, order such person to be detained in safe custody or delivered to any relative or friend. No order for detention in a public mental health establishment shall be made otherwise than in accordance with rules under Mental Healthcare Act, 2017. No order for delivery to relative or friend shall be made except upon application of such relative or friend and on his giving security that the person shall be properly taken care of, prevented from doing injury, and produced for inspection.

SECTION 375 - POWER OF STATE GOVERNMENT TO EMPOWER OFFICER IN CHARGE TO DISCHARGE
Core Content:
The State Government may empower the officer in charge of the jail in which a person is confined under section 369 or 374 to discharge all or any of the functions of the Inspector-General of Prisons under section 376 or 377.

SECTION 376 - PROCEDURE WHERE PRISONER OF UNSOUND MIND IS REPORTED CAPABLE OF MAKING HIS DEFENCE
Core Content:
If a person is detained under section 369(2), and in the case of a person detained in a jail, the Inspector-General of Prisons, or in the case of a person detained in a public mental health establishment, the Mental Health Review Board, certifies that such person is capable of making his defence, he shall be taken before the Magistrate or Court at such time as appointed, and the Magistrate or Court shall deal with such person under section 371. The certificate shall be receivable as evidence.

SECTION 377 - PROCEDURE WHERE PERSON OF UNSOUND MIND DETAINED IS DECLARED FIT TO BE RELEASED
Core Content:
