If a person is detained under section 369(2) or 374, and the Inspector-General or Mental Health Review Board certifies that he may be released without danger of his doing injury to himself or to any other person, the State Government may order him to be released, or to be detained in custody, or to be transferred to a public mental health establishment. If ordered to be transferred to a public mental health establishment, the State Government may appoint a Commission consisting of a Judicial and two medical officers. Such Commission shall make a formal inquiry into the state of mind of such person, take such evidence as is necessary, and shall report to the State Government, which may order his release or detention as it thinks fit.

SECTION 378 - DELIVERY OF PERSON OF UNSOUND MIND TO CARE OF RELATIVE OR FRIEND
Core Content:
Whenever any relative or friend of any person detained under section 369 or 374 desires that he shall be delivered to his care and custody, the State Government may, upon application of such relative or friend and on his giving security, order such person to be delivered. If the person so delivered is accused of any offence, and the inspecting officer certifies at any time that such person is capable of making his defence, such Magistrate or Court shall call upon the relative or friend to produce him before the Magistrate or Court, and upon such production proceed under section 371. The certificate of the inspecting officer shall be receivable as evidence.

BNSS CHAPTER XXVIII: PROVISIONS AS TO OFFENCES AFFECTING THE ADMINISTRATION OF JUSTICE (Sections 379-391)
SECTION 379 - PROCEDURE IN CASES MENTIONED IN SECTION 215
Core Content:
When, upon an application made to it or otherwise, any Court is of opinion that it is expedient in the interests of justice that an inquiry should be made into any offence referred to in section 215(1)(b) (offences against public justice committed in or in relation to a proceeding in that Court or in respect of a document produced in evidence), such Court may, after such preliminary inquiry as it thinks necessary, record a finding to that effect, make a complaint thereof in writing, send it to a Magistrate of the first class having jurisdiction, take sufficient security for the appearance of the accused, and bind over any person to appear and give evidence.

Procedure:

Court of opinion expedient to inquire into section 215(1)(b) offence

After preliminary inquiry if necessary

Record finding

Make complaint in writing

Send to first class Magistrate having jurisdiction

Take security for appearance of accused (or send in custody if non-bailable)

Bind over any person to appear and give evidence

SECTION 380 - APPEAL
Core Content:
Any person on whose application any Court other than a High Court has refused to make a complaint under section 379, or against whom such a complaint has been made, may appeal to the Court to which such former Court is subordinate, and the superior Court may direct withdrawal of the complaint or making of the complaint. An order under this section shall be final and not subject to revision.

SECTION 381 - POWER TO ORDER COSTS
Core Content:
Any Court dealing with an application for filing a complaint under section 379 or an appeal under section 380, shall have power to make such order as to costs as may be just.

SECTION 382 - PROCEDURE OF MAGISTRATE TAKING COGNIZANCE
Core Content:
A Magistrate to whom a complaint is made under section 379 or 380 shall, notwithstanding anything in Chapter XVI, proceed, as far as may be, to deal with the case as if it were instituted on a police report. Where it is brought to the notice of such Magistrate that an appeal is pending against the decision arrived at in the judicial proceeding out of which the matter has arisen, he may, if he thinks fit, at any stage, adjourn the hearing of the case until such appeal is decided.

SECTION 383 - SUMMARY PROCEDURE FOR TRIAL FOR GIVING FALSE EVIDENCE
Core Content:
If, at the time of delivery of any judgment or final order disposing of any judicial proceeding, a Court of Session or Magistrate of the first class expresses an opinion to the effect that any witness had knowingly or wilfully given false evidence or had fabricated false evidence with the intention that such evidence should be used in such proceeding, it or he may, if satisfied that it is necessary and expedient in the interest of justice that the witness should be tried summarily, take cognizance of the offence and may, after giving the offender a reasonable opportunity of showing cause, try such offender summarily and sentence him to imprisonment for a term which may extend to three months, or to fine which may extend to one thousand rupees, or with both. If an appeal or revision is preferred against the judgment or order, the Court shall stay further proceedings until disposal of the appeal or revision.

SECTION 384 - PROCEDURE IN CERTAIN CASES OF CONTEMPT
Core Content:
When any such offence as is described in section 210, 213, 214, 215 or 267 of BNS is committed in the view or presence of any Civil, Criminal, or Revenue Court, the Court may cause the offender to be detained in custody, and may, at any time before the rising of the Court on the same day, take cognizance of the offence and, after giving the offender a reasonable opportunity of showing cause, sentence the offender to fine not exceeding one thousand rupees, and, in default of payment of fine, to simple imprisonment for a term which may extend to one month.

Procedure:

Offence under BNS 210,213,214,215,267 committed in view/presence of Court

Court may detain offender in custody

Before rising of Court on same day, take cognizance

Give reasonable opportunity to show cause

Sentence to fine ≤₹1,000, in default simple imprisonment up to 1 month

SECTION 385 - PROCEDURE WHERE COURT CONSIDERS THAT CASE SHOULD NOT BE DEALT WITH UNDER SECTION 384
Core Content:
If the Court considers that a person accused of any of the offences referred to in section 384 should be imprisoned otherwise than in default of fine, or that a fine exceeding two hundred rupees should be imposed, or is for any other reason of opinion that the case should not be disposed of under section 384, such Court, after recording the facts and the statement of the accused, may forward the case to a Magistrate having jurisdiction to try the same, and may require security for appearance.

SECTION 386 - WHEN REGISTRAR OR SUB-REGISTRAR TO BE DEEMED A CIVIL COURT
Core Content:
When the State Government so directs, any Registrar or any Sub-Registrar appointed under the Registration Act, 1908, shall be deemed to be a Civil Court within the meaning of sections 384 and 385.

SECTION 387 - DISCHARGE OF OFFENDER ON SUBMISSION OF APOLOGY
Core Content:
When any Court has under section 384 adjudged an offender to punishment, or has under section 385 forwarded him to a Magistrate for trial, for refusing or omitting to do anything which he was lawfully required to do or for any intentional insult or interruption, the Court may, in its discretion, discharge the offender or remit the punishment on his submission to the order or requisition of such Court, or on apology being made to its satisfaction.

SECTION 388 - IMPRISONMENT OR COMMITTAL OF PERSON REFUSING TO ANSWER OR PRODUCE DOCUMENT
Core Content:
If any witness or person called to produce a document or thing before a Criminal Court refuses to answer such questions as are put to him or to produce any document or thing in his possession which the Court requires him to produce, and does not, after a reasonable opportunity has been given to him, offer any reasonable excuse for such refusal, such Court may, for reasons recorded, sentence him to simple imprisonment, or commit him to custody for any term not exceeding seven days, unless in the meantime he consents to be examined and to answer, or to produce the document or thing. If he persists in his refusal, he may be dealt with under section 384 or 385.

Key Time Limit: Committal not exceeding 7 days

SECTION 389 - SUMMARY PROCEDURE FOR PUNISHMENT FOR NON-ATTENDANCE BY A WITNESS IN OBEDIENCE TO SUMMONS
Core Content:
If any witness being summoned to appear before a Criminal Court is legally bound to appear at a certain place and time in obedience to the summons and without just excuse neglects or refuses to attend at that place or time or departs before the time at which it is lawful for him to depart, and the Court is satisfied that it is expedient in the interests of justice that such a witness should be tried summarily, the Court may take cognizance of the offence and after giving the offender an opportunity of showing cause, sentence him to fine not exceeding five hundred rupees.

SECTION 390 - APPEALS FROM CONVICTIONS UNDER SECTIONS 383, 384, 388 AND 389
Core Content:
Any person sentenced by any Court other than a High Court under section 383, 384, 388, or 389 may, notwithstanding anything in this Sanhita, appeal to the Court to which decrees or orders made in such Court are ordinarily appealable. The provisions of Chapter XXXI shall apply to such appeals. An appeal from conviction by a Court of Small Causes shall lie to the Court of Session. An appeal from conviction by any Registrar or Sub-Registrar deemed to be a Civil Court shall lie to the Court of Session.

SECTION 391 - CERTAIN JUDGES AND MAGISTRATES NOT TO TRY CERTAIN OFFENCES WHEN COMMITTED BEFORE THEMSELVES
Core Content:
Except as provided in sections 383, 384, 388 and 389, no Judge of a Criminal Court (other than a Judge of a High Court) or Magistrate shall try any person for any offence referred to in section 215, when such offence is committed before himself or in contempt of his authority, or is brought under his notice as such Judge or Magistrate in the course of a judicial proceeding.

BNSS CHAPTER XXIX: THE JUDGMENT (Sections 392-406)
SECTION 392 - JUDGMENT
Core Content:
The judgment in every trial in any Criminal Court of original jurisdiction shall be pronounced in open Court by the presiding officer immediately after termination of trial or at some subsequent time not later than forty-five days, of which notice shall be given to the parties or their advocates. Pronouncement may be by delivering the whole judgment, reading out the whole judgment, or reading out the operative part and explaining the substance in a language understood by the accused or his advocate. If the accused is in custody, he shall be brought up to hear judgment either in person or through audio-video electronic means. The Court shall, as far as practicable, upload a copy of the judgment on its portal within seven days.

Key Time Limits: Judgment within 45 days of trial termination; upload within 7 days

SECTION 393 - LANGUAGE AND CONTENTS OF JUDGMENT
Core Content:
Every judgment shall be written in the language of the Court, shall contain the points for determination, the decision thereon and the reasons, shall specify the offence and section under which convicted and the punishment. If judgment of acquittal, state the offence of which accused is acquitted. When conviction is for an offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life or imprisonment for a term of years, the judgment shall state the reasons for the sentence awarded, and in case of sentence of death, the special reasons for such sentence. When any person is sentenced to death, the sentence shall direct that he be hanged by the neck till he is dead.

SECTION 394 - ORDER FOR NOTIFYING ADDRESS OF PREVIOUSLY CONVICTED OFFENDER
Core Content:
When any person, having been convicted of an offence punishable with imprisonment for a term of three years or upwards, is again convicted of any offence punishable with imprisonment for a term of three years or upwards, the Court may order that his residence and any change of, or absence from, such residence after release be notified for a term not exceeding five years from the date of expiration of sentence. If the conviction is set aside, such order becomes void. The State Government may make rules for carrying out the provisions.

SECTION 395 - ORDER TO PAY COMPENSATION
Core Content:
When a Court imposes a sentence of fine or a sentence of which fine forms a part, the Court may order the whole or any part of the fine recovered to be applied in defraying expenses of prosecution, in payment to any person of compensation for any loss or injury caused by the offence, in paying compensation to persons entitled under Fatal Accidents Act, 1855, or in compensating any bona fide purchaser of stolen property if such property is restored to the person entitled thereto. When a Court imposes a sentence of which fine does not form a part, the Court may order the accused person to pay by way of compensation such amount as may be specified to the person who has suffered any loss or injury. No such payment shall be made before the period for appeal has elapsed, or if appeal presented, before decision of appeal.

SECTION 396 - VICTIM COMPENSATION SCHEME
Core Content:
Every State Government in co-ordination with Central Government shall prepare a scheme for providing funds for compensation to the victim or his dependents who have suffered loss or injury and who require rehabilitation. When Court recommends compensation, the District Legal Service Authority or State Legal Service Authority shall decide the quantum. If the trial Court is satisfied that compensation awarded under section 395 is not adequate for rehabilitation, or where cases end in acquittal or discharge and victim has to be rehabilitated, it may make recommendation for compensation. Where offender is not traced or identified, the victim or his dependents may apply to the State or District Legal Services Authority for compensation. The Authority shall complete enquiry within two months. The Authority may order immediate first-aid or medical benefits free of cost on certificate of police officer not below SHO or Magistrate.

Key Time Limit: Enquiry within 2 months

SECTION 397 - TREATMENT OF VICTIMS
Core Content:
All hospitals, public or private, whether run by Central Government, State Government, local bodies or any other person, shall immediately provide the first-aid or medical treatment, free of cost, to the victims of any offence covered under BNS sections 64-71 or 124(1) or under POCSO sections 4,6,8,10, and shall immediately inform the police of such incident.

SECTION 398 - WITNESS PROTECTION SCHEME
Core Content:
Every State Government shall prepare and notify a Witness Protection Scheme for the State with a view to ensure protection of the witnesses.

SECTION 399 - COMPENSATION TO PERSONS GROUNDLESSLY ARRESTED
Core Content:
Whenever any person causes a police officer to arrest another person, if it appears to the Magistrate that there was no sufficient ground for causing such arrest, the Magistrate may award such compensation, not exceeding one thousand rupees, to be paid by the person so causing the arrest to the person so arrested. If more persons than one are arrested, compensation may be awarded to each. Compensation may be recovered as if it were a fine, and if not recovered, the person by whom it is payable shall be sentenced to simple imprisonment for such term not exceeding thirty days.

SECTION 400 - ORDER TO PAY COSTS IN NON-COGNIZABLE CASES
Core Content:
Whenever any complaint of a non-cognizable offence is made to a Court, the Court, if it convicts the accused, may, in addition to the penalty imposed, order him to pay to the complainant, in whole or in part, the cost incurred by him in the prosecution, and may further order that in default of payment, the accused shall suffer simple imprisonment for a period not exceeding thirty days. Such costs may include expenses in respect of process-fees, witnesses and advocate's fees.

SECTION 401 - ORDER TO RELEASE ON PROBATION OF GOOD CONDUCT OR AFTER ADMONITION
Core Content:
When any person not under twenty-one years of age is convicted of an offence punishable with fine only or with imprisonment for a term of seven years or less, or when any person under twenty-one years of age or any woman is convicted of an offence not punishable with death or imprisonment for life, and no previous conviction is proved, the Court may, instead of sentencing him at once, direct that he be released on his entering into a bond or bail bond to appear and receive sentence when called upon during such period (not exceeding three years) and in the meantime to keep the peace and be of good behavior. In any case where a person is convicted of theft, theft in a building, dishonest misappropriation, cheating or any offence punishable with not more than two years' imprisonment or any offence punishable with fine only and no previous conviction is proved, the Court may, if it thinks fit, release him after due admonition.

SECTION 402 - SPECIAL REASONS TO BE RECORDED IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
Where in any case the Court could have dealt with an accused person under section 401 or under the Probation of Offenders Act, 1958, or a youthful offender under the Juvenile Justice Act, 2015, but has not done so, it shall record in its judgment the special reasons for not having done so.

SECTION 403 - COURT NOT TO ALTER JUDGMENT
Core Content:
Save as otherwise provided by this Sanhita or by any other law for the time being in force, no Court, when it has signed its judgment or final order disposing of a case, shall alter or review the same except to correct a clerical or arithmetical error.

SECTION 404 - COPY OF JUDGMENT TO BE GIVEN TO ACCUSED AND OTHER PERSONS
Core Content:
When the accused is sentenced to imprisonment, a copy of the judgment shall, immediately after pronouncement, be given to him free of cost. On application of the accused, a certified copy of the judgment, or a translation in his own language if practicable, shall be given without delay, and where the judgment is appealable, given free of cost. Where a sentence of death is passed or confirmed, a certified copy shall be immediately given free of cost. The Court shall inform the accused of the period within which to appeal if sentenced to death and an appeal lies as of right.

SECTION 405 - JUDGMENT WHEN TO BE TRANSLATED
Core Content:
The original judgment shall be filed with the record of the proceedings and where the original is recorded in a language different from that of the Court, and if either party so requires, a translation thereof into the language of the Court shall be added to such record.

SECTION 406 - COURT OF SESSION TO SEND COPY OF FINDING AND SENTENCE TO DISTRICT MAGISTRATE
Core Content:
In cases tried by the Court of Session or a Chief Judicial Magistrate, the Court or such Magistrate shall forward a copy of its or his finding and sentence (if any) to the District Magistrate within whose local jurisdiction the trial was held.

BNSS CHAPTER XXX: SUBMISSION OF DEATH SENTENCES FOR CONFIRMATION (Sections 407-412)
SECTION 407 - SENTENCE OF DEATH TO BE SUBMITTED BY COURT OF SESSION FOR CONFIRMATION
Core Content:
When the Court of Session passes a sentence of death, the proceedings shall forthwith be submitted to the High Court, and the sentence shall not be executed unless it is confirmed by the High Court. The Court passing the sentence shall commit the convicted person to jail custody under a warrant.

SECTION 408 - POWER TO DIRECT FURTHER INQUIRY TO BE MADE OR ADDITIONAL EVIDENCE TO BE TAKEN
Core Content:
If, when such proceedings are submitted, the High Court thinks that a further inquiry should be made into, or additional evidence taken upon, any point bearing upon the guilt or innocence of the convicted person, it may make such inquiry or take such evidence itself, or direct it to be made or taken by the Court of Session. Unless the High Court otherwise directs, the presence of the convicted person may be dispensed with.

SECTION 409 - POWER OF HIGH COURT TO CONFIRM SENTENCE OR ANNUL CONVICTION
Core Content:
In any case submitted under section 407, the High Court may confirm the sentence, or pass any other sentence warranted by law; or may annul the conviction, and convict the accused of any offence of which the Court of Session might have convicted him, or order a new trial; or may acquit the accused person. No order of confirmation shall be made until the period allowed for preferring an appeal has expired, or, if an appeal is presented within such period, until such appeal is disposed of.

SECTION 410 - CONFIRMATION OR NEW SENTENCE TO BE SIGNED BY TWO JUDGES
Core Content:
In every case so submitted, the confirmation of the sentence, or any new sentence or order passed by the High Court, shall, when such Court consists of two or more Judges, be made, passed and signed by at least two of them.

SECTION 411 - PROCEDURE IN CASE OF DIFFERENCE OF OPINION
Core Content:
Where any such case is heard before a Bench of Judges and such Judges are equally divided in opinion, the case shall be decided in the manner provided by section 433 (reference to another Judge).

SECTION 412 - PROCEDURE IN CASES SUBMITTED TO HIGH COURT FOR CONFIRMATION
Core Content:
In cases submitted by the Court of Session to the High Court for the confirmation of a sentence of death, the proper officer of the High Court shall, without delay, after the order of confirmation or other order has been made, send either physically or through electronic means, a copy of the order, under the seal of the High Court and attested with his official signature, to the Court of Session.

BNSS CHAPTER XXXI: APPEALS (Sections 413-435)
SECTION 413 - NO APPEAL TO LIE UNLESS OTHERWISE PROVIDED
Core Content:
No appeal shall lie from any judgment or order of a Criminal Court except as provided by this Sanhita or by any other law. The victim shall have a right to prefer an appeal against any order acquitting the accused or convicting for a lesser offence or imposing inadequate compensation, and such appeal shall lie to the Court to which an appeal ordinarily lies against the order of conviction of such Court.

Note: Victim has statutory right to appeal against acquittal, lesser offence, or inadequate compensation.

SECTION 414 - APPEAL FROM ORDERS REQUIRING SECURITY OR REFUSAL TO ACCEPT OR REJECTING SURETY
Core Content:
Any person who has been ordered under section 136 to give security for keeping the peace or for good behaviour, or who is aggrieved by any order refusing to accept or rejecting a surety under section 140, may appeal against such order to the Court of Session.

SECTION 415 - APPEALS FROM CONVICTIONS
Core Content:
Any person convicted on a trial held by a High Court in its extraordinary original criminal jurisdiction may appeal to the Supreme Court. Any person convicted on a trial held by a Sessions Judge or Additional Sessions Judge or on a trial held by any other Court in which a sentence of imprisonment for more than seven years has been passed may appeal to the High Court. Any person convicted on a trial held by a Magistrate of the first class or second class, or sentenced under section 364, or in respect of whom an order has been made or sentence passed under section 401 by any Magistrate, may appeal to the Court of Session. For appeals against sentence under BNS sections 64-71 (rape, etc.), the appeal shall be disposed of within six months.

Key Time Limit: Rape/sexual offence appeals: 6 months

SECTION 416 - NO APPEAL IN CERTAIN CASES WHEN ACCUSED PLEADS GUILTY
Core Content:
Where an accused person has pleaded guilty and has been convicted on such plea, there shall be no appeal if the conviction is by a High Court; or if the conviction is by a Court of Session or Magistrate of first or second class, except as to the extent or legality of the sentence.

SECTION 417 - NO APPEAL IN PETTY CASES
Core Content:
No appeal by a convicted person in petty cases: where High Court passes only sentence of imprisonment ≤3 months or fine ≤₹1,000; where Court of Session passes only sentence of imprisonment ≤3 months or fine ≤₹200; where first class Magistrate passes only sentence of fine ≤₹100; where in summary trial Magistrate passes only sentence of fine ≤₹200. Exception: appeal allowed if any other punishment combined with it.

SECTION 418 - APPEAL BY STATE GOVERNMENT AGAINST SENTENCE
Core Content:
State Government may direct Public Prosecutor to present an appeal against sentence on ground of inadequacy: to Court of Session if sentence by Magistrate; to High Court if sentence by any other Court. Central Government may also direct for offences investigated by Central agency. Court shall not enhance sentence without giving accused reasonable opportunity to show cause. For appeals against sentence under BNS sections 64-71 (rape, etc.), appeal shall be disposed of within six months.

Key Time Limit: Rape/sexual offence appeals: 6 months

SECTION 419 - APPEAL IN CASE OF ACQUITTAL
Core Content:
District Magistrate may direct Public Prosecutor to appeal to Court of Session from order of acquittal passed by Magistrate in respect of cognizable and non-bailable offence. State Government may direct Public Prosecutor to appeal to High Court from original or appellate order of acquittal by any Court other than High Court. Central Government may also direct for offences investigated by Central agency. No appeal to High Court under this section except with leave of High Court. Complainant may present appeal to High Court if High Court grants special leave on application within six months (if complainant public servant) or sixty days (otherwise). If special leave refused, no appeal lies under sub-section (1) or (2).

Key Time Limits: 6 months (public servant complainant); 60 days (other complainants)

SECTION 420 - APPEAL AGAINST CONVICTION BY HIGH COURT IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
Where the High Court has, on appeal, reversed an order of acquittal of an accused person and convicted him and sentenced him to death or to imprisonment for life or to imprisonment for a term of ten years or more, he may appeal to the Supreme Court.

SECTION 421 - SPECIAL RIGHT OF APPEAL IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
When more persons than one are convicted in one trial, and an appealable judgment or order has been passed in respect of any of such persons, all or any of the persons convicted at such trial shall have a right of appeal.

SECTION 422 - APPEAL TO COURT OF SESSION HOW HEARD
Core Content:
An appeal to the Court of Session or Sessions Judge shall be heard by the Sessions Judge or by an Additional Sessions Judge. An appeal against a conviction on a trial held by a Magistrate of the second class may be heard and disposed of by the Chief Judicial Magistrate. An Additional Sessions Judge or Chief Judicial Magistrate shall hear only such appeals as the Sessions Judge makes over to him or as the High Court directs.

SECTION 423 - PETITION OF APPEAL
Core Content:
Every appeal shall be made in the form of a petition in writing presented by the appellant or his advocate, and shall (unless the Court otherwise directs) be accompanied by a copy of the judgment or order appealed against.

SECTION 424 - PROCEDURE WHEN APPELLANT IN JAIL
Core Content:
If the appellant is in jail, he may present his petition of appeal and the copies to the officer in charge of the jail, who shall thereupon forward such petition and copies to the proper Appellate Court.

SECTION 425 - SUMMARY DISMISSAL OF APPEAL
Core Content:
If upon examining the petition of appeal and copy of the judgment, the Appellate Court considers that there is no sufficient ground for interfering, it may dismiss the appeal summarily. No appeal presented under section 423 shall be dismissed unless the appellant or his advocate has had a reasonable opportunity of being heard. No appeal presented under section 424 shall be dismissed except after giving the appellant a reasonable opportunity of being heard, unless the Court considers the appeal frivolous.

SECTION 426 - PROCEDURE FOR HEARING APPEALS NOT DISMISSED SUMMARILY
Core Content:
If the Appellate Court does not dismiss the appeal summarily, it shall cause notice of the time and place of hearing to be given to the appellant or his advocate, to such officer as State Government appoints, and if appeal from conviction in complaint case, to the complainant, and if appeal under section 418 or 419, to the accused. The Appellate Court shall then send for the record and hear the parties. If the appeal is only as to the extent or legality of sentence, the Court may dispose of without sending for the record.

SECTION 427 - POWERS OF APPELLATE COURT
Core Content:
After perusing the record and hearing the parties, the Appellate Court may, if it considers no sufficient ground for interfering, dismiss the appeal, or may: (a) in appeal from acquittal, reverse and direct further inquiry, re-trial, or find guilty and pass sentence; (b) in appeal from conviction, reverse and acquit/discharge or order re-trial, or alter finding maintaining sentence, or alter nature/extent of sentence but not enhance; (c) in appeal for enhancement of sentence, reverse and acquit/discharge, order re-trial, or enhance or reduce sentence; (d) in appeal from any other order, alter or reverse; (e) make any consequential order. Sentence shall not be enhanced unless accused has had opportunity to show cause.

SECTION 428 - JUDGMENTS OF SUBORDINATE APPELLATE COURT
Core Content:
The rules contained in Chapter XXIX as to judgment of original Court shall apply to judgment in appeal of a Court of Session or Chief Judicial Magistrate. Unless the Appellate Court otherwise directs, the accused shall not be brought up or required to attend to hear judgment delivered.

SECTION 429 - ORDER OF HIGH COURT ON APPEAL TO BE CERTIFIED TO LOWER COURT
Core Content:
Whenever a case is decided on appeal by the High Court, it shall certify its judgment or order to the Court by which the finding, sentence or order appealed against was recorded or passed. If such Court is of a Judicial Magistrate other than CJM, the judgment shall be sent through the CJM; if of an Executive Magistrate, through the District Magistrate.

SECTION 430 - SUSPENSION OF SENTENCE PENDING APPEAL; RELEASE OF APPELLANT ON BAIL
Core Content:
Pending any appeal by a convicted person, the Appellate Court may, for reasons recorded, order that execution of sentence be suspended and that he be released on bail or on his own bond. Before releasing a person convicted of an offence punishable with death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for not less than ten years, the Court shall give opportunity to Public Prosecutor to show cause against such release. Where the convicted person satisfies the Court that he intends to present an appeal, the Court shall order him released on bail for such period as will afford sufficient time to present the appeal and obtain orders, if: (i) he is on bail and sentenced to imprisonment ≤3 years; or (ii) the offence is bailable and he is on bail.

SECTION 431 - ARREST OF ACCUSED IN APPEAL FROM ACQUITTAL
Core Content:
When an appeal is presented under section 419, the High Court may issue a warrant directing that the accused be arrested and brought before it or any subordinate Court, and the Court before which he is brought may commit him to prison pending disposal of the appeal or admit him to bail.

SECTION 432 - APPELLATE COURT MAY TAKE FURTHER EVIDENCE OR DIRECT IT TO BE TAKEN
Core Content:
In dealing with any appeal, the Appellate Court, if it thinks additional evidence necessary, shall record its reasons and may either take such evidence itself, or direct it to be taken by a Magistrate or, when the Appellate Court is a High Court, by a Court of Session or a Magistrate. The accused or his advocate shall have the right to be present when additional evidence is taken.

SECTION 433 - PROCEDURE WHERE JUDGES OF COURT OF APPEAL ARE EQUALLY DIVIDED
Core Content:
When an appeal under this Chapter is heard by a High Court before a Bench of Judges and they are divided in opinion, the appeal, with their opinions, shall be laid before another Judge of that Court, and that Judge shall deliver his opinion, and the judgment or order shall follow that opinion. If one of the Judges or that other Judge so requires, the appeal shall be re-heard and decided by a larger Bench.

SECTION 434 - FINALITY OF JUDGMENTS AND ORDERS ON APPEAL
Core Content:
Judgments and orders passed by an Appellate Court upon an appeal shall be final, except in cases provided for in section 418, 419, 425(4) or Chapter XXXII. Notwithstanding final disposal of an appeal against conviction, the Appellate Court may hear and dispose of an appeal against acquittal under section 419 arising out of the same case, or an appeal for enhancement of sentence under section 418 arising out of the same case.

SECTION 435 - ABATEMENT OF APPEALS
Core Content:
Every appeal under section 418 or 419 (appeal against sentence or acquittal by State/Central Government) shall finally abate on the death of the accused. Every other appeal under this Chapter (except from a sentence of fine) shall finally abate on the death of the appellant. Where the appeal is against conviction and sentence of death or imprisonment, and the appellant dies during pendency, any near relative (parent, spouse, lineal descendant, brother or sister) may within thirty days apply for leave to continue the appeal; if leave granted, appeal shall not abate.

Key Time Limit: 30 days for near relative to apply

BNSS CHAPTER XXXII: REFERENCE AND REVISION (Sections 436-445)
SECTION 436 - REFERENCE TO HIGH COURT
Core Content:
Where any Court is satisfied that a case pending before it involves a question as to the validity of any Act, Ordinance or Regulation or of any provision contained therein, the determination of which is necessary for disposal of the case, and is of opinion that such Act, Ordinance, Regulation or provision is invalid or inoperative but has not been so declared by the High Court or Supreme Court, the Court shall state a case setting out its opinion and reasons and refer the same for decision of the High Court. A Court of Session may, if it thinks fit, refer for decision of the High Court any question of law arising in any case pending before it. Any Court making a reference may, pending decision of High Court, either commit accused to jail or release him on bail to appear when called upon.

SECTION 437 - DISPOSAL OF CASE ACCORDING TO DECISION OF HIGH COURT
Core Content:
When a question has been so referred, the High Court shall pass such order thereon as it thinks fit, and shall cause a copy of such order to be sent to the Court by which the reference was made, which shall dispose of the case conformably to the said order. The High Court may direct by whom the costs of such reference shall be paid.

SECTION 438 - CALLING FOR RECORDS TO EXERCISE POWERS OF REVISION
Core Content:
The High Court or any Sessions Judge may call for and examine the record of any proceeding before any inferior Criminal Court situate within its or his local jurisdiction for the purpose of satisfying itself or himself as to the correctness, legality or propriety of any finding, sentence or order, and as to the regularity of any proceedings of such inferior Court. When calling for such record, the High Court or Sessions Judge may direct that execution of any sentence or order be suspended, and if accused is in confinement, that he be released on his own bond or bail bond pending examination of the record. All Magistrates (Executive or Judicial, original or appellate) are deemed to be inferior to the Sessions Judge. The powers of revision shall not be exercised in relation to any interlocutory order. If an application under this section has been made to the High Court or Sessions Judge, no further application by the same person shall be entertained by the other.

SECTION 439 - POWER TO ORDER INQUIRY
Core Content:
On examining any record under section 438 or otherwise, the High Court or the Sessions Judge may direct the Chief Judicial Magistrate by himself or by any subordinate Magistrate to make further inquiry into any complaint which has been dismissed under section 226 or section 227(4), or into the case of any person accused who has been discharged. No Court shall make any direction for inquiry into the case of any person who has been discharged unless such person has had an opportunity of showing cause.

SECTION 440 - SESSIONS JUDGE'S POWERS OF REVISION
Core Content:
In the case of any proceeding the record of which has been called for by himself, the Sessions Judge may exercise all or any of the powers which may be exercised by the High Court under section 442(1). The provisions of sections 442(2),(3),(4),(5) shall apply to such proceeding, with references to High Court construed as references to Sessions Judge. Where any application for revision is made by or on behalf of any person before the Sessions Judge, the decision of the Sessions Judge thereon shall be final and no further proceeding by way of revision shall be entertained by the High Court or any other Court.

SECTION 441 - POWER OF ADDITIONAL SESSIONS JUDGE
Core Content:
An Additional Sessions Judge shall have and may exercise all the powers of a Sessions Judge under this Chapter in respect of any case which may be transferred to him by or under any general or special order of the Sessions Judge.

SECTION 442 - HIGH COURT'S POWERS OF REVISION
Core Content:
In the case of any proceeding the record of which has been called for by itself or which otherwise comes to its knowledge, the High Court may, in its discretion, exercise any of the powers conferred on a Court of Appeal by sections 427, 430, 431 and 432 or on a Court of Session by section 344. When the Judges composing the Court of revision are equally divided in opinion, the case shall be disposed of as provided by section 433. No order under this section shall be made to the prejudice of the accused or other person unless he has had an opportunity of being heard. Nothing authorises a High Court to convert a finding of acquittal into one of conviction. Where an appeal lies and no appeal is brought, no proceeding by way of revision shall be entertained at the instance of the party who could have appealed. Where an appeal lies but an application for revision has been made to the High Court under the erroneous belief that no appeal lies, the High Court may treat the application for revision as a petition of appeal.

SECTION 443 - POWER OF HIGH COURT TO WITHDRAW OR TRANSFER REVISION CASES
Core Content:
Whenever one or more persons convicted at the same trial make application to a High Court for revision and any other person convicted at the same trial makes application to the Sessions Judge for revision, the High Court shall decide which Court should finally dispose of the applications. If the High Court decides to dispose of all applications itself, it shall direct that applications pending before the Sessions Judge be transferred to itself; if it decides not to, it shall direct that applications made to it be transferred to the Sessions Judge.

SECTION 444 - OPTION OF COURT TO HEAR PARTIES
Core Content:
Save as otherwise expressly provided, no party has any right to be heard either personally or by an advocate before any Court exercising its powers of revision; but the Court may, if it thinks fit, hear any party either personally or by an advocate.

SECTION 445 - HIGH COURT'S ORDER TO BE CERTIFIED TO LOWER COURT
Core Content:
When a case is revised under this Chapter by the High Court or a Sessions Judge, it or he shall certify its decision or order to the Court by which the finding, sentence or order revised was recorded or passed, and the Court to which the decision or order is so certified shall make such orders as are conformable to the decision so certified, and if necessary, the record shall be amended accordingly.

SECTION 446 - POWER OF SUPREME COURT TO TRANSFER CASES AND APPEALS
Core Content:
Whenever it is made to appear to the Supreme Court that an order under this section is expedient for the ends of justice, it may direct that any particular case or appeal be transferred from one High Court to another High Court or from a Criminal Court subordinate to one High Court to another Criminal Court of equal or superior jurisdiction subordinate to another High Court. The Supreme Court may act only on the application of the Attorney-General of India or of a party interested, supported by affidavit or affirmation (except when applicant is Attorney-General or Advocate-General). If application is dismissed and was frivolous or vexatious, the Supreme Court may order the applicant to pay compensation to any person who opposed the application.

Procedure:

Supreme Court may transfer cases/appeals between High Courts or between Criminal Courts under different High Courts

Ground: expedient for ends of justice

Application only by Attorney-General of India or party interested

Application by motion, supported by affidavit (unless applicant is Attorney-General or Advocate-General)

If dismissed and frivolous/vexatious, Supreme Court may order compensation to opposing party

SECTION 447 - POWER OF HIGH COURT TO TRANSFER CASES AND APPEALS
Core Content:
Whenever it is made to appear to the High Court that a fair and impartial inquiry or trial cannot be had in any Criminal Court subordinate thereto, or that some question of law of unusual difficulty is likely to arise, or that an order under this section is required by any provision of this Sanhita or will tend to the general convenience of the parties or witnesses or is expedient for the ends of justice, it may order that any offence be inquired into or tried by any Court not qualified under sections 197 to 205 but otherwise competent, or that any particular case or appeal be transferred from one Criminal Court to another Criminal Court of equal or superior jurisdiction, or that any particular case be committed for trial to a Court of Session, or that any particular case or appeal be transferred to and tried before itself.

Procedure:

High Court may transfer cases on grounds of:

(a) Fair and impartial inquiry/trial cannot be had

(b) Question of law of unusual difficulty likely to arise

(c) Required by any provision of BNSS

(d) General convenience of parties or witnesses

(e) Expedient for ends of justice

High Court may act on report of lower Court, application of party interested, or own initiative

No application for transfer within same sessions division unless made to Sessions Judge and rejected

Application by motion, supported by affidavit (unless applicant is Advocate-General)

Accused applying may be directed to execute bond for compensation

Accused shall give notice to Public Prosecutor with copy of grounds; at least 24 hours between notice and hearing

High Court may stay proceedings pending disposal of application

If application dismissed and frivolous/vexatious, High Court may order compensation

When High Court transfers case to itself for trial, it shall observe same procedure as lower Court would have observed

Key Time Limit: 24 hours between notice and hearing

SECTION 448 - POWER OF SESSIONS JUDGE TO TRANSFER CASES AND APPEALS
Core Content:
Whenever it is made to appear to a Sessions Judge that an order under this sub-section is expedient for the ends of justice, he may order that any particular case be transferred from one Criminal Court to another Criminal Court in his sessions division. The Sessions Judge may act on the report of the lower Court, application of a party interested, or his own initiative. The provisions of sections 447(3),(4),(5),(6),(7) and (9) apply, except that the sum for compensation shall not exceed ten thousand rupees.

Key Limit: Compensation not exceeding ₹10,000

SECTION 449 - WITHDRAWAL OF CASES AND APPEALS BY SESSIONS JUDGES
Core Content:
A Sessions Judge may withdraw any case or appeal from, or recall any case or appeal which he has made over to a Chief Judicial Magistrate subordinate to him. At any time before trial or hearing has commenced before the Additional Sessions Judge, a Sessions Judge may recall any case or appeal which he has made over to any Additional Sessions Judge. Where a Sessions Judge withdraws or recalls a case or appeal, he may either try the case in his own Court or hear the appeal himself, or make it over to another Court for trial or hearing.

SECTION 450 - WITHDRAWAL OF CASES BY JUDICIAL MAGISTRATES
Core Content:
Any Chief Judicial Magistrate may withdraw any case from, or recall any case which he has made over to, any Magistrate subordinate to him, and may inquire into or try such case himself, or refer it for inquiry or trial to any other such Magistrate competent to inquire into or try the same. Any Judicial Magistrate may recall any case made over by him under section 212(2) to any other Magistrate and may inquire into or try such cases himself.

SECTION 451 - MAKING OVER OR WITHDRAWAL OF CASES BY EXECUTIVE MAGISTRATES
Core Content:
Any District Magistrate or Sub-divisional Magistrate may make over, for disposal, any proceeding which has been started before him, to any Magistrate subordinate to him; and may withdraw any case from, or recall any case which he has made over to, any Magistrate subordinate to him, and dispose of such proceeding himself or refer it for disposal to any other Magistrate.

SECTION 452 - REASONS TO BE RECORDED
Core Content:
A Sessions Judge or Magistrate making an order under section 448, 449, 450 or 451 shall record his reasons for making it.

BNSS CHAPTER XXXIV: EXECUTION, SUSPENSION, REMISSION AND COMMUTATION OF SENTENCES (Sections 453-477)
SECTION 453 - EXECUTION OF ORDER PASSED UNDER SECTION 409
Core Content:
When in a case submitted to the High Court for the confirmation of a sentence of death, the Court of Session receives the order of confirmation or other order of the High Court thereon, it shall cause such order to be carried into effect by issuing a warrant or taking such other steps as may be necessary.

SECTION 454 - EXECUTION OF SENTENCE OF DEATH PASSED BY HIGH COURT
Core Content:
When a sentence of death is passed by the High Court in appeal or in revision, the Court of Session shall, on receiving the order of the High Court, cause the sentence to be carried into effect by issuing a warrant.

SECTION 455 - POSTPONEMENT OF EXECUTION OF SENTENCE OF DEATH IN CASE OF APPEAL TO SUPREME COURT
Core Content:
Where a person is sentenced to death by the High Court and an appeal lies to the Supreme Court under Article 134(1)(a) or (b), the High Court shall order execution to be postponed until the period for appeal has expired, or if appeal preferred, until disposed of. Where sentence of death is passed or confirmed and the person applies for a certificate under Article 132 or Article 134(1)(c), the High Court shall postpone execution until such application is disposed of, or if certificate granted, until period for appeal to Supreme Court has expired. Where the High Court is satisfied that the person intends to present a petition to the Supreme Court for special leave under Article 136, it shall postpone execution for such period as it considers sufficient to enable him to present such petition.

SECTION 456 - COMMUTATION OF SENTENCE OF DEATH ON PREGNANT WOMAN
Core Content:
If a woman sentenced to death is found to be pregnant, the High Court shall commute the sentence to imprisonment for life.

SECTION 457 - POWER TO APPOINT PLACE OF IMPRISONMENT
Core Content:
Except when otherwise provided, the State Government may direct in what place any person liable to be imprisoned or committed to custody shall be confined. If any person liable to be imprisoned is in confinement in a civil jail, the Court or Magistrate may direct that the person be removed to a criminal jail. When removed to criminal jail, he shall on release be sent back to civil jail, unless three years have elapsed (in which case deemed released from civil jail) or the Court certifies he is entitled to be released from civil jail.

SECTION 458 - EXECUTION OF SENTENCE OF IMPRISONMENT
Core Content:
Where the accused is sentenced to imprisonment for life or for a term, the Court shall forthwith forward a warrant to the jail or other place where he is to be confined, and unless already confined there, forward him with the warrant. Where sentenced to imprisonment till the rising of the Court, no warrant to jail is necessary, and accused may be confined in such place as the Court may direct. Where accused not present when sentenced, Court shall issue warrant for his arrest for forwarding to jail; sentence commences on date of arrest.

SECTION 459 - DIRECTION OF WARRANT FOR EXECUTION
Core Content:
Every warrant for the execution of a sentence of imprisonment shall be directed to the officer in charge of the jail or other place in which the prisoner is, or is to be, confined.

SECTION 460 - WARRANT WITH WHOM TO BE LODGED
Core Content:
When the prisoner is to be confined in a jail, the warrant shall be lodged with the jailer.

SECTION 461 - WARRANT FOR LEVY OF FINE
Core Content:
When an offender has been sentenced to pay a fine but no such payment has been made, the Court may issue a warrant for the levy of the amount by attachment and sale of any movable property belonging to the offender, or issue a warrant to the Collector to realise the amount as arrears of land revenue from movable or immovable property of the defaulter. If the sentence directs imprisonment in default and the offender has undergone such imprisonment, no Court shall issue such warrant unless for special reasons recorded, or unless it has made an order for payment of expenses or compensation out of the fine.

SECTION 462 - EFFECT OF SUCH WARRANT
Core Content:
A warrant issued under section 461(a) may be executed within the local jurisdiction of such Court, and shall authorise attachment and sale of any such property outside such jurisdiction when endorsed by the District Magistrate within whose jurisdiction such property is found.

SECTION 463 - WARRANT FOR LEVY OF FINE ISSUED BY A COURT IN ANY TERRITORY TO WHICH THIS SANHITA DOES NOT EXTEND
Core Content:
When an offender has been sentenced to pay a fine by a Criminal Court in any territory to which BNSS does not extend and the Court issues a warrant to the Collector of a district in BNSS territories authorising him to realise the amount as arrears of land revenue, such warrant shall be deemed to be a warrant issued under section 461(b) by a Court in BNSS territories.

SECTION 464 - SUSPENSION OF EXECUTION OF SENTENCE OF IMPRISONMENT
Core Content:
When an offender has been sentenced to fine only and to imprisonment in default, and the fine is not paid forthwith, the Court may order that the fine be payable in full within 30 days or in installments, suspend execution of sentence of imprisonment, and release the offender on bond conditioned for appearance. If the fine or installment is not paid on or before the due date, the Court may direct sentence of imprisonment to be carried into execution at once.

Key Time Limit: 30 days for payment or between installments

SECTION 465 - WHO MAY ISSUE WARRANT
Core Content:
Every warrant for the execution of a sentence may be issued either by the Judge or Magistrate who passed the sentence, or by his successor-in-office.

SECTION 466 - SENTENCE ON ESCAPED CONVICT WHEN TO TAKE EFFECT
Core Content:
When a sentence of death, imprisonment for life or fine is passed on an escaped convict, such sentence shall take effect immediately. When a sentence of imprisonment for a term is passed on an escaped convict: (a) if the new sentence is severer in kind than the sentence he was undergoing when he escaped, it takes effect immediately; (b) if not severer, it takes effect after he has suffered a further period equal to that which remained unexpired of his former sentence. A sentence of rigorous imprisonment is severer than simple imprisonment.

SECTION 467 - SENTENCE ON OFFENDER ALREADY SENTENCED FOR ANOTHER OFFENCE
Core Content:
When a person already undergoing a sentence of imprisonment is sentenced on a subsequent conviction to imprisonment or imprisonment for life, such imprisonment shall commence at the expiration of the previous sentence, unless the Court directs that the subsequent sentence shall run concurrently. Where a person sentenced to imprisonment for default of furnishing security is, whilst undergoing such sentence, sentenced to imprisonment for an offence committed prior to such order, the latter sentence shall commence immediately. When a person already undergoing imprisonment for life is sentenced on a subsequent conviction to imprisonment for a term or imprisonment for life, the subsequent sentence shall run concurrently.

SECTION 468 - PERIOD OF DETENTION UNDERGONE BY ACCUSED TO BE SET OFF AGAINST SENTENCE OF IMPRISONMENT
Core Content:
Where an accused person has, on conviction, been sentenced to imprisonment for a term (not being imprisonment in default of payment of fine), the period of detention undergone by him during investigation, inquiry or trial of the same case and before the date of such conviction shall be set off against the term of imprisonment imposed, and his liability shall be restricted to the remainder, if any. In cases referred to in section 475 (life imprisonment for offences where death is also a punishment), such period of detention shall be set off against the period of fourteen years referred to in that section.

Illustration:
X is arrested on Jan 1, remains in jail during trial, and is convicted and sentenced to 5 years imprisonment on Dec 31. The 365 days of pre-conviction detention are set off against the 5-year sentence. X only needs to serve 4 years (minus any other set-offs).

SECTION 469 - SAVING
Core Content:
Nothing in section 466 or 467 shall excuse any person from any part of the punishment to which he is liable upon his former or subsequent conviction. When an award of imprisonment in default of payment of fine is annexed to a substantive sentence and the person is after its execution to undergo further substantive sentence or sentences, effect shall not be given to the award of imprisonment in default until the person has undergone the further sentence or sentences.

SECTION 470 - RETURN OF WARRANT ON EXECUTION OF SENTENCE
Core Content:
When a sentence has been fully executed, the officer executing it shall return the warrant to the Court from which it is issued, with an endorsement under his hand certifying the manner in which the sentence has been executed.

SECTION 471 - MONEY ORDERED TO BE PAID RECOVERABLE AS A FINE
Core Content:
Any money (other than a fine) payable by virtue of any order made under this Sanhita, and the method of recovery of which is not otherwise expressly provided for, shall be recoverable as if it were a fine.

SECTION 472 - MERCY PETITION IN DEATH SENTENCE CASES
Core Content:
A convict under sentence of death or his legal heir or any other relative may file a mercy petition before the President under Article 72 or the Governor under Article 161 within thirty days from the date on which the Superintendent of the jail informs him about dismissal of appeal, review or SLP by Supreme Court, or about confirmation of death sentence and expiry of time to file appeal. Petition may initially be made to Governor and on its rejection, to President within sixty days from rejection. The Superintendent shall ensure every convict files mercy petition within sixty days; if not received from other convicts, he shall send their details to Central/State Government. Central Government shall seek comments of State Government and consider petition and make recommendations to President within sixty days from receipt of comments. President may consider and decide; if more than one convict, petitions shall be decided together. Upon receipt of President's order, Central Government shall within forty-eight hours communicate to State Home Department and Superintendent of jail. No appeal lies against order of President or Governor, and any question as to arriving of decision shall not be inquired into in any Court.

Key Time Limits:

30 days from jail Superintendent's information to file mercy petition

60 days from Governor's rejection to file with President

60 days for Central Government to make recommendations

SECTION 473 - POWER TO SUSPEND OR REMIT SENTENCES
Core Content:
When any person has been sentenced to punishment for an offence, the appropriate Government may, at any time, without conditions or upon any conditions which the person sentenced accepts, suspend the execution of his sentence or remit the whole or any part of the punishment. The appropriate Government may require the presiding Judge to state his opinion on whether the application should be granted. If any condition is not fulfilled, the appropriate Government may cancel the suspension or remission, and the person may be arrested without warrant and remanded to undergo the unexpired portion. The appropriate Government may make rules. "Appropriate Government" means: (a) Central Government for offences against Union executive power; (b) State Government for other cases.

SECTION 474 - POWER TO COMMUTE SENTENCE
Core Content:
The appropriate Government may, without the consent of the person sentenced, commute: (a) death sentence to imprisonment for life; (b) imprisonment for life to imprisonment for a term not less than seven years; (c) imprisonment for seven years or more to imprisonment for a term not less than three years; (d) imprisonment for less than seven years to fine; (e) rigorous imprisonment to simple imprisonment for any term to which that person might have been sentenced.

SECTION 475 - RESTRICTION ON POWERS OF REMISSION OR COMMUTATION IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
Notwithstanding anything in section 473, where a sentence of imprisonment for life is imposed on conviction of a person for an offence for which death is one of the punishments provided by law, or where a sentence of death imposed on a person has been commuted under section 474 into imprisonment for life, such person shall not be released from prison unless he had served at least fourteen years of imprisonment.

Key Time Limit: Minimum 14 years for life imprisonment in death-eligible offences

SECTION 476 - CONCURRENT POWER OF CENTRAL GOVERNMENT IN CASE OF DEATH SENTENCES
Core Content:
The powers conferred by sections 473 and 474 upon the State Government may, in the case of sentences of death, also be exercised by the Central Government.

SECTION 477 - STATE GOVERNMENT TO ACT AFTER CONCURRENCE WITH CENTRAL GOVERNMENT IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
The powers of State Government to remit or commute a sentence for an offence which was investigated by any Central agency, or involved Central Government property, or was committed by a Central Government servant, shall not be exercised except after concurrence with the Central Government. No order of suspension, remission or commutation passed by State Government in relation to a person convicted of offences, some of which relate to Union executive power, shall have effect unless an order has also been made by Central Government in relation to those offences.

BNSS CHAPTER XXXV: PROVISIONS AS TO BAIL AND BONDS (Sections 478-496)
SECTION 478 - IN WHAT CASES BAIL TO BE TAKEN
Core Content:
When any person other than a person accused of a non-bailable offence is arrested or detained without warrant, or appears or is brought before a Court, and is prepared at any time to give bail, such person shall be released on bail. If such person is indigent and unable to furnish surety, the officer or Court may discharge him on his executing a bond. If a person is unable to give bail bond within a week of arrest, it shall be sufficient ground to presume he is indigent. Where a person has failed to comply with conditions of bond regarding time and place of attendance, the Court may refuse to release him on bail on a subsequent occasion.

Key Time Limit: 1 week to presume indigence

SECTION 479 - MAXIMUM PERIOD FOR WHICH UNDER-TRIAL PRISONER CAN BE DETAINED
Core Content:
Where a person has, during investigation, inquiry or trial for an offence (not being an offence for which death or life imprisonment is specified), undergone detention for a period extending up to one-half of the maximum period of imprisonment specified for that offence, he shall be released on bail by the Court. If such person is a first-time offender (never convicted of any offence in the past), he shall be released on bond if he has undergone detention for one-third of the maximum period. The Court may, after hearing Public Prosecutor and for reasons recorded, order continued detention for longer than one-half, or release on bail bond instead of his bond. No such person shall be detained during investigation, inquiry or trial for more than the maximum period of imprisonment provided for the offence. The period of detention caused by delay caused by the accused shall be excluded. Where investigation, inquiry or trial in more than one offence or in multiple cases are pending against a person, he shall not be released on bail. The Superintendent of jail shall, on completion of one-half or one-third of the period, make an application in writing to the Court for release of such person on bail.

Key Time Limits:

Release at 1/2 of maximum sentence (1/3 for first-time offenders)

Cannot exceed maximum sentence

SECTION 480 - WHEN BAIL MAY BE TAKEN IN CASE OF NON-BAILABLE OFFENCE
Core Content:
When any person accused of a non-bailable offence is arrested or appears before a Court other than High Court or Court of Session, he may be released on bail, but: (i) shall not be released if reasonable grounds believe he has been guilty of an offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life; (ii) shall not be released if offence is cognizable and he had been previously convicted of an offence punishable with death, life, or 7+ years, or had been previously convicted on two or more occasions of a cognizable offence punishable with 3+ years but less than 7 years. Exception: Court may release a child, woman, or sick/infirm person, or for any other special reason. If the offence is punishable with death, life, or 7+ years, the Court shall not release on bail without giving opportunity of hearing to Public Prosecutor. If it appears there are not reasonable grounds but sufficient grounds for further inquiry, accused shall be released on bail. For offences punishable with 7+ years or under BNS Chapters VI, VII, XVII, or abetment/conspiracy/attempt thereof, the Court shall impose conditions: (a) attend in accordance with bond; (b) not commit similar offence; (c) not induce/threaten/promise witnesses or tamper with evidence. The Court shall record reasons. If trial of non-bailable offence is not concluded within 60 days from first date of taking evidence, and accused is in custody during whole period, he shall be released on bail unless Magistrate otherwise directs for reasons recorded. If after conclusion of trial and before judgment, Court is of opinion there are reasonable grounds to believe accused not guilty, it shall release him on bond.

Key Time Limits: 60 days from first date of taking evidence

SECTION 481 - BAIL TO REQUIRE ACCUSED TO APPEAR BEFORE NEXT APPELLATE COURT
Core Content:
Before conclusion of trial and before disposal of appeal, the Court trying the offence or the Appellate Court shall require the accused to execute a bond or bail bond to appear before the higher Court as and when such Court issues notice in respect of any appeal or petition filed against the judgment. Such bond shall be in force for six months. If the accused fails to appear, the bond stands forfeited and procedure under section 491 shall apply.

Key Time Limit: Bond valid for 6 months

SECTION 482 - DIRECTION FOR GRANT OF BAIL TO PERSON APPREHENDING ARREST (Anticipatory Bail)
Core Content:
When any person has reason to believe that he may be arrested on an accusation of having committed a non-bailable offence, he may apply to the High Court or Court of Session for a direction under this section. The Court may direct that in the event of such arrest, he shall be released on bail. The Court may include conditions such as making himself available for interrogation, not making inducement/threat/promise to witnesses, not leaving India without permission, and other conditions under section 480(3). If such person is thereafter arrested without warrant on such accusation, and is prepared to give bail, he shall be released on bail. If a Magistrate taking cognizance of such offence decides that a warrant should be issued, he shall issue a bailable warrant in conformity with the direction. This section does not apply to arrest for offences under BNS section 65 (rape on woman under 16) and section 70(2) (gang rape on woman under 18).

Procedure:

Person apprehending arrest for non-bailable offence applies to High Court or Court of Session

Court may direct release on bail in event of arrest

Conditions may be imposed

If arrested, shall be released on bail

Magistrate shall issue bailable warrant in conformity with direction

Does not apply to BNS 65 or 70(2)

SECTION 483 - SPECIAL POWERS OF HIGH COURT OR COURT OF SESSION REGARDING BAIL
Core Content:
A High Court or Court of Session may direct that any person accused of an offence and in custody be released on bail, and if the offence is of the nature specified in section 480(3), may impose any condition. It may also set aside or modify any condition imposed by a Magistrate. Before granting bail to a person accused of an offence exclusively triable by Court of Session or punishable with imprisonment for life, notice shall be given to Public Prosecutor unless not practicable for reasons recorded. Before granting bail for offence under BNS 65 or 70(2), notice to Public Prosecutor within fifteen days from receipt of notice of application. The presence of the informant or any person authorised by him shall be obligatory at the hearing of bail application for BNS 65 or 70(2). A High Court or Court of Session may direct that any person released on bail be arrested and committed to custody.

Key Time Limit: 15 days notice for BNS 65/70(2)

SECTION 484 - AMOUNT OF BOND AND REDUCTION THEREOF
Core Content:
The amount of every bond executed under this Chapter shall be fixed with due regard to the circumstances of the case and shall not be excessive. The High Court or the Court of Session may direct that the bail required by a police officer or Magistrate be reduced.

SECTION 485 - BOND OF ACCUSED AND SURETIES
Core Content:
Before any person is released on bond or bail bond, a bond for such sum of money as the police officer or Court thinks sufficient shall be executed by such person, and by one or more sufficient sureties conditioned that such person shall attend at the time and place mentioned and continue so to attend until otherwise directed. Any condition imposed for release shall also be contained in the bond. If the case so requires, the bond shall also bind the person to appear when called upon at the High Court, Court of Session or other Court. The Court may accept affidavits in proof of sufficiency or fitness of sureties, or may hold inquiry or cause inquiry to be made.

SECTION 486 - DECLARATION BY SURETIES
Core Content:
Every person standing surety to an accused person for his release on bail, shall make a declaration before the Court as to the number of persons to whom he has stood surety including the accused, giving therein all the relevant particulars.

SECTION 487 - DISCHARGE FROM CUSTODY
Core Content:
As soon as the bond or bail bond has been executed, the person for whose appearance it has been executed shall be released. When he is in jail, the Court admitting him to bail shall issue an order of release to the officer in charge of the jail, who shall release him. This section does not require release of any person liable to be detained for some other matter.

SECTION 488 - POWER TO ORDER SUFFICIENT BAIL WHEN THAT FIRST TAKEN IS INSUFFICIENT
Core Content:
If, through mistake, fraud or otherwise, insufficient sureties have been accepted, or if they afterwards become insufficient, the Court may issue a warrant of arrest directing that the person released on bail be brought before it and may order him to find sufficient sureties, and on his failing so to do, may commit him to jail.

SECTION 489 - DISCHARGE OF SURETIES
Core Content:
All or any sureties for the attendance and appearance of a person released on bail may at any time apply to a Magistrate to discharge the bond. On such application, the Magistrate shall issue a warrant of arrest directing that the person so released be brought before him. On his appearance or voluntary surrender, the Magistrate shall direct the bond to be discharged, and shall call upon such person to find other sufficient sureties, and if he fails to do so, may commit him to jail.

SECTION 490 - DEPOSIT INSTEAD OF RECOGNIZANCE
Core Content:
When any person is required by any Court or officer to execute a bond or bail bond, such Court or officer may, except in the case of a bond for good behaviour, permit him to deposit a sum of money or Government promissory notes to such amount as the Court or officer may fix in lieu of executing such bond.

SECTION 491 - PROCEDURE WHEN BOND HAS BEEN FORFEITED
Core Content:
Where a bond under this Sanhita is for appearance or production of property before a Court and it is proved to the satisfaction of that Court that the bond has been forfeited, the Court shall record the grounds of such proof, and may call upon any person bound by such bond to pay the penalty thereof or to show cause why it should not be paid. If sufficient cause is not shown and the penalty is not paid, the Court may proceed to recover the same as if such penalty were a fine. Where such penalty cannot be recovered, the surety shall be liable to imprisonment in civil jail for a term which may extend to six months. The Court may remit any portion of the penalty. Where a surety dies before the bond is forfeited, his estate shall be discharged. Where a person who furnished security under section 125, 136 or 401 is convicted of an offence constituting breach of the bond, a certified copy of the judgment may be used as evidence against his surety, and the Court shall presume the offence was committed by him unless contrary proved.

Key Time Limit: Imprisonment up to 6 months for surety

SECTION 492 - CANCELLATION OF BOND AND BAIL BOND
Core Content:
Without prejudice to section 491, where a bond or bail bond is for appearance and is forfeited for breach of a condition, (a) the bond executed by such person as well as the bond executed by his sureties shall stand cancelled; and (b) thereafter no such person shall be released only on his own bond in that case, if the police officer or Court is satisfied there was no sufficient cause for the failure. He may be released upon execution of a fresh personal bond and bond by one or more sureties.

SECTION 493 - PROCEDURE IN CASE OF INSOLVENCY OR DEATH OF SURETY OR WHEN A BOND IS FORFEITED
Core Content:
When any surety to a bail bond becomes insolvent or dies, or when any bond is forfeited under section 491, the Court by whose order such bond was taken, or a Magistrate of the first class may order the person from whom such security was demanded to furnish fresh security, and if such security is not furnished, such Court or Magistrate may proceed as if there had been a default in complying with such original order.

SECTION 494 - BOND REQUIRED FROM CHILD
Core Content:
When the person required by any Court or officer to execute a bond is a child, such Court or officer may accept, in lieu thereof, a bond executed by a surety or sureties only.

SECTION 495 - APPEAL FROM ORDERS UNDER SECTION 491
Core Content:
All orders passed under section 491 shall be appealable: (i) in the case of an order made by a Magistrate, to the Sessions Judge; (ii) in the case of an order made by a Court of Session, to the Court to which an appeal lies from an order made by such Court.

SECTION 496 - POWER TO DIRECT LEVY OF AMOUNT DUE ON CERTAIN RECOGNIZANCES
Core Content:
The High Court or Court of Session may direct any Magistrate to levy the amount due on a bond for appearance or attendance at such High Court or Court of Session.

BNSS CHAPTER XXXVI: DISPOSAL OF PROPERTY (Sections 497-505)
SECTION 497 - ORDER FOR CUSTODY AND DISPOSAL OF PROPERTY PENDING TRIAL IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
When any property is produced before any Criminal Court or Magistrate during any investigation, inquiry or trial, the Court or Magistrate may make such order as it thinks fit for the proper custody of such property pending conclusion of the investigation, inquiry or trial. If the property is subject to speedy and natural decay, or if the Court thinks it expedient, it may order it to be sold or otherwise disposed of.

SECTION 498 - ORDER FOR DISPOSAL OF PROPERTY AT CONCLUSION OF TRIAL
Core Content:
When an inquiry or trial in any Criminal Court is concluded, the Court may make such order as it thinks fit for the disposal of any property or document produced before it or in its custody, or regarding the delivery of such property to the person entitled to possession. If the person entitled is known, the Court may order the property to be delivered to him. If the person entitled is unknown, the Court may detain it and issue a proclamation requiring any person who may have a claim to appear and establish his claim within six months. When any property is sold before conclusion of trial, the Court may order the net proceeds to be paid to the person entitled.

Key Time Limit: 6 months for claim

SECTION 499 - PAYMENT TO INNOCENT PURCHASER OF MONEY FOUND ON ACCUSED
Core Content:
When any person is convicted of any offence which includes, or amounts to, theft or receiving stolen property, and the Court is satisfied that any money found on the accused person was taken from the person from whom the property was stolen, and that such person is the bona fide purchaser of such money from the accused, the Court may order the money to be returned to such bona fide purchaser.

SECTION 500 - APPEAL AGAINST ORDERS UNDER SECTION 498 OR SECTION 499
Core Content:
Any person aggrieved by an order made under section 498 or 499 may appeal against it to the Court to which appeals ordinarily lie from convictions by the former Court. The Appellate Court may stay the order pending disposal of appeal, or may modify, alter or annul the order and make any further orders that may be just. These powers may also be exercised by a Court of appeal, confirmation or revision while dealing with the case.

SECTION 501 - DESTRUCTION OF LIBELLOUS AND OTHER MATTER
Core Content:
On a conviction under BNS sections 294, 295, or 356(3)(4), the Court may order the destruction of all copies of the thing in respect of which the conviction was had. On a conviction under BNS sections 274, 275, 276 or 277 (adulteration of food/drugs), the Court may order the food, drink, drug or medical preparation to be destroyed.

SECTION 502 - POWER TO RESTORE POSSESSION OF IMMOVABLE PROPERTY
Core Content:
When a person is convicted of an offence by use of criminal force or show of force or by criminal intimidation, and it appears to the Court that by such use of force or intimidation any person has been dispossessed of any immovable property, the Court may order that possession of the same be restored to that person after evicting by force, if necessary, any other person who may be in possession. No such order shall be made more than one month after the date of conviction. Where the trial Court has not made such an order, the Court of appeal, confirmation or revision may make such order. No order made under this section shall prejudice any right or interest which any person may be able to establish in a civil suit.

Key Time Limit: 1 month from conviction

SECTION 503 - PROCEDURE BY POLICE UPON SEIZURE OF PROPERTY
Core Content:
Whenever the seizure of property by any police officer is reported to a Magistrate, and such property is not produced before a Criminal Court during inquiry or trial, the Magistrate may make such order as he thinks fit respecting the disposal of such property or the delivery of such property to the person entitled to possession. If the person entitled is known, the Magistrate may order the property to be delivered to him on such conditions as he thinks fit. If such person is unknown, the Magistrate may detain it and issue a proclamation specifying the articles and requiring any person who may have a claim to appear and establish his claim within six months from the date of such proclamation.

SECTION 504 - PROCEDURE WHERE NO CLAIMANT APPEARS WITHIN SIX MONTHS
Core Content:
If no person within such period establishes his claim to such property, and if the person in whose possession such property was found is unable to show that it was legally acquired by him, the Magistrate may by order direct that such property shall be at the disposal of the State Government and may be sold by that Government. An appeal shall lie against any such order to the Court to which appeals ordinarily lie from convictions by the Magistrate.

SECTION 505 - POWER TO SELL PERISHABLE PROPERTY
Core Content:
If the person entitled to possession of such property is unknown or absent and the property is subject to speedy and natural decay, or if the Magistrate is of opinion that its sale would be for the benefit of the owner, or that the value of such property is less than ten thousand rupees, the Magistrate may at any time direct it to be sold. The provisions of sections 503 and 504 shall apply to the net proceeds of such sale.

Key Limit: Value less than ₹10,000

BNSS CHAPTER XXXVII: IRREGULAR PROCEEDINGS (Sections 506-512)
SECTION 506 - IRREGULARITIES WHICH DO NOT VITIATE PROCEEDINGS
Core Content:
If any Magistrate not empowered by law to do any of the following things erroneously in good faith does that thing, his proceedings shall not be set aside merely on the ground of his not being so empowered: (a) issue search-warrant under section 97; (b) order police to investigate an offence under section 174; (c) hold an inquest under section 196; (d) issue process under section 207 for apprehension of a person within his local jurisdiction who has committed an offence outside such jurisdiction; (e) take cognizance of an offence under section 210(1)(a) or (b); (f) make over a case under section 212(2); (g) tender a pardon under section 343; (h) recall a case and try it himself under section 450; (i) sell property under section 504 or 505.

SECTION 507 - IRREGULARITIES WHICH VITIATE PROCEEDINGS
Core Content:
