If any Magistrate, not being empowered by law in this behalf, does any of the following things, his proceedings shall be void: (a) attaches and sells property under section 85; (b) issues a search-warrant for a document, parcel or other thing in custody of a postal authority; (c) demands security to keep the peace; (d) demands security for good behaviour; (e) discharges a person lawfully bound to be of good behaviour; (f) cancels a bond to keep the peace; (g) makes an order for maintenance; (h) makes an order under section 152 as to a local nuisance; (i) prohibits repetition or continuance of a public nuisance under section 162; (j) makes an order under Part C or Part D of Chapter XI; (k) takes cognizance of an offence under section 210(1)(c); (l) tries an offender; (m) tries an offender summarily; (n) passes a sentence under section 364 on proceedings recorded by another Magistrate; (o) decides an appeal; (p) calls for proceedings under section 438; (q) revises an order passed under section 491.

SECTION 508 - PROCEEDINGS IN WRONG PLACE
Core Content:
No finding, sentence or order of any Criminal Court shall be set aside merely on the ground that the inquiry, trial or other proceedings took place in a wrong sessions division, district, sub-division or other local area, unless it appears that such error has in fact occasioned a failure of justice.

SECTION 509 - NON-COMPLIANCE WITH PROVISIONS OF SECTION 183 OR SECTION 316
Core Content:
If any Court before which a confession or other statement of an accused person recorded under section 183 or 316 is tendered in evidence finds that any of the provisions of either of such sections have not been complied with, it may, notwithstanding anything in section 94 of Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, take evidence in regard to such non-compliance, and may, if satisfied that such non-compliance has not injured the accused in his defence on the merits and that he duly made the statement recorded, admit such statement. This section applies to Courts of appeal, reference and revision.

SECTION 510 - EFFECT OF OMISSION TO FRAME, OR ABSENCE OF, OR ERROR IN, CHARGE
Core Content:
No finding, sentence or order by a Court of competent jurisdiction shall be deemed invalid merely on the ground that no charge was framed or on the ground of any error, omission or irregularity in the charge including any misjoinder of charges, unless, in the opinion of the Court of appeal, confirmation or revision, a failure of justice has in fact been occasioned thereby. If failure of justice has been occasioned, the Court may order that a charge be framed and trial recommenced from after framing of charge, or direct a new trial upon a charge framed in whatever manner it thinks fit. If the Court is of opinion that no valid charge could be preferred, it shall quash the conviction.

SECTION 511 - FINDING OR SENTENCE WHEN REVERSIBLE BY REASON OF ERROR, OMISSION OR IRREGULARITY
Core Content:
No finding, sentence or order passed by a Court of competent jurisdiction shall be reversed or altered by a Court of appeal, confirmation or revision on account of any error, omission or irregularity in the complaint, summons, warrant, proclamation, order, judgment or other proceedings before or during trial or in any inquiry or other proceedings, or any error or irregularity in any sanction for the prosecution, unless in the opinion of that Court, a failure of justice has in fact been occasioned thereby. In determining whether a failure of justice has been occasioned, the Court shall have regard to the fact whether the objection could and should have been raised at an earlier stage in the proceedings.

SECTION 512 - DEFECT OR ERROR NOT TO MAKE ATTACHMENT UNLAWFUL
Core Content:
No attachment made under this Sanhita shall be deemed unlawful, nor shall any person making the same be deemed a trespasser, on account of any defect or want of form in the summons, conviction, writ of attachment or other proceedings relating thereto.

BNSS CHAPTER XXXVIII: LIMITATION FOR TAKING COGNIZANCE OF CERTAIN OFFENCES (Sections 513-519)
SECTION 513 - DEFINITIONS
Core Content:
For the purposes of this Chapter, "period of limitation" means the period specified in section 514 for taking cognizance of an offence.

SECTION 514 - BAR TO TAKING COGNIZANCE AFTER LAPSE OF PERIOD OF LIMITATION
Core Content:
Except as otherwise provided, no Court shall take cognizance of an offence after the expiry of the period of limitation. The period of limitation shall be: (a) six months, if the offence is punishable with fine only; (b) one year, if the offence is punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding one year; (c) three years, if the offence is punishable with imprisonment for a term exceeding one year but not exceeding three years. For offences which may be tried together, limitation determined with reference to the offence which is punishable with the more severe punishment. For computing the period, the relevant date shall be the date of filing complaint under section 223 or the date of recording of information under section 173.

Key Time Limits:

6 months for fine-only offences

1 year for imprisonment up to 1 year

3 years for imprisonment 1-3 years

SECTION 515 - COMMENCEMENT OF PERIOD OF LIMITATION
Core Content:
The period of limitation shall commence: (a) on the date of the offence; or (b) where commission was not known to the person aggrieved or any police officer, the first day on which such offence comes to the knowledge of such person or any police officer, whichever is earlier; or (c) where it is not known by whom the offence was committed, the first day on which the identity of the offender is known to the person aggrieved or the police officer making investigation, whichever is earlier. In computing the said period, the day from which such period is to be computed shall be excluded.

SECTION 516 - EXCLUSION OF TIME IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
In computing the period of limitation, the time during which any person has been prosecuting with due diligence another prosecution against the offender shall be excluded, provided the prosecution relates to the same facts and is prosecuted in good faith in a Court which from defect of jurisdiction or other cause of a like nature is unable to entertain it. Where institution of prosecution has been stayed by an injunction or order, the period of continuance of the injunction or order shall be excluded. Where notice of prosecution has been given, or where previous consent or sanction of Government is required, the period of such notice or time required for obtaining such consent or sanction shall be excluded. Where the offender has been absent from India or has avoided arrest by absconding or concealing himself, such time shall be excluded.

SECTION 517 - EXCLUSION OF DATE ON WHICH COURT IS CLOSED
Core Content:
Where the period of limitation expires on a day when the Court is closed, the Court may take cognizance on the day on which the Court reopens. A Court shall be deemed to be closed on any day if, during its normal working hours, it remains closed on that day.

SECTION 518 - CONTINUING OFFENCE
Core Content:
In the case of a continuing offence, a fresh period of limitation shall begin to run at every moment of the time during which the offence continues.

SECTION 519 - EXTENSION OF PERIOD OF LIMITATION IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
Notwithstanding anything contained in the foregoing provisions, any Court may take cognizance of an offence after the expiry of the period of limitation, if it is satisfied on the facts and in the circumstances of the case that the delay has been properly explained or that it is necessary so to do in the interests of justice.

BNSS CHAPTER XXXIX: MISCELLANEOUS (Sections 520-531)
SECTION 520 - TRIALS BEFORE HIGH COURTS
Core Content:
When an offence is tried by the High Court otherwise than under section 447 (transfer to itself), it shall, in the trial of the offence, observe the same procedure as a Court of Sessions would observe if it were trying the case.

SECTION 521 - DELIVERY TO COMMANDING OFFICERS OF PERSONS LIABLE TO BE TRIED BY COURT-MARTIAL
Core Content:
The Central Government may make rules consistent with this Sanhita and the Air Force Act, Army Act, Navy Act, and any other law relating to Armed Forces, as to cases in which persons subject to army, naval or air-force law shall be tried by a Court to which this Sanhita applies or by a Court-martial. When any person is brought before a Magistrate and charged with an offence for which he is liable to be tried either by a Court under BNSS or by a Court-martial, the Magistrate shall have regard to such rules, and shall in proper cases deliver him to the commanding officer for trial by Court-martial. Every Magistrate shall, on receiving a written application from the commanding officer, use his utmost endeavours to apprehend and secure any person accused. A High Court may direct that a prisoner detained in any jail be brought before a Court-martial for trial.

SECTION 522 - FORMS
Core Content:
Subject to the power conferred by Article 227 of the Constitution, the forms set forth in the Second Schedule, with such variations as the circumstances of each case require, may be used for the respective purposes therein mentioned, and if used shall be sufficient.

SECTION 523 - POWER OF HIGH COURT TO MAKE RULES
Core Content:
Every High Court may, with the previous approval of the State Government, make rules as to the persons who may be permitted to act as petition-writers in Criminal Courts subordinate to it, regulating the issue of licences to such persons, the conduct of business by them, and the scale of fees to be charged by them, providing a penalty for contravention, and any other matter which may be provided by rules made by the State Government. All rules shall be published in the Official Gazette.

SECTION 524 - POWER TO ALTER FUNCTIONS ALLOCATED TO EXECUTIVE MAGISTRATE IN CERTAIN CASES
Core Content:
If the Legislative Assembly of a State by a resolution so permits, the State Government may, after consultation with the High Court, by notification, direct that references in sections 127, 128, 129, 164 and 166 to an Executive Magistrate shall be construed as references to a Judicial Magistrate of the first class.

SECTION 525 - CASES IN WHICH JUDGE OR MAGISTRATE IS PERSONALLY INTERESTED
Core Content:
No Judge or Magistrate shall, except with the permission of the Court to which an appeal lies from his Court, try or commit for trial any case to or in which he is a party, or personally interested, and no Judge or Magistrate shall hear an appeal from any judgment or order passed or made by himself. A Judge or Magistrate shall not be deemed to be a party to, or personally interested in, any case by reason only that he is concerned therein in a public capacity, or by reason only that he has viewed the place in which an offence is alleged to have been committed and made an inquiry in connection with the case.

SECTION 526 - PRACTISING ADVOCATE NOT TO SIT AS MAGISTRATE IN CERTAIN COURTS
Core Content:
No advocate who practices in the Court of any Magistrate shall sit as a Magistrate in that Court or in any Court within the local jurisdiction of that Court.

SECTION 527 - PUBLIC SERVANT CONCERNED IN SALE NOT TO PURCHASE OR BID FOR PROPERTY
Core Content:
A public servant having any duty to perform in connection with the sale of any property under this Sanhita shall not purchase or bid for the property.

SECTION 528 - SAVING OF INHERENT POWERS OF HIGH COURT
Core Content:
Nothing in this Sanhita shall be deemed to limit or affect the inherent powers of the High Court to make such orders as may be necessary to give effect to any order under this Sanhita, or to prevent abuse of the process of any Court or otherwise to secure the ends of justice.

SECTION 529 - DUTY OF HIGH COURT TO EXERCISE CONTINUOUS SUPERINTENDENCE OVER COURTS
Core Content:
Every High Court shall so exercise its superintendence over the Courts of Session and Courts of Judicial Magistrates subordinate to it as to ensure that there is an expeditious and proper disposal of cases by the Judges and Magistrates.

SECTION 530 - TRIAL AND PROCEEDINGS TO BE HELD IN ELECTRONIC MODE
Core Content:
All trials, inquiries and proceedings under this Sanhita, including (i) issuance, service and execution of summons and warrant; (ii) examination of complainant and witnesses; (iii) recording of evidence in inquiries and trials; and (iv) all appellate proceedings or any other proceeding, may be held in electronic mode, by use of electronic communication or use of audio-video electronic means.

Procedure:

Trials, inquiries, proceedings may be held in electronic mode

Includes issuance, service, execution of summons and warrant

Includes examination of complainant and witnesses

Includes recording of evidence

Includes appellate proceedings

SECTION 531 - REPEAL AND SAVINGS
Core Content:
The Code of Criminal Procedure, 1973 is hereby repealed. Notwithstanding such repeal, if immediately before commencement of BNSS there is any appeal, application, trial, inquiry or investigation pending, it shall be disposed of, continued, held or made in accordance with CrPC, 1973 as if BNSS had not come into force. All notifications, proclamations, powers conferred, forms provided, rules, local jurisdictions, sentences passed, orders, rules and appointments (not being Special Magistrates) made under CrPC and in force immediately before commencement shall be deemed to have been made under corresponding provisions of BNSS. Any sanction or consent given under CrPC in pursuance of which no proceeding was commenced shall be deemed to have been given under corresponding provisions of BNSS. Where the period specified for an application under CrPC had expired on or before commencement, nothing in BNSS shall enable any such application to be made by reason only that a longer period is specified by BNSS.

Effect:

CrPC 1973 repealed

Pending cases continue under CrPC

Existing notifications, rules, appointments continue under BNSS

Sanctions/consents continue under BNSS

Expired limitation periods not revived
